O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	You, dear children, I have completed this book which is the end of the science of medicine, its fulfillment, and have concluded it with explanations and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I completed this with a treatise, which is the part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And since the work of hands is closely guarded in our region and unknown throughout, the science has degenerated and become depleted, and there remains no trace of its power other than small descriptions in ancient books about what the hands have done.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this comes error and vanity, and intentions are closed, and knowledge is estranged.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	I believe I want to revive it by following the order of this treatise, according to its method of exposition and explanation and its abbreviations;
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	and I will bring together the forms of cautery instruments and other tools for this work with the addition of explanations and preparations as needed.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason that no good masters of hands are to be found in our time, the art of medicine has become neglected.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And he who wishes to excel in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, must know the judgment of the members, their forms and connections and separations, and have knowledge of bones and nerves and veins and the number of their openings, and understand the movement and rest of veins, and from where they originate.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	And Hippocrates says that the name without work is meaningless, and with work, it is powerful;
et meismement en l’art de main.	and particularly in the art of the hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	We tell you at the beginning of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the things mentioned above, will surely fall into error and harm others.
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	for I have often seen many of those who engage in this science and abandon themselves without knowledge or experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	Because I have seen a foolish thing that affects the abscess of scrofula or the neck of a woman, and affects the arteries of the neck.
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	for this causes so much blood that the woman dies in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	And see another miracle where a stone is removed from a man's chest, and the stone was large.
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	it also removes a piece of the bladder, and he bled from his wound for three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to treat him, and I saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone; I knew well that if it was not cut out, he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	And see another miracle where he treated the duke of our land who had a broken leg and a wound from the fracture.
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	and the ignorant doctor tightened the fracture over the wound with strong force and left no space for the wound to heal, and he left it in that state until the end.
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	and instruct him not to dislocate it again.
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	and wait until the leg is completely swollen and bruised and comes to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	I am called to come to him, and I hastened to go free the leg;
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	and when I freed it, the pain disappeared entirely.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	But any attempt at corruption was already confirmed within the limb, and it could not be healed.
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	and it does not cease the corruption of sending through the member as long as the member is completely dead.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I also saw another wonder: the abscess became worse, and then it was inflamed due to the malignancy of its lordship.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For the ulcer, when it is pure of melancholic humor, it does not suit that one should touch it with iron if it is not in a part that can be entirely removed what is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	And for this reason, dear child, it is necessary for you to know that the art of healing is divided into two parts:
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	that is to say, work where there is danger in many arrangements;
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	and I will show, in each part of this book, where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	For this reason, it is important for you to guard yourself, so that the foolish eyes cannot speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	If you take up your weapons in courage, and confront your enemies lightly but firmly, and use the best method, by the grace of God, you will achieve salvation and be happy.
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	and abandon the gloomy diseases of sorrow, healthily.
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	and remove your weapons of doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can pass from this world to the other in glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	Galen does not mention any of his warnings:
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Do not take any dangerous illness too seriously, unless you are called a fool for it.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise into three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	The first chapters deal with fire cautery and medicinal agues, and the chapters are ordered from the head down to the feet.
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	and the shapes of instruments, and the tools for cautery, and everything necessary for the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	The second sentence translates to: The following chapters are about cutting and piercing, and the use of suction cups and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar procedures.
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	and it describes the chapters arranged and the shapes of the instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar conditions.
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	and it is ordered from the greatest pain down to the least, and describes the shapes of the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	So, remembering the work, it is necessary that I describe the quality of aid and the harm or benefit of each condition.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	I say that the qualities of aid, and its harmful effects, are the longest to explain and the most subtle sciences, containing secret answers.
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	and about this, many of the wise ones spoke, and agreed upon it.
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	and I will be content with few of my words, for I dread the lengthiness.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	I say that cautery helps universally for every complexion where it has matter, regardless of the complexities.
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	This is to know: a hot complexion with regard to matter, and a dry complexion without regard to matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	In a hot and dry complexion, they combined matter, devised something, and said that cautery is great help.
et li autre dirent le contraire:	and the other ones said the opposite:
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	that cautery is not worth for illness that comes from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	For the nature of fire is hot, and it should not be treated for hot illness with heat or dryness;
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	and he who does the opposite of cauterization provides great aid for hot, dry disease that comes upon the body of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of man and its moisture to the heat of fire, you feel the body is warm.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	Because I have found it to be true through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	And in every case, no one should intervene unless they have tried it themselves, and who knows by long experience the chapter of cauterization, and the diversity of complexions of men, and their dispositions and causes of illness, and the outcomes and the passage of time.
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	we have only fear from other complexions, especially for cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all agreed and came together for the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know this, son, that cautery combines fire in a way that is a secret of healing, and indeed it is a greater kindness than the fiery medicine cautery.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and it does not come from outside except to the member that is hot, and it does not harm any other member.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	Burning medicines come from one part to another by removing, and bring to the limb diseases of great healing.
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	and perhaps the patient suffers.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	He does not hesitate because of his nobility and the goodness of his nature, unless there is excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	And this is what I have found by experience and through the length of my service and study in the art, and it was about the truth of things.
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	and therefore I excuse the length of my speech, for I do not like to deprive you of the secret that is hidden in fire, and the quality of the work, how it drives diseases from the body, as the philosopher demonstrates.
or le recevez en vos pensees.	or consider it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know this, my son, that there is agreement among them as to when cauterization should be performed and the prayers recited.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	And I say that cauterization is appropriate at all times, because the harmful pain is removed with the help of gentle cauterization.
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	and especially when cauterization is for necessary and urgent pain, so that no greater evil comes to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	And never think, dear child, as they do wrongfully;
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	for the illness that is healed by cautery does not relapse;
et il le dient ensi;	and thus it should be done;
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	but it is not always as they should care for it, because cautery is only a medicine that changes the complexion and dries up the humors that cause pain; it is a powerful remedy for quick healing, and its virtue lies in its effect and mastery.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	And it is possible for the illness to come according to the constitution of the patient and the nature of the disease and its virtue.
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	and they are assembled within him as excesses through the acquisition of meats and similar things, unless cautery is administered to him where there is little excess and moisture, just as cautery for stones due to pain and similar conditions, and this pain does not return.
mais ce avient poc.	but this rarely happens.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	And many people do not understand at all why cautery is called the last resort of medicine, and it is indeed true.
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	but they do not believe that cautery is worth anything after medicine; their intentions are false, and cautery is the last resort of medicine because when we administer remedies in any disease and they do not work, then let us use cautery, and it is effective.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then it becomes clear that cautery is indeed the last resort of medicine, not at all according to the understanding of learned fools.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	The ancients said that gold cautery instruments are more effective than iron ones, and they only spoke of fire for the quality of gold and for the high value of its substance.
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	and they said that the gold in cautery instruments does not rust, but this is not true because I have tried it, and I have found that it does indeed rust in no men.
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	and fire cautery is more valuable than metal, as they say.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	But even when you heat gold instruments, you are not sure if they are hot enough by the color of the gold, and they may cool down before you know it.
et s’on le chaufe trop;	and if it is heated too much;
si font au feu;	it turns black from the fire.
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	and thus it is enough hindrance.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason, we use fire cautery as we have equipped it with our tools for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Now we have ordered this chapter from the beginning to the end, so that the way may be lighter to follow.
dou cautere olivaire	olive cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	Fire cautery is useful for moisture and cold on the head, and it helps with conditions caused by a disease called "soda," and by many humors that flow from the head to the ears, and due to numerous dreams and toothaches and throat pain, and especially with all diseases caused by cold such as paralysis and soda and apoplexy and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	The form of this cautery is such that the patient is purged by a solvent medicine cleansing the third or fourth harmful substance, according to the virtue and age and habituation of the patient's illness.
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	and then make the patient's head clean.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	and then make the patient lie down with their head between your hands, and place their hands on some weight.
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	after, place the root of your palm on the root of their nose between their two eyes;
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	and when your two hands come together, if blood drips from the wound, heat the cautery called "olive" with which this form is made:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	and place the sign of ink on the joint, and then slowly and gently lower and pull your hand, disrupting it.
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	then gently release your hand, and stabilize the joint when you see the bone begin to move slightly.
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	and if you do not see it, repeat the cautery until you can see the bone, as I told you.
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	After taking a little silk thread, wrap it around and make it soft cotton, and place it on the dislocation, and leave it for three days.
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	After that, place the moistened cotton on it.
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	and leave it until the inflammation subsides.
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that, dress the wound with "tetrafarmace" until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	And they said to each other, as long as the wound remains open, more pus is discharged.
et por ce si aide mues.	and for this reason, aid is sought.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they say that one must not leave the cautery for so long that the bone itself is burned; then remove the burned part from the bone, and it will be healed.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	And he tells the other that one must let the cautery remain in place for as long as it takes, and push so hard that they make a gap in the bone just as wide as the turn of a woman's wrist to allow the humors to escape.
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	and the wound must remain open for a long time.
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	After the wound, one must cure and dress it.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	And these two methods of cautery do not seem to be good in all cases, except for those who have no other choice.
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	and it seems to me that I should leave this.
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	because the tissues are weakened by continuous washing with liquid of a certain nature, as we testify in other members.
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	and also when the joint of the patient is weak by nature, and the initial appearance of cautery is safer and more mobile for me, from this I proceed to perform with safety.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	the ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	When chronic pain persists for a prolonged period, the patient should use herbs and pills known as "coughing" remedies, as well as enemas and applications of oil and plasters.
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	and if one performs the cautery as we have previously mentioned, it will not be effective.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	Take care if the patient's shoulder is of a strong nature and not too frozen.
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	then cauterize deeply, as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	After that, cauterize each corner of the shoulder bone, as we have said before, and also cauterize the part called "vasselz".
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	and hold the eyes, which are used for applying suction.
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	and take your hand so that you do not see anything just to the bone:
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	the patients suffer much greater pain from this cautery than from others, and I will speak of that later;
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	and it is necessary that the cauterization of the horns be more subtle than that of the middle part of the head, and this is its form:
dou cautere dou chief	For fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	When there is sudden severe pain in a part of the head, and the disease spreads to the oil, and the symptoms are purged with purgative medicines, and other treatments have been tried as described in the classification of diseases, and none of these help:
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	Then he performs cauterization according to two manners, that is to say, with hot medicines and by fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	If he cauterizes with hot medicines, it is when you press a sore on the skin and remove the crust and flesh in small pieces, then makes an incision where the pain resides in such a way that you can push back the sore from under the skin.
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	and when it is pushed back, if he holds the limb still and tightens it well, and leaves it thus for twelve hours.
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	and then dislodge and treat it further with garlic, and leave the wound thus for two or three days.
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	then place cotton soaked in butter over it until the pus ceases.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	After the dressing, as long as it is healthy;
et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	and if you see that it is not suitable for any of the burning remedies I have written about or the dosage for treating them,
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The fire cautery is done according to this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the fire cautery with this tool:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	And it is called "closed" because the head is shaped like a shell or hat with a slight curvature, and it has a small appearance.
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	and place it on the painful joint, hold your hand and gently twist it a little, until half of the intensity of the pain is gone.
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	and relax your hand so that the artery does not feel pain, which is numb, and allows blood to flow abundantly.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors;	After applying cotton in the form of thread, place it on the joint for three days.
puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	then I apply moist cotton soaked in butter, and then cure the wound with a bandage until it is healed;
et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	and if you want to cauterize this migraine with the cautery called "cultellare" (a kind of instrument), be sure to not block the artery in this migraine which is not very old.
de emigraine	of migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans;	When you treat a migraine as we have previously explained in the divisions of illnesses, and it does not benefit, and you see that the cautery mentioned in medicine is not enough, then you must heat the cautery called "cultellare" until it becomes white.
et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os;	and thus he should mark the affected area with a line half as long as a finger, and once his hand is steady, pull it away so as not to injure the artery or reach down to the bone.
et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;	and guard the jaw that moves when chewing, so that the nerves pay no heed to the movement or spasm does not come upon the patient, and beware of the blood flow from the artery when it is cut, for cutting it causes great fear, especially to those who do not know or are untrained and inexperienced.
et laisse l’uevre em mi voie;	and leave the wound half-healed;
mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	but I will tell you how to retain blood when an artery is cut, and I will show you where it hardens in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And if you see that this cautery is not enough to heal the disease, and the patient suffers, cauterize the opposite side as well as we have said, and treat the wound until it is clean.
et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz;	and if you see, apply the cautery that we have said in this chapter for the extraction of an artery, with the cautery having two blades.
et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	and this fire cautery is one of the best remedies for him and most helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	about the pain of the ears due to cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When there is pain in the ear due to cold, and various solutions and treatments as we have mentioned in the previous section have been applied, but the pain persists, use this cautery called "point," which has the following shape:

et ait X poins entor chescune oreille;	and make X marks around each ear;

de la torture de la bouche	regarding the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie;	The torture that must be cured by cautery is limited to those affecting fluid movement, as we have explained in the sections on illness.
et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	and do not perform cautery on conditions that arise from dryness and nerve pain.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres:	When you cure this condition of fluid movement from dryness and purging from the head and gargling, it is not effective. Therefore, you must cauterize the patient with three cauteries.
l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres;	one at the root of the ear, another slightly above the temple, and the third in the adjustment of the two lips.
et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce;	and place the cautery on the part that opens to the healthy space, and make it cauterize at the top of the ear, a little below the curve at the top, and another one in the temple just as far;
et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse;	and leave the cautery on until half of the heart is burned;
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the shape of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros;	and it resembles the scalpel we have described before, but it is a little more subtle, and it is necessary that the knife be slightly thicker.
aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After treatment, reset it as I have said before, as long as it is healthy.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres:	When apoplexy is old and you cure it as we have said, but the patient does not benefit, and has no fever, then make four cauterizations.
II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac;	On the two horns of the head, take the head itself, and emit (or release) the limb called "vessel" as we have said before, and do no cauterization on the mouth of the stomach.
et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	and so it is cured as we have said above.
de litargie	The term "de litargie" seems to be a

de la froidor dou chief	from cold at the top

de l’epilempsie	From epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics should not use fire cautery except for those who are phlegmatic, and it is first necessary to purify the brain with years and other remedies that we have discussed in the section on great suffering from long-term medication.

et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir;	and heat it gently over fire so that the patient can bear it;
aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier;	after evacuating the circle inside the joint, and leaving it to cool down;

et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	and then place a moist cloth soaked in butter and gelatine on it.
de l’awe des eulz	of the eyes

When the eyes come first through the signs I mentioned in the previous section, then begin and give to the patient something to drink, a purifying medicine for the head, and guard against all moisture, and make him sweat or take a bath while fasting.

dou cors des larmes	two parts of the eye

de coi ci est li forme:	Due to which the form is:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont;	And if you see that making cauteries on the joints makes them as long as the bones,
et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and do not let go of the instrument until the third part of the paper is burned, according to the manner I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	the hairs that prevent the oil from entering
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres:	Never does it happen that the hairs of the skin are turned to a different color, and they prick the patient, and cauterization is performed in two ways.
c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	that is to say, with fire, or with burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals;	The fire cautery instructs the patient to let the hairs grow long and even.
et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.

aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz;	after signing on the paper with a symbol as powerful as the flame, and it is like the beginning of the sign among the hairs;
puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	then put moist cotton soaked in egg white and musk from the pistachio on the oil, then heat the cautery with which this shape is formed:

et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil;	and the signs of the success of the treatment are that you see the skin retreating, and the hairs standing on end at the tip of the oil.

aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the treatment of healing as long as it is clean.

et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz;	and apply it gently if it does not cool down, then spread over the shape you have made as if from a mold, and place some paper on top of it.
et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi;	and if the disease persists only in one place, then surgery should be performed there, and also both places.

Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, then remove the medicine from your body.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision;	And once the stinging has passed, if the limb is raised above the heart, and you see the paper lifting as if it were lifted by constriction of fire or by incision.
et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	and if it is so, then it is good.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point;	If no, then apply more medicine to the limb or the medicine has not opened up completely, as long as your work is even and your joints are well-set.

Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you have to take care of yourself, be very careful with your work so that it does not seek out the medicine by itself.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant;	And if the paper becomes soft after and the hairs prick in the oil, repeat the treatment on that joint which has been softened with the paper, just as you did before.
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	after the treatment, until it is healed;
et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	and this is the form of the wound with much pain;
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens;	And know that the bones of men are diverse in size, both large and small, according to your constraints.
et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	and do not deviate from the right path for he who has the study of this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Of the treatment of a fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have discussed regarding diseases, and your treatments do not benefit the patient, then it is necessary to perform cautery on them in this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	Instruct the patient to place his head on your healthy side.
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	and place the patient's head between your hands in such a manner that it does not move, and do not let go of his head.
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;	after moistening a cloth with vinegar or juice of parsley on oil;
aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:	after heating the cautery instrument that is suitable:
et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;	and it should be shaped like the head of a quill, assembling the edge to be the cautery.
se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente;	if you see that it is pointed from one end to the other, and if you see that it is also like a tent;
mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	But nevertheless, this that is dry deserves to be moved for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche;	After pressing the fistula, it should be opened, and then drain the pus, and dry it.
et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe;	and if it closes again after opening, pull strongly on the bow.
aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie;	after applying hot cautery, place your hand on the heated part with the oil, ensuring your hand does not move erratically.
et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	and apply the cautery to the fat of the oil, and the corruption.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you begin the cautery near the bone, that would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors;	If this does not work, apply the cautery again, and if you need to, do it a third time, and leave it for three days.
aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers;	after applying a moist cloth dipped in butter, and treating the dry dressing until it is healed, and if forty days pass without healing, then apply an ague-corrosive medicine while the bone is exposed.
et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	and the treatment according to what comes in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a kind of cautery for a fistula that no one of the ancients spoke of.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu;	Grasp the fistula firmly, and fix the place;
aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	after that, place a subtle pressure on it so that this is the shape:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc;	and it forms the quantity of a drop.
et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil;	and hold your hand firm, so that the patient does not move, and let the drop fall into its place.
et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe:	and it is necessary to place on the patient a moist cotton ball in order to help them rest.
li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	He plunges deeply into the wound from which the abscess flows, and the health returns through the marvelous strength of medicine.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the ulcer is clean through the cautery we have mentioned, that is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If this is not the case, then it is necessary to administer ice or cold water, and return the ulcer to the body within the cold, according to what is appropriate for its place.
des crevaices en levres	cracks in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times cracks appear in the lips, which are called "poil," especially on the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these wounds as we have discussed in detail, and the treatment does not benefit, then use a small cauterizing instrument according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font;	and places the medicine in those wounds until it reaches the root.
aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	after healing, reset the joint until it is whole.
de l’aposteme de la goule	from the abscess of the mouth
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule;	When an abscess forms at the root of the tongue or jaw, or in the uvula, or in the palate, or at the roots of teeth, after putrefaction and rot, it becomes inflamed and turns into a fistula.
et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie:	and you treat it as we have said before, but it does not improve.
adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule;	then it is necessary that you apply cautery according to the quantity of the fistula;
aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu;	after the opening or perforation of the fistula, hold your hand until the heat reaches the bottom and there is no more bleeding.
et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do so once or twice after the treatment that we have mentioned in treatments, as long as it is healed;
et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin;	and if it is treated thus, it is good;
et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	and if that does not help, you must then discover the place and remove the corrupt bone, according to what you find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	no movement of the joints
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain;	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and treatment with medicine is ineffective, then place the sick person's head in a healthy place.
aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent;	after applying the heat for the cautery, watch for the formation of blisters, in this way that you place a bandage over the tooth.
et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent;	and place the hot cautery over the patient's wound, holding your hand so that the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth.
aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit;	after releasing your hand, and recommencing the cautery according to your will;
aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	after filling the patient's mouth with salt water, leave it for an hour and rinse with hot water.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this same manner, the tooth that was moving becomes confirmed, the gums are softened and restrained, and the moisture is dried up.
de la dolor des dens	about the pain of teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	When tooth pain comes from cold, or there is frost or chill, and the remedies of medicine are ineffective, then it needs cautery according to these two ways:
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	and with butter cautery and fire cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	The butter cautery is such that you press the butter into a hot steel or copper spoon.
aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez;	after taking cotton and wrapping it around the tip of a stick, soak it in melted butter, and apply it gently to the painful tooth until it cools.
et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	and thus do this often until the virtue of the butter reaches the root of the tooth; and if you see that the moist cloth and cotton are too hard to work with, apply the hot iron to the painful tooth until the heat eases the toothache.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	He should perform the fire cautery by applying it so that he pricks with an iron or bronze needle, making it thick enough for the flame not to reach the patient's mouth.
aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez;	After heating the cautery, from which the shape will form, place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery cools down.
fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	Do this often, as the pain will be just as intense on the following day or even more so.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer;	And it is important that the patient fills his mouth with good butter in the rush of that cautery and then sucks on a hot brick.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir;	and perform cautery on the part of the body that you wish, according to your ability;
et c’est li forme de la caine:	and this is the form of the cautery instrument:
des scrophules	Of scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie;	When the scrofula (a type of swelling) is filled with cold moisture and unresponsive to medication, then apply heat to the cautery instrument afterwards, creating an opening for the steam to escape from the cautery onto the other part.
et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume;	and then apply hot cautery to the abscess once, as is necessary, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess.
et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors;	and if the abscess is small due to applying cautery according to its quantity, leave it thus for three days.
et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee;	and apply a moist cloth with butter until the burn is healed.
aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	after healing, remove the bandages and tents as soon as it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The shape of the cane:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives;	When moisture conquers the channels of the body, especially when it arises from a cold complexion, then it is necessary that the patient be first relieved by solvent medications.
aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	After the fire cautery at the root of the throat, be careful not to go near the throat, and do not drink anything hot but a little.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant;	After that, perform another cautery at the joint of the collarbone and spine, and be it the cauterization known as 'clavicle' from which we have the form before.
et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	and heal the joint as we have said before, as long as it is healthy.
de la toust	from the heat
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai .II cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis;	When all and every illness of the promon (possibly referring to the pronate or palm of the hand) is due to cold moisture, and the patient has no fever or stiffness, and it is an old illness, then make .II cauteries (two types of treatments) on their will;
et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles;	and another cautery, cut between the two mammals (possibly referring to the breast or chest area);
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	and this cautery, which is called "clavile" according to the shape as said before.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles;	And if you see, perform cautery by pricking all the cautery points called "points" from which the form of the ear disease is as it is before;
et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	and the points should be up to 30, or as deep as necessary.

Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And because the cautery is lighter, because you do it three times in turn.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	On the dislocation of the shoulder.
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit;	Afterwards, remember the patients on their backs and sides;
aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre;	after that, open the passageway inside the swelling with your left hand;

et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres;	and cauterize the wound gently until it feels firm to the touch, and let the shape of the cautery guide you in making four cauterizations.
et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres;	and for this reason, the cautery is made with a tool having three prongs, so that the shape of the cauterization consists of six cauterizations.
et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and the nerves vary according to the sensitivity of each person, and this is the shape of the cautery with three prongs:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And never should it be adjusted on this nerve, for there are eight burns.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil;	After placing the fire cautery, apply crushed herbs with a cloth;
aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After resting the patient, do not move the limbs for a long time until they are completely healed.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated from above, such a thing happens poorly, then make a fire cautery on the thick skin with a cautery claw or many cauteries with sharp points.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and moisture is removed, and health returns to the patient.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When coldness and much moisture come to the stomach while it is being stretched from its natural state, catarrh multiplies within it, and conventional treatment methods do not help, then the patient should be careful on his back, extending his legs and arms.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture;	Then, make three cauterizations removing the skin with a knife, each about as thick as a finger, claving the cautery entirely through, and two more cauterizations on either side so that the appearance of the cauteries forms three angles, with enough space between them so they are not joined together when they become gangrenous.
et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	and instruct them to perform the cautery so that they mark both parts of the heart, and let the shape of the cauter be according to this form without adjustment:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme;	and if you undergo cauterization with a great cautery on the stomach according to this form;
et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche;	and whoever has fear of this cautery, perform the cauterization by pricking and signing on the stomach in a dot according to the quantity that you see fit;
puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	then cauterize it completely at the cautery called "dot".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment we have previously discussed, as long as it is healthy.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez;	As for the liver, it experiences pain from fresh and moist heat, and a great accumulation of phlegm, as long as it is severely deprived of its natural condition due to excesses.
et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil;	and the patient is treated with what we have mentioned in parts, but it does not help, and it is necessary that the patient be mindful of their head.
et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient;	and the sign of three cauterizations according to this form and this figure and this quantity on the liver, removing the hypochondria, where the pains of the human body originate.
et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi;	and say there should be enough space between each cautery, the thickness of a finger.
et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere;	and the cautery should be long throughout the body, and do not press too much with your hand on any part of the cautery.
et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez;	and burn only the middle part of the heart, and the patient should be upright on their feet.
et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais;	and if he cannot, lying down, extend his legs, and ease his breathing.
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors;	And if you wish to cauterize these wounds with a knife, being skilled and wise in the art, be careful not to burn all the heart, for you would cause severe damage throughout the body.
et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	and that it does not come to a boil, for the heart is very delicate at this place, and the wise ones know it.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile:	When there is an abscess in the liver, and you need to know if it is within the flesh of the liver or in the membrane:
s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort;	If he is on the bed, he feels the patient pain not too severe.
et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	and if he is in the bandage, he feels severe pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste;	And when this treatment requires the patient to look around, it is necessary that the patient keeps their head still.
et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	and then seal the wound where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which is similar to a ring, from which comes this form:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers;	And cauterize with fire until the colors are burned, and come just to the point of syphilis, while the putrefaction is entirely gone.
aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez;	after the treatment, according to the treatment of effusions until it is healed;
et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	and it is not advisable to use this cauterization unless by one who has studied deeply the art of medicine and whose hands have never failed in treating these illnesses.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then he can safely operate, but I still think it is better to leave it.
dou cautere de pleuresin	Fire cautery
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere:	The ancients said that one should make cauterizations with tears from roots of aristologe, and in this manner:
pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois;	Take a long root of aristologe (a type of plant), the largest you can find, and ensure it is dry, as well as equally thick and long as your arm.
et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe;	and moisten it in oil, and hold it over the fire, and cauterize (the area) between the shoulder blade and the collarbone, and make smaller cauterizations slightly descending in the part that is under the beard.
et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc;	and also cauterize between the fifth rib and the sixth, slightly declining behind.
et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules;	and I use cautery on the worst part, and another on the stomach, and between the shoulders, and along both sides of the pain, remove the cautery that is between the shoulders.
et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	and do not press my hand, but open it firmly as if smelling something.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme;	And they say that no ancient person should use the fire cautery like a razor, burning it and placing it between the ribs, as it reaches this abscess.
et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	and suddenly the pain arises, as we have said about the abscess of the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this case, there is great fear among the patients, and many die now, or a fistula appears that cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the mouse as we have said about the divisions of treatments, and it does not benefit, then they attach three ways of cautery that are good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant;	Dislocate it in such a way that you make three cauterizations, or four, along the length of the mouse, according to the shape of the cautery of the fire that we have mentioned above.
