et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	and the most skilled surgeons cleverly create their own instruments, according to what their works and the illness show them, for there are many diseases where the ancients did not teach any instruments due to their diversity; and if they break a bone or a fragment, or it splinters, and they seek the instruments that they need, as I have told you, and are aided by gestures, this is how the form is:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;	and they should be large and well-holding for holding the bone, that it does not escape, but can hold and remove;
et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	and then restore the proper use of medicine suitable to it, and if there is putrefaction in the bone, even if it is small, remove it with all these instruments.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer:	When the tooth does not appear according to the natural course of growth, and its shape is ugly, especially in young women, it is necessary that you know if the tooth has grown after the other teeth, and is not in the proper place, and cannot be filed or polished.
adonques lou raie;	then the extraction.
et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	and if it is stuck with a tooth, takes this instrument whose form is as follows, resembling a small beak, and made of sharp iron in all parts.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the dentist should work slowly and carefully with his hands for the pain of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it is apparent that it can be filed, then file it from one side as the shape allows.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles;	and it is also like the lime used to make needles;
et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece;	and with the lime, gently tap the tooth with your finger several times, so that it does not move until it is ready to come out.
puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	then in the end, it has no rasping edge, and its density cuts too deeply and damages the tongue; so you must smooth out the roughness until it is even, so that it does not damage or impair speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth aches
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;	When the tooth aches, either by striking or pulling, and the patient cannot bite down without pain, he can be cured with restrictive medications, but that is of no use.
si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;	if they need to restrain it with a golden thread, for the silver thread turns green and rots, but gold never changes.
et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens;	and the thread should be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the amount of space between the teeth.
et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part;	and if you need to align the teeth, take the thread and wrap it around the two healthy teeth twice, then place the pieces between the loose teeth, as many as there are, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side firmly.
puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point;	then begin to cover again just up to the part where you apply pressure, and gently yet firmly hold your hand in place until it does not move.
et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	and make sure your finger is at the root of the tooth so it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue;	Then cut the pieces of thread with pliers, assemble them, and insert them between the healthy tooth and the one with the cavity so it does not damage the tongue.
et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil;	and then leave it as tight as it can be for as long as possible, and if it loosens, the threads will break, unless held by another thread.
si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	if it could stay put and serve thus all its time, and this is the shape of the teeth and the figure of the correct placement of the two healthy teeth, and the two jaws, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit;	And when the tooth is dislodged, it should be carefully reset in its place, fresh by fresh, as we have said.
et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	and do not attempt this unless you are skilled and patient; never form it like a bone tooth, but place it in the missing spot, holding it as we have said, and letting it stay thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	from cutting the tongue's ligament
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi;	No such bonds come from beneath the tongue or nature, but thus we are born.
ou par accident de plaie soudee;	or due to an accidental deep wound;
et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	and the work is such that you open the mouth of the patient with pain, and hold his head in your hands, and gently extract the tongue;
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	then cut the large nerve tie, as long as the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if there is stiffness or other, and it is a sudden wound, if it pulls the hook and cuts widely that tie.
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	and ensure that the cut is not too deep, for the artery below.
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	once you have done that, raise the limb with hot water and ash, or cold water, then apply a compress of linen below the tongue.
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	and every night, apply this mixture to the patient, so that the limb cannot heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	and if a fever develops, apply a compress of crushed vitriol to the limb.
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	and if it does not heal, if cauterized with a slow-acting cautery, which is good.
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	then apply another treatment as long as it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	and if you see it is red or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is cancer.
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	and if it turns pale and there is moisture, cut the tumor with a sharp instrument, and free it from both sides.
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	and if it does not leave your work, dip it in vinegar until it is stained, then return to your task while you treat everything thoroughly.
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then lift the limb from rest and silence, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	from the abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	Sometimes a condition enters the throat called "godath", which is properly known as the "two mandrels", and when you treat them, as we have said in the previous discussion, if they remain unhealthy, be careful.
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	If it is an abscess of small size and dark color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron, also for the discharge of pus.
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	but leave it until it is dry, and then you will remove it, or it would break on its own.
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	and if it is of white color with thin roots, then have the instrument ready to cover it, but first ensure that the abscess is calm and at ease.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	Then make the patient wait before the sun, and his feet should be in good condition, and open the mouth, and press the tongue down with the instrument between his hands, pressing it against the whole tool, from which this form is derived.
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	and be of silver or subtle gold as well as our knives:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	You cannot press the tongue against all of this tool, and you see the abscess, so take the awl and the file, and insert them into the flesh, pulling upwards more than you can.
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	and do not attempt to extract anything from the wounds with it, then cut with the instrument, which forms a shape that resembles strength.
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	but nevertheless the instrument bends this way and that, and it is very sharp, made of iron or steel.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument at hand, if it is like pincers, thus is its form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	and it has incisions on one side and no incisions on the other.
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and when you have cut one of the tendons, cut the other in the same way, and after the incision, rinse the patient's wound with hot water and cold, clear water, and it is necessary to gargle the patient with these waters or with extracts from pomegranates cooked with cinnamon or mulberry leaves and similar things, until the blood stops.
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then apply the cure as long as he is healthy;
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	and never does any other abscess form in the throat than the two mandibles, so cut them as you would the two mandibles.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was formed inside her throat, namely a small abscess.
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	and had a lot of pus closed in the throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the blocked passage, and could not eat or drink, and would have died if left that way for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so swollen that it had pushed two ribs through the two openings in the throat where it entered.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	I have often hastened to do so, and inserted a point into one place, then drove it through, and pulled out a great portion of bowel.
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	then I did the same thing on the other side of the opening, and opened the mouth and pressed the tongue.
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	after inserting the point into these abscesses, and taking out a portion, I did not pull out much blood.
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	and thus the throat of the woman was opened, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I did not stop cutting this abscess for a long time.
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	and it makes the abscess heal again, and fills the cavity that I had emptied, as long as it was very large.
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	then I designed and cauterized it inside the throat:
ensi demora sens croistre;	so it delays feeling better;
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	and I left these parts behind, and only God becomes of them after me.
de l’uve	from the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	When the eye returns to its socket, and it is swollen and distant, it is called "perpendicular".
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	and if it is detached, thick, and round, it is called "uve".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	When it is treated as we have described in the previous section, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the abscess is calm, and it is subtle, then it is necessary to drain it.
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	and that is round and not long.
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	and it is red or of a dark color, then it is necessary to be careful with the incision.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the sick person.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	It is necessary, when you see this, according to the manner I have said, of cleansing and lengthening, that you make the patient sit before the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument of which we spoke earlier.
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	then insert the hook into the eye and remove it from the inside, and cut with the second instrument that I spoke of for incising the two mandras.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	and it is necessary that you do not cut off more than the excess beyond the natural limit.
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	because if you do not take care, it will cause distress to the voice and speech;
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and after the incision, use the same method we described for incising the two glands, and dress it as long as it is clean.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient suffers from great pain, it is necessary that you use an instrument for cauterization to alleviate the sensitive pain.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	The method of cauterization must be sharp and quick.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	And it is that the patient places his head on a healthy surface, and then presses the tongue with the instrument described in the chapter on cautery (fire treatment), using a hot compress, not too thick or too thin.
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	and using the care of this instrument, which forms thus:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	And let there be a clever person with a beard, who puts on the medicine as if it were the handle of a spoon, and places the instrument over all the medicine on the eye.
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	and the patient should lie on their side, so that the saliva and mucus from their mouth flows out of the medicine into their throat, soothing it.
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	then take your hand and press the medicine onto the eye for half an hour, until you see it cease to sting and the pain from the medicine is soothed.
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, dampen the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument completely into the wound over the cotton until the cotton is saturated with blood.
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	and do this often, as long as the cauterization is perfect, then leave it to dry, and after three or four days, remove it.
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	And if you need to redo the cauterization with the medicine, when you redo it, after the cauterization, wipe around the wound with cotton soaked in butter and change anything that is around the medicine.
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	and it is raised from cold water, and it is cured with gargles as long as it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	This treatment is safer than incision, rather than cauterization.
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	if it is treated with fumigation according to this method, take plenty of salt and hyssop and oregano and rue and chamomile and similar herbs, and combine them all in a pot or some of them, and put it on the fire and boil;
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	and the pot should be well sealed with strong clay, and attached to the pot is a handle according to this method:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	And whether it is of silver or gold, and if one of the joints is squeezed into the mouth of the patient with pain, until the vapour rises to the eye through the canal, until the eye becomes numb.
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	after the recurrence often, while the eye is dry, be sure not to do this at the beginning of the formation of the abscess, as many things may occur.
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	and do not make any movements except during the decline of the hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	And if this instrument is not present, take a canal and insert a piece of cloth into the mouth of the patient, so that it is not too hot.
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	Because the heat of fire does not allow moisture to collect in the mouth, and this is a good cure that brings overall health.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	Often there is a burning sensation in the throat from bone or fish spine, or any other thing;
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	so it is necessary that you treat what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you can see the thing move.
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	and if it does not open and is withdrawn into the throat, it is necessary to make the patient vomit so that the food in the stomach is cooked.
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	perhaps if the thing turns around by vomiting;
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	or the patients swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of naval (stringy part of an apple), or a root of lettuce, or a crumb of dry bread;
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	and it swallows the sponge string, and then spits it out;
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	and when it comes back to its place, if it swells up, then pull gently;
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not come from what we have said, take a plunger tool according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	and let the tool be curved at the end if it can more easily enter the throat, and hold the head slightly raised.
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	and be careful not to touch the epiglottis, so that it does not come out, and do not push the bone inside.
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	and it is necessary that the patient pushes the tool, because he should move it or the thing is open.
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	if the bottle goes down, where it is pulled out with all tools equally, as long as it comes out completely.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	Never should medicine be applied without reason, as I said in the previous section, through the treatment of medicines;
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	and if it does not benefit, then look in the throat of the patient suffering from disease in sunlight, and press their tongue with the tool I have told you;
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the vein, draw it out with all its tiny hooks, or subtle pincers that are fit for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that does not work, take a horsehair rope and tie it around the throat of the patient, then slowly tighten or loosen the rope until the vein heats up and this is done often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient is filled with water all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	then take a full glass of cold water, open the mouth, and pour it in, moving the tongue with your hand often.
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	and if at once he feels the cold water, then quiet.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	And if it does not quiet down as we have said, then smoke the patient with the instrument I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye.
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	do this many times, for it will loosen without target.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	And the method of fumigation is that you light a pot with hot coals, and place it over an open dish in the middle, and through this opening, the instrument's thread will emerge.
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	then he applies the fumigation, and the patient puts the cane's end in his mouth, and closes it tightly, so that no smoke escapes but only reaches up to his nose.
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	and now the nose will bleed, and if it does not stop, the fumigation should be repeated several times.
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	and the patient suffers from thirst, eats salty and bitter things, but does not drink water.
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	and then he/she must be less concerned about speaking or moving under this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	And the shape of the instrument with which one treats the wound, if it is possible to see it, resembles curved pincers designed to enter the throat.
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	and it resembles the beak of a curlew, and has the roughness of lime, so that whatever it grasps, it cannot let go.
et vez ci la forme:	and here is the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	Many appearances of abscesses are, according to the memory that comes to mind after reading this book, and they vary in piercing and sizing.
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	and this is in two ways; one is in its own image, and of those that hold moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second method is for the joints where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscess of the upper part is different from that of the lower, and the abscess of the fleshy part of the shoulder is different from that which comes in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	And if an abscess is not to be pierced until the bowel is entirely dried up according to its completion.
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	and if they are such that it is necessary to pierce them when they are dried out and do not die according to their completion, as abscesses that are located in the joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come from damaged joints, and they are left as they are until the pus is drained, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint become corrupted, leading to contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	Or the abscess is located in the main limb, and if you delay piercing until it is entirely dried up, it will harm the principal limb.
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	if it is possible to remove the source, so that it does not harm any further;
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	and it is not advisable that you pierce an abscess without first completing the healing process, lest, after removing the source, it becomes infected inside and develops a fistula.
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	and will not heal completely.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	And it is important that you know the appropriate time for piercing an abscess when it is completely healed, and this is when the pain has subsided, the fever has disappeared, there is a reduction in pain and swelling, and the abscess head becomes softer and smoother.
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	and it is necessary that you make the piercing sit more dependent on the abscess, where it opens movement.
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	and the piercing should be as long as the skin, and if the abscess is in the hand or foot, or in the joints and tendons and arteries, and everywhere it is even where there is no curvature.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	When these swellings occur, according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when there are abscesses in soft flesh, it is better to let the incision heal completely before moving it, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	For if you pierce it in front of that, the skin will be stretched with the blood from it, and is filled with much filth.
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	and by chance they harden the lips and deepen the wound within him.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if an abscess is pierced according to the thickness of the flesh and the part that the member needs.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	and it is necessary that you make small incisions, small openings;
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	and in large incisions, large openings, and many fissures according to the size of the abscess;
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	and if at such abscesses it is necessary to press the heart, and cover;
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	when it has become as dry as cloth, and is numb, then it needs to be treated like blisters.
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	and if they are split in three angles, and if there are such as one copes with also like the fleece of mint, as abscesses from arrows.
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	and if there are such as one makes a round incision of various sizes and shapes.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	Those that have no head, like a soft, superficial abscess, it is necessary to pierce them deeply.
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	and it is necessary when the abscess is large and has a strong bow, and you pierce it, if you cannot draw out all the bow in that moment, but only part of it.
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	then cauterize the abscess until the next day, then draw out nothing from it.
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	do this many times, gradually, until the bow completely draws out.
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	most often the patients are of weak constitution, or pregnant women, or very young children, or old and frail nobles.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For often the patient will jump with the release of the pus, and by chance might die, and you will not notice.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	Therefore, avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have perceived your abscess, if the wound has drained, and observe whether the wound of the abscess is small.
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	and if it is a deep wound, then apply these attempts with linen or fresh cotton.
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	and if it is a large abscess with many openings, then you must insert a tent in each so that they meet.
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	and if you have removed a portion of hard skin around the abscess and it remains open, then you should fill it with old cotton or dried linen rags without moisture, and bind it for three days.
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the bone, and the treatment of healing as long as it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if the progression of blood occurs in your work, apply cold water and ice, wet the cloth, and repeatedly place it on the affected area.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	And if the blood poisoning persists, with proper governance and treatment, and the powders that I have mentioned in this book, and if it is winter, and the veins or abscesses are very sensitive, then it is necessary to place several moistened cloths soaked in wine and hot oil on them.
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	and if it is in summer, and the vein is fleshy, then it is necessary to place moistened cloths in water and cold oil, or wine and hot oil, for three days, as we have said.
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then dislodge the abscess and dry it and treat it, as appropriate, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	And it is necessary to know universally in the treatment of abscesses:
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	or as told to you, how one must proceed with the treatment of abscesses, read this chapter now.
des soros	From the sources
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Or consider how small boils come, which are like our skin's threads, just as the joiner of a woman's garment, and there are many of these appearances.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	There are some large and such ones where there is moisture as well as pulsation;
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	and if it is of such that are hard and resistant to cutting, and there is no doubt, then the arteries do not act against it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of size is such that you must try all instruments called "entromissory", from which the form comes as follows, something it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, and they open it from above down, it causes pain.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	And when the moisture is drained, if it does not leave any trace of the skin containing the moisture, because it returns again when left alone.
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if present;
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	if not, with water and twine, and apply to the wound, and leave it until the other day;
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	and they will correct those who are delayed from breathing.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	And then begin the bandage again, as before, on the second day, and the third, as long as you know that it does not hinder breathing.
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then dress the wound with suitable medicine as long as it is healthy.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	And if the abscess persists and becomes large, following this form, then cut it deeply.
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	and apply these ointments, and scrape all parts, and put all your care into drawing out the poison from the wound where it lies.
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	and if it causes the patient pain, do as I have told you.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do the same for an abscess that is deep, and cut and cure it as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cut into the deep and moist abscess, which is lighter because they have less blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	And if none of these abscesses or parts where there is no moisture, and among these deep abscesses that I extracted from the shoulder of an old woman;
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	and I found the abscess as hard as a sharp, white stone that cannot be broken.
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	and if none of these helps, one would also make a wound as if from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	In other cases of abscesses occurring in the head or neck area, those who come as leaders of the children and affect the roots of the ears, the opening should be kept entirely closed for as long as possible to allow the pus to drain.
et les cure si com il covient.	and treat it as necessary.
des scrophules	Of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times this abscess appears in the neck, and dissolves the adhesions, and engenders anger, and never comes elsewhere in the body, and is painful, and severely entangled with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	And each scrofula (scaly skin condition) is properly located within its own cavity, just as the neck and abscesses in the head, as we have said.
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	and the appearances of these scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	Some of these contain moisture, and some are malicious and do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	in that one where you see a good disposition to the touch, and it resembles the color of healthy flesh, and it is quiet from every side and is not exposed to any coldness in the collar or to the artery or vessel, and is not too deep.
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	you must then lift it from above, and peel it from every part, and the two lips of the heart should be at once, if necessary, as we have said in the chapters of the head.
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	And then pull little by little, and be sure not to catch the nerve or vein, and do not use too much force or dig too deep, so that the hand does not slip, and look ahead too much, lest you catch something you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	And if you catch the vein or artery, and it does not allow you to work, then put in the wound vitriol ground, or any powder that stops blood, and close the wound.
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	and leave it until the abscess is calm, and the wound is softened, and begin to heal.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	And when the wound is stained with blood, it returns to your work, as long as you complete it.
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	then seek your finger's clue if it persists no small scabs, if it scrapes and becomes dirty.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	And if there is a large vein at the root of the scab, it is not enough that you scrape this scab at its root, but tie it with a thick double thread and let it fall without harm.
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	then use the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you clean the entire abscess, it is necessary that you close the two edges of the wound and sew them now, so that there is no unnecessary delay due to the size of the abscess.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	If it is necessary for you to understand how to treat the root of the dislocation, pull it firmly, and dress it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	Those scrofulas that hold an excess, cut them where they seem to be closing;
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	and make the cut as previously mentioned, depending on it, then he applies these remedies and similar things, so that it corrupts those who are delayed by corruption.
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when the wound is well cleaned, if the healing remedy begins to work, as long as it is healed.
de squinance	squinance (Old French) translates to "dislocation
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	The ancients spoke and wrote about the treatment of the throat.
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	but I have never seen it done in our land, and it is written in their word's scripture.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	For those with a narrow throat, it is necessary to avoid the fold in the throat called the "epiglottis";
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	and no help is done through this, because all the veins and the source of the disease are in those who have an abscess hot in the mouth, or in the throat, or in both jaws.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the tongue, it is necessary to cover the epiglote to prevent the damage that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, we should cut it in three circles or four a small slit through, between the two circles or according to the depth of the cut, not into the cartilage;
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and if these muscles are suitable for cutting the epiglottis, so that there is no harm, and the vessels are long and thin.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	And if the master is fearful, then it is necessary to stretch the throat skin all around the wound, and cut the heart until it reaches the bone.
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	and avoid the vessels of blood, if you see anything, and then cut the swelling, as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated by cutting the flowing part of the bone that jumps due to the broken place, and through the loss of voice.
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	And when the hour has passed and there is doubt about the strangulation, bring together the two edges of the wound with care, and cut through them right up to the cartilage.
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then administer medications that induce vomiting, as long as the patient is healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albuscasim (a surgical tool) should not be used unless the throat is completely sealed, and the patient is judged to be near death, as it lacks the necessary strength.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then pinch the epiglottis so that the patient cannot cough, and they will breathe through the wound, thus preventing death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	and for this, the ancients command the wound to remain open until the ill-will of the disease has passed, and it passes in three days or four. And then they command that the wound be stitched and treated, as long as it was cured.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a young woman took a knife, and pushed it into her throat, cutting through part of the channel of her tongue.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to cure her, but I found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that had issued from it, and realized that it had no power to reach the veins or flow into the throat; the only outlet was through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I rushed, and sewed up the wound, and treated it until it was healthy.
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and since the damsel had no further need of it, she returned to her condition before.
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	because I say that in the construction of the epiglottis, there should be no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the great throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	A hernia of the throat is called a "neck hernia," and it is a large swelling in color of an arrow, and it occurs mostly in women.
et est selonc II manieres:	and this is according to two manners:
naturez, et accidens;	natural and accidental;
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	for nature has no power.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	and the accidental is according to two manners, of which one resembles flesh, and the other manner resembles an abscess that arises from an artery.
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and it causes fear, and one should not attempt to make fire outside except in a small space, testing and carefully examining the entire opening.
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	If you let it grow out as much as a new grass, and it does not give way to any force, if it is held tight, just as we hold our own limbs, and treat it with all its equipment, if there is none.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and surround it carefully, and treat it as appropriate, as long as it is completely healed.
des nous	From us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many ways of which I will describe all their similarities;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and it is necessary that I explain the entire difference between our and their origin.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	I say that the cause is heat and fever as long as the ebullition has not passed and the putrefaction is complete.
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	then rest the fever and the heat.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With the new heat, there is neither fever nor pain, and it retains satisfaction, which is its own sack and follows the colour of the body, and begins as a small seed, and grows large.
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and they follow the same appearances, whether it is fat or moist, and have a similar colour as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	You should, when you come to treat someone with a new injury, test and inquire about all the tools called "instrument" according to their form, as described in the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the method of examining abscesses is that you press more or less moistly on the abscess, and move your fingers in and out little by little, until you know that the instrument has reached the center, according to the size of the abscess.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	then extract the instrument, and be careful that no part remains inside.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If the moisture running under the skin changes its color, as I have described for other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if no moisture comes out after inserting the instrument, you know it is a hard abscess. Then make a cross over it and grasp it with pincers, gently peeling it from each side to remove the skin where it lies, so that you treat it properly with new skin.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot pull it out whole, then pull it out in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if nothing remains, it will return to the body many times.
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if a small amount remains and does not cause you pain, apply some corrosive powders or hot compresses to the wound, close it up, and treat it with soothing remedies until it heals.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if the wound becomes large, cut both edges of the wound and treat it with remedies to prevent infection.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	and if the pain is strong or severe, use quick-acting vinegar and leave it for two to three days until the wound heals and the blood flow subsides.
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	then return to covering what has been dislocated from the new.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	See the shapes of the instruments used, which are of three types:
grans et moien et petit;	large, medium, and small;
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	and take three quarters which are called "albaret," and one which is called "breb," and there are three ways of doing this:
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	grasp, gentle, and small, to encircle the abscesses of fistules;
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and are also like needles with which the spells are cut, and they are of gold, or iron, or silver, and the ones that are yellow are more effective in encircling the abscesses of fistules.
et sont de III manieres:	and they are of three kinds:
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	great, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the opening's size.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	The shapes of the incisions are much alike, as you can see here:
grans, moiens, et petis;	great, medium, and small;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	and if the incisions have two curves of three kinds as well;
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	and if they are once that have three curves, and are also of three manners;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	and if they are once that have two curves, and once only one curve, and are of three manners;
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and all this is necessary for their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of these, which is made to cut, is sharp, and there are some that do not cut well from both sides, which scratch the skin, so that one does not sever the vein or nerve.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	and from these intrusions, the threads are withdrawn in different ways, so that the patient does not lose them during the opening of abscesses.
et sont de III manieres:	and they are of three kinds:
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	great, small, and medium, as you see.
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and do not use it on any other part than on fleshy parts, such as legs, arms, breasts, and similar places.
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and never use any other small instrument, resembling the edges of fingers, according to this form, to stop the blood.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it should never be placed in a place that heals the cutting of veins, and arteries, and never according to this great form.
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	never inflame the breasts of any man when they begin to be corrupted, as long as they appear like a woman's.
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	and remain disfigured and swollen, and anyone who wants to cure them must act carefully according to this form of this line b until g.
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then remove the fat, and apply medicinal fire to the wound, then close the two lips of the wound with stitches, and heal it as long as it is clean.
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	and it holds the eyes steady, relaxing them due to their great size, as happens with women, if they pinch in two ribs above, through two similar openings;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	so that one holds the other at the end of both, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line .b. to line .g.
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then scrape off the skin between the two lips, remove the fat, and apply what we have mentioned about stitching and powders, and whatever is necessary in the treatment, as long as it is healthy.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not clean, or the incision is not fully made, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to blood flow, it is necessary that you fill the wound with moist cotton in a corrosive dressing.
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and leave it until it absorbs the moisture and fat, then treat it when it is clean.
des apostemes des asselles	Of abscesses under the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	Abscesses under the armpits that present as hard scrofulous nodules or with scales, and if they contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line B to line G.
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess has been drained, apply clean cotton to the wound and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton and continue with appropriate treatment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess resembles scrofula, they should treat it as we have said in the treatment of scrofula, and if the wound gapes, apply cautery as we have mentioned before.
de la routure de l’artere	from the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is exposed and the skin above it is sewn shut, many abscesses often form, and this also happens in the vein with an infected and abscessed swelling.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if you recognize it thus, as coming from an artery, then cut deep into the abscess;
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement;	and when you feel it with your hands, if the feeling is strange;
et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when it is about the vein, there will be bright red appearance;
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is foolish to cover this abscess, especially when it is deep within the flesh and filled with angers and other parts, and it is very great.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	It is necessary to avoid iron care, and he who has a main injury should also be careful, and for him who has an arteriolar injury, make a cut through the skin from above for a long time.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then open the flesh at certain intervals, and carefully remove the artery from the tissues while it is exposed.
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples;	then insert a needle from below and pierce it through to the other side, gripping the artery with a double thread in two places, as I have taught you about the extraction of the two arteries in the temples.
puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	then mark the place between the two links of an instrument until no blood comes out from it, and carefully open the abscess.
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	then apply the treatment gently, as long as the wound is open.
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then apply this treatment to the healing wound as long as it is healthy.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	and if the abscess is as large as a vein, it is necessary that you hold in your hand what you can of the abscess across all the skin, then insert the needle through the place you are holding in your hand, and pierce it, and make a double thread, so that you draw it from the other side.
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil;	then, as I have told you, take the abscess, where one of the parts of the bone meets the other through the flesh;
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus;	and if you doubt that the thread is not strong enough, insert another needle through all parts of the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and hold the threads in four places.
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then cut the abscess until the excess is removed, then cut away the excess from around it and leave what is attached.
puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then place a moist cloth soaked in wine and oil on it, then administer treatments with bandages and poultices until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	from the abscess of the nail bed
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	As abscesses come from arteries and veins, so too do they occur in the nail bed when it is injured or subjected to excessive strain, and similar conditions.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this occurs more often with dislocations and joints in all limbs, which are painful abscesses, and their appearance resembles the color of the body, and they have many different arrangements causing pain.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	and when they stretch it, the patient feels pain, and it is not entirely healed to the body's satisfaction but rather pulls away from the heart.
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer:	and it must remain still in all directions, neither going forward nor backward, neither above nor below; and the one with joints should not be covered with iron.
par aventure i vanroit contraction;	Perhaps he might experience a contraction;
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and he who is the head or forehead, makes the skin contract with the spatula.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, if you have pliers, cut it off at its base;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is large, if you hang it with a hook, and peel it off, then remove the bone and close the wound with stitches, and apply the cure until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	Des grosses boces pendans" translates to "hanging large mouths" in
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros;	No such thing happens in bellies or any other place, and it is a disease called "fungus" because of its appearance, it has subtle roots, and big excrements.
et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	and it has small and large parts.
et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	and I have seen at home those who had these in their bellies that were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, they were white, had a thin root, were deeply split, and constantly exuded moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I collected them and found one weighing XVIII ounces and the other VI З. The work in the incision is such that if you look at the patient, you will see they are moist, and the color of the joint is white and moist with a subtle root;
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	if it is scooped out with a wide spatula, then perform the fire cautery in your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	For cutting often brings great risks of bleeding, and if blood does not cease, then hasten to cauterize.
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors;	and if you see the patient afraid and anxious about the incision, take a well-made thread of silk, and bind it as we have said, and leave it for a day.
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail;	then hold it in place, and do not stop pulling the thread of silk until it dislocates the joint, and feel for its release.
et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne;	and if the roots are thick, be afraid to dislocate them especially in the abdomen, but you can still dislocate half of them, then cauterize it so that it does not come back.
puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	then treat the wound, and ensure you do not cover the part that is of a bad colour, with poor sensation, and leaking milk.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an enlarged abscess, and I will come to the treatment of this ulcer later.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the wound is closed.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the bulge is due to cautery or an incision on the bowel or bladder, and it is located in the abdomen and not in any of the bowels, as it occurs in other openings, or blood coming from veins or arteries according to what is above, or from flatulence;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	and if it is through the opening of the bowel and through the discharge of the bladder, then the colour of the abscess resembles the colour of the skin, and it is a slight thing without pain, and opens up from various issues.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the intestines, then it is more diverse, and when you press it with your fingers, it recovers and then returns, and perhaps it becomes squeezed, greatly constricting the entrance to the bath or through hard work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie;	And if it is due to moisture, it is a slight thing, and opens well when you press it with your hand, it does not constrain.
et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	and if it is due to blood, it opens up with these signs: a swollen and hard abscess, and is fixed in quantity.
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	and if it is due to wind (or gas), it is soft upon touching, and the work (or condition) is such that you look and see it appears due to blood from an artery, or vein, or wind (or gas).
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If it is necessary, you must leave the cure.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, both for the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is due to the intestine or bowels, then you must instruct the patient to keep still, and lie flat, then tie a sign around the entire circumference of the belly.
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then command the patient to gently move it between your hands, then go around the place you marked with the whole edge of the bandage, and stretch half of the abscess above all the great needle.
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	then tie it around with a strong thread or firm silk string, and make sure the wound is completely closed.
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	then open half of the abscess extended over the ligament, and stretch your finger index, and seek the intestine.
