se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	if you feel it caught in the ligament, free it, and pull the intestine out through the opening in the abdomen.
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	and if you find the bowel, catch it at the narrowest point, and cut off the excess.
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	and if the artery or vein runs counter to your work, then return to your task and take two needles, and push them through firmly, and turn both needles in the direction you have made the piercing.
puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	then stretch the abscess in four directions over the needles, and if you see them, remove the needles, and leave the joint to rot until it disintegrates on its own;
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	when it is soft and pliable, then treat it as it should be treated, and cure the abscess as we have said;
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and extract the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the joint as it should be treated, and bind the joint.
dou chancre	A cancerous wound
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer;	We have spoken in the previous section about the appearances of ulcers, and how they should be treated with medicine, and how one must avoid the iron cure.
et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement;	and let us speak of the ulcer that erupts in the mouth, and take great care in its cure, and say to the ancients that when an ulcer is in a place where it can be scraped, as with an ulcer on the breast, or on the thigh, or similar places, then all of it must be removed when it first appears.
et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner;	and when it is large and old, then you should not approach it, for I never knew anyone to be cured of it.
ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	no one has ever been cured of it before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire;	And for the work, when it is in place or can be removed, as we have said, it is that you should at no time rid the patient of black blood;
puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige;	then make it healthier if there is evident swelling, then cut the patient's pain in the good place to perform the work;
puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier;	then pour your ointments or chancre, and the head from all parts, and the bone from all parts, leaving nothing behind;
et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and let the blood flow out completely, and carefully press the place in your hand or with any object, and if the bleeding continues from the artery or vein, cauterize it until the blood is stopped.
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then seek other treatment as long as he is healthy.
de ydropisie	Of hydropsis
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer:	We have previously discussed the similarities of hydrops, and in what way the accumulation of water occurs, as well as the signs of each condition, and the treatments using medications, and those cured with iron.
si est eclites soulement;	if it is only inflamed.
et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances:	and one should not apply iron to these two conditions.
c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose;	This is to know, namely, tympanitis and yposchrodia, for it is a deadly thing;
donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses;	Then, when you treat this appearance of edema called "ecrites" with medicine, and the cure does not benefit the patient, consider if they are weak or if they have another illness besides edema, such as stomach troubles, diarrhea, and similar conditions.
si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance;	If you do not touch it with iron, for there is doubt.
et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	If you see the patient is very strong and has no other illness but edema alone, and they are neither too weak nor too strong, then thus should you act:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	Place the patient upright on your hands, and the attendant presses the belly while bringing water to the lowest part of the wound, then take the spiny spatula according to this form.
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And make incisions from both sides.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	with a point, but not so deep as to reach the intestines when inserted, and it cannot tear.
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines:	then check if there is any inflammation towards the intestines:
si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil;	if it is necessary that you open them from the anus, insert the knife three fingers deep directly below the knuckle.
et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois;	and if there is a drooping due to sick liver, it is on the left side of the buttock three fingers' breadth;
et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	and if it is due to mucus, it should be on the right side, and it does not suit that the sick lie on the fracture so that excesses do not flow to that weak place.
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor;	then perforate all the skin with the instrument, and press, and hold your hand over all the space between the skin and the muscle as if scraping it to the quantity of a fingernail or around.
puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	then pierce the wound until the sponge comes to the surface, and this is the blood, then pull out the tool, and take out this instrument which forms:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus;	and it resembles a thin silver chain, made of fine or light gold, and on the underside there is a small opening.
et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus;	and on one side, three openings;
et II d’autre part, et I d’autre;	and two on the other side, and one on the other;
et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	and it is the bone cut as if with a quill, and this is the form of the incision that the scribes make with the quill:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument;	at the top of them is the inflammation, so that when the instrument comes into contact with water, it now descends onto the instrument.
vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	empty it then half or a third, for if you remove more than is necessary at that moment, by chance the patient might die due to the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he might lose his palm, or come close to death.
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz;	but according to the amount of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue in the sick person mean, and their pulses.
puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere;	then take the instrument and hold the water, and it is now held by the force that stops the gap on the affected part, of which I have spoken, so you pierce according to this manner.
puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	then continue with the instrument the next day, if you see the patient suffering, and take a small quantity of water;
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	Take no action, and keep yourself from straining as long as it doesn't cause any pain but a little bit of thirst.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre;	And if you doubt about the patient and leave them with much thirst, treat them with a burial mound or hot sand, and by sweating or a bath and in the sun, and dyeing with wine;
et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	and treat them with drying medications as long as they are healthy, and apply cautery to the stomach and liver and spleen after draining the water, as I have said above.
de l’estopement de la verge	from the obstruction of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No child is born without an opening in the penis, or if the opening is small, or it is not in its proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary to pierce through all the subtle spatules according to this form.
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet;	Then insert or open a subtle plug from below, and hold it and keep it thus for three days or four, and when he wishes to urinate, the plug will be removed, and he will urinate, and then have it replaced.
et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	and if, by chance, he does not remember, since the hot urine will not allow the plug to be kept closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the opening is small, it is a gentle closure of the bladder, as we have said, and it will enlarge.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut;	Those who do not have a plug in their place are cursed, because no one is born with a plug at the top of their penis, so they cannot urinate until they lower their penis.
et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	and they cannot move because the material cannot reach the joint, and this is a serious illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient;	And the method of the procedure is that the patient should lie on their back, then the upper arm and shoulder blade should be positioned as if it were a quill, so that the opening is in the middle, as it should be.
et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and be careful of the bleeding that often occurs, and if it happens, apply pressure to stop the blood flow, and treat the wound until it heals.
des pustules de la verge	from the pus of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide;	Many times this illness comes to the tree (body), and it is an appearance of a ugly scar;
et en i a malignes et non malignes;	and it has both malignant (cancerous) and benign (non-cancerous) forms;
si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien;	you should then make them (wounds) bleed gently, clean and dress them with moist cotton in an Egyptian manner;
puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	then continue the dressing (process) until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the illness is malicious, with a putrid and foul appearance, it requires cautery treatment.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier;	Once you have it, and if the splint is tight around the limb, part of it inside the skin and part outside, then you must first remove the splint that is inside.
et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	and if it is nailed, then pull it out.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion;	Because when you bind it together, unless the position of the limb is assured, then there will be piercing, and blackening and decay in the bone and joint.
si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	so it is necessary to remove all that is black and corrupt, then bind it with a plaster of honey and flour made from red apple bark and wool, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if a blood flow occurs, then apply the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble:	The cautery helps as the disposition of the limbs allows:
c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption;	that is to say, at the discharge of pus, and at the corruption,
et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi;	and if the tip of the rod is corrupted and withdrawn, it is necessary that you insert or drive a plug of wood into the rod, and let the patient urinate among them.
et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	and when the hair is seen to be dry at the top of the rod, which happens to those who have not been circumcised, or it causes a wound or abscess, it is then necessary that you scrape it with a sharp instrument, until the bonds are freed and all parts of the rod's opening are healed.
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil;	and if it is a difficult thing to devise, then you should scrape it with the spatula at any point on the stick and the blade.
puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	then separate the pieces gently, and place a thin, moistened linen cloth over it with cold water, so that it does not dry out immediately.
de la circoncision	from circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies;	Circumcision is not a dislocation of continuity like other wounds;
toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	however, when we perform this work of our own will, especially on children, it is necessary that we make the best and lightest operation for their healing.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of circumcision for their children, because they do not use it in their law, and we only have what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule;	For I have seen most of the masters and elders who performed circumcision near the anus, and they had great strength, and used all kinds of new tools.
si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	if they moved because there were two threads, and by chance one is cut above and the other below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre;	or he reattaches it, and the pain is doubled, and the purification of the wound near the anus is not assured for the point of the member.
et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	and to the purification of the nail, by chance the iron escapes and the wound heals, and often it happens that they do not need purification, and I have seen this happen.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the washing done with force on all the links of thread, I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces cut precisely from above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens;	For when you press your hand, if it is even in all parts, then you can feel the pulse.
mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir;	but the fingers should be well stretched around the skin.
et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	and the first method should be gentle if you want to encourage the child to breathe, if it hears, that you are only tightly tying the thread around the umbilical cord and then releasing it in all ways, so as not to hurt.
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens;	then stretch it straight between your hands and regain the strength in your hands or feet so that the baby does not see any of the tools.
puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens;	then place your hand on the staff and blow through your breath, holding it at the top until the end of the staff is together.
puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien;	then thoroughly clean it from the dirt that is gathered on it, then tie the joint with a double thread, and bind it to another string.
et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	and hold it at the second tie with the little finger and thumb, and cut between the two strings, then gently lift the breath from above and hold the top of the staff.
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres;	then let the blood flow drop by drop, for that is how it heals.
et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and place powder on top and below the powder I mix with a half cup of cooked egg white tempered with rose water, confit with good rose oil and fresh, and leave it until the other day, and treat with another treatment as long as it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste:	The method for purification is as follows:
li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	both feet should be clean and cut, and the nails should also be long and even:
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision;	the error in purification is when the veins burst during incision:
donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme;	Then you must extend your finger, so that the joint makes an abscess.
et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	and hold it evenly, and if you cannot hold your finger, use pincers, and then apply the compress.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement;	And if they remain for three days, and the skin under the arrow is swollen, leave it until the abscess has healed, and gently remove the skin.
si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	if the compress is as you can make it, and it protects the part of the arrow, it will not harm anything.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point;	Treat therefore the place of a sudden wound from gunpowder, which we have spoken about in our treatment of gunpowder, and if it is cauterized too much, and goes above, then it will not harm.
cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Treat it, as we have said, while it is whole and healthy.
dou retenement de l’urine	retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is a sign of stone or frozen blood, or bowels, or a blocked passage, or similar conditions, as we have said in our divisions.
et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz;	and if the urine cannot be released, and you see the retention due to a stone in the bladder or at the neck of the bladder, then the patient should be bent over on his knees.
et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet;	and place them incorrectly on their back, and stretch their belly from the upper part of their back, and hold the patient still as much as possible.
et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	and then they constrict the colic of the bladder at the expression of the stone above, so that the urine is released.
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme:	and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer extraction with all the instrument called "syringe", which has this form:
et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil;	and let them be delicate silver arrows, as if from a bird's feather;
et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	and let the knife be one palm long and half again, and sharp at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue;	And the method of urination is that you take a double thread, tie one end with a wool or cotton ball at the urethral opening, and then wrap the other end tightly around your finger inside the syringe.
et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	and cut off the excess thread and squeeze it tightly towards the top of the syringe, then grease the syringe with oil or butter and egg yolk, place the patient in a comfortable position, and rise the bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and lukewarm water.
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude;	then gently insert the syringe into the shaft, until it reaches the base of the penis, then bend the penis upwards towards the body.
puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors;	then squeeze the syringe before reaching the bladder, and feel the patient's pain reaching the empty thing, and this is not done properly according to these orders because the direction it goes in is twisted.
puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	then pull the thread through all the wool bit by bit, and the urine follows the thread, then extract it forcefully, and stop the urine flow.
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	and begin the syringing as long as the bladder is empty and the patient is calm.
des maladies de la vessie	From the diseases of the bladder.
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When ulcerations or abscesses come to the bladder, and putrefaction is gathered there, you should draw off water and medicines through a device called a "clepsydra", and it is made in this form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus:	It is closed, and if it opens again:
II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois;	from one side, and the other, as you can see;
et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	and the hair roots by which the cure is made so sharp that it stops the pain without addition, if we can extract the moisture and drive out as much as necessary.
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens;	and when you see your drugs in the bladder, place the end of the probe in the moisture, and pull gently until it is out.
si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens;	if you pull out the moisture with the probe, then quickly twist the handle firmly inwards;
si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	if the moisture goes inside completely and comes to the bladder now, so that the patient feels it;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie:	and this is the form of a gentle enema by which the bladder is enemeated;
si est ci:	If there is a fire burn:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut;	And it is of silver or gold, and it is the most precious part;
et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet;	and remove it from the skin where it adheres.
puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu;	then take a sheep's bladder and fill it with the moisture you intend to use for a warm enema; then bind it between the two breasts with a strong double thread, and heat the moisture over the fire.
puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	then insert the tip of the enema bag into the rectum, and squeeze your hand over the bladder until the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder.
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor;	and if you do not have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle of it, and pierce it evenly all around.
puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument;	then insert a strong thread into these openings, reassemble the circle as one does with a dal (a traditional dish), and inside place what you see fit of oil and moisture and water, and bind it with the instrument.
et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	and do as you did with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	from the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines;	We have already discussed the methods of cutting and extraction, together with medicinal remedies.
et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille;	and he explains the distinction between a stone that has grown within a person, its signs, and in which stone one must perform surgery.
et en la vessie, et en la verge;	and in the bladder, and in the penis;
et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit;	I say that the stone which is inside the bladder occurs more frequently in children, and it is a sign of acute urinary tract infection, similar to water in its subtlety.
et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist;	and open the wound wide, and greatly soothe the patient's pain, and probe it many times, and then it heals slowly.
et a mout de ces saut li fondemens;	and at the mouth of these sores, we find their origins.
et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece;	and the healing of children is light until they are four years old, and it is very difficult for the elderly, and it is in the middle for those between youth and old age.
et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	and the cure is lighter for those who have great stones than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to treatment, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient with a enema, to draw out all the impurities from the bowels.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it often becomes trapped, seeking to pass the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut;	Then take the patient by the feet, and upright him, and move him from side to side, so that the stone descends to the very bottom of the bladder, and never stays in the high part.
puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval;	then make him sit between your hands, with his hands resting on his thighs, so that the bladder is completely inclined downward.
puis la quier et la touche dedens;	then place your hand inside and touch it.
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	if you feel the stone in the space, then hasten now to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis;	And if it does not yield to pressure from the fingers, moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand, and the patient is suffering from a chronic condition, or your middle finger for a younger patient;
et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie;	and press it firmly in its base, grasp the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, if there is pain in the groin area;
puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	then press with your finger, and the stone will move away from where you feel it;
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille;	And instruct the patient to press the bladder with their hand, and command them to stretch their right hand above them, and with their left hand, remove the skin covering the stones in the area where the incision is made;
puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	then I press the sponge tightly, which forms this shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre;	and make incisions between what is between the cheeks and the anus, not in the middle but along the left side of the opening.
et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	and it should be straight on the stone, and your fingers should be either above or below it, and cut across so that it becomes wide enough to accommodate the stone's size, but narrow inside, according to the quantity of the stone, not too large.
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail;	in case the fingers pressing on the one below (the stone) suddenly slip, so that it comes out without effort;
et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges:	and knows that there is hard or sharp stone where it has corners or edges.
si est griés a issir;	if it is caught trying to escape;
et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	and if it is like a thread, thin and round, whose exit is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant;	At the place where it has corners and edges, make the size larger;
et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe;	and if it does not yield, you need to use pincers that are also like a file on the tip, to extract the stone so that it does not escape.
ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief;	you must remove the sharp instrument from the shoulder;
et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	and if you cannot do it thus, if the wound widens and the blood flows, and the sinew strains like vinegar;
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	and if there is more than one stone, first remove the largest one at the base of the bladder, then cut it out, and after that pull out the smaller ones if there are any others.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, they must cut it out carefully, making a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide:	For two things often happen to the patient:
ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder;	if he dies, or the urine comes back again through the opening where the bones cannot join together;
mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	but nevertheless make every effort to draw it out or clean it out with pincers, as long as you treat it piece by piece;
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut;	and when you have completed your work, apply to the wound incense and aloe and dragon's blood, tighten it, and place over it a moist cloth in oil and wine, or oil and rosewater and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess;
puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	Then resolve the patient's complaint on his collarbone, and do not loosen the bandage for three days.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you dislocate it, if a lot of oil and water arises from the place, then apply the treatment with ointment of dye and basil ointment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine:	And if abscesses form in the wound and cause corrosion, and blood clots in the bladder, and by this means the urination is stopped, known in this manner as sudden with the urine.
boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	Then apply pressure to the wound, and extract the blood clot, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder, and cause putrefaction.
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then cleanse the wound with water and salt and vinegar, and assist it in every way you can, as long as it is healthy.
et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	and it is necessary that all the herbs you use to cure him, tie his two legs, and apply remedies on top of the joint.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir;	And if the stone is small, and it is located in the urethra, and it is stuck together, and urine cannot pass through.
si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	if you cure it as I say, cutting many times, then the size of the cut is an excuse for its size due to this cure.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have tested it this way.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take the iron at the beginning according to this form, and place it at three angles into the fire:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie;	then take a thread and tie it around the urethra behind the stone so that it cannot go back into the bladder;
puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere;	then gently turn the drill into the stick until it reaches the stone.
et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part;	and turn the drill back to your hand in the stone little by little, as you can pierce the stone from another side.
si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	if the urine comes, then press your hand against that which is stuck from the stone inside the stick.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	if it is finally broken and bursts with the urine, causing the patient pain;
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie;	and if you cannot do this for any reason, then take a sharp stone and another from above, then make the stick into a hook on the stone between the two links, then pull it out forcefully, and loosen the ligament, and clean the frozen blood in the wound.
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it while it is clean.
de la piere des femmes	of the woman's stone" (referring to kidney stones)
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses:	It is rare for stones to become entangled in women, and if it does happen, the treatment is difficult, and it is hindered by three things:
l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge;	One reason is that perhaps the woman is a virgin.
et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	and the second reason is that one cannot find a woman well-versed in uncovering herself for men, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains;	And the third way is that, perhaps, one cannot find a woman well-versed in this art of healing.
et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil;	and the fourth way is that the stone in the woman's body is often harder than in men, so a deeper incision must be made, and great care should be taken. And if it becomes necessary, you must seek the help of a wife well-versed in this art, and with barely any time to spare, and if you do not find one, then do not hesitate to use a subtle, uncast method.
et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	and it presents a wise dance in the life of women, where a woman who knows a part of the art, and instructs her to do what you command regarding the investigation of the stone;
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge:	and carefully consider if this woman is a virgin:
adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere;	then she must remove her hand or finger and seek the stone;
et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and if she finds it, despite the pain in her finger, she should remove her finger or hand from the stone, and advise her to withdraw her finger or hand with the patient, pressing her left hand on the swollen bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse;	If it is cut, it is necessary to move it little by little from the entrance of the bladder down to the thigh bone, until it reaches the root of the thigh.
puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie;	then cut into the stone at the root of the thigh, where it is most painful, and feel the pain in that part.
et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	and do not move it from above or below the stone, but make the first cut small.
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont:	then insert the blade into the cut, feeling the pain deeply in the wound as much as the stone can come out, and know that there are many ways of stones.
c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	This is to know, small and large and rough and smooth, long and round, and which have roots.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you know these things to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And if the wound does not heal, take vitriol powder and apply it to the place, holding it for an hour until the pain is alleviated.
puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	then return to your work, as long as the stone is hard, and have the tools I told you for extracting stones from people to assist you in your task.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide;	and if the wound persists, and it is an artery that has been cut, apply powder to the place and press with bandages and bindings, and do not repeat this, leaving the stone and not pulling it, unless the patient dies.
puis cure la plaie.	then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is calmed and the eyes open, return to your work while the stone is still hard.
de hernie carnouse	of flesh herniation
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef;	Raming water is nothing other than the combination of moisture or white starch, which is detached from the heart of the objects, containing the heat.
et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef;	and it is called "starch", and it is never properly in the cloth of the egg, if one believes that it is another substance.
et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit;	and it is the skin of the object between the white starch that we have mentioned.
et ceu n’avient se poc non.	and this happens no more.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this rameous is due to weakness that affects the testicles, and this material expands.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors:	And never does it come from a blow on the joints, and this moisture has many colors.
ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	or it turns to yellow, or it is without red, or black, or clear white, and this happens more.
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	and these are the signs to recognize this assembly, for if it is white as we have said, then the abscesses are red, very long like an eye, and do not open the joints, because moisture surrounds them all.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if there is moisture in the wound itself, so it appears as an abscess with part of the flesh, and because of this, one thinks it is another wound.
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien;	and if there is moisture between the skin of the coils and the white part, then it smells well.
donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	then when you see to know the colour of the moisture, try to pull out all the foreign objects within it, which will show its form beforehand.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after, judge of what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors;	And when we treat it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be healed according to their strength and the replenishment of their body;
puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	then lay him on his back, on one thing a little raised, and place beneath him several sheets of cloth.
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions;	then sit him on his left side, and command the attendant to sit on his right, and extend the staff towards one of the two ribs at the heart's edge.
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	then take the scalpel, and cut through the skin of the ribs from top to bottom, and make your cut completely straight by following the contour of the rib's skin until it turns white, and carefully strip away the flesh according to its natural tendency.
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont;	Then make a clean cut with a sharp instrument through the soft tissue filled with water, and extract all the water, then place your fingers, and the swelling will subside.
et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement;	and do not touch the heart of the swelling, but only the affected area.
cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	cut it all or in pieces, carefully along the edge, for if you do not cut it cleanly and sharply, the water will return.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac;	and if the bubble bursts out of your control, it is important to return it to its place once you have completed the work with the swelling.
puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then join the two books of the heart with a stitch, then treat it as other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc;	And if you find the heart corrupted by another illness, it is necessary that you bind the veins that are suspended, in doubt of the flow of blood.
puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	then cut the vein from all that is suspended, extract the heart, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices;	And if the vein is joined into two parts, knowing that these are two branches;
si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	if you treat the other part just as you did the first one evenly, then wipe away the blood, and put a clean moistened compress over the wound with rose oil.
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and place another moistened cloth with wine and oil, and put two cushions on top, and cover it with double-layered fabrics, and bind it tightly according to this form.
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil;	Then take two fabrics, make them of shredded wool according to this appearance and join them with stitching at the top of the leg opening, one covering the inside from the crotch to the back, and the other covering the outside from the wrist to the tip.
et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	and the other two joints at the top of the two arms, and gather all the restrictions in the loop of the arm's bone;
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	and under no circumstances should this cautery branch be used on a limb the size of iron, but rather you should make a delicate cut with a scalpel, and strip the skin from the veins, and heat it as we have said before, so that the white part containing the blood is exposed.
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	if you take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that white part at certain intervals, and peel it with this hot and delicate cautery.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout;	And the doctor, in every way you can, as long as you stretch it all out;
et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef;	and ensure that the fire does not touch the egg;
et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve;	and know that this work is safer;
et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	and hold them steady, preventing blood from escaping, and move the tools carefully;
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	and if anything goes against you, whether an abscess or bleeding or any other complication, treat it as described above.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit;	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to undergo this operation due to its horror, then administer perforation as I have told you, and make sure that when you are certain through the signs we have mentioned, that the dislocation is caused by moisture, then leave the patient in a raised position.
pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors;	then incise the abscess at the base of the entire spatule-shaped area deeply with the perforator.
et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	and make the perforation wide enough for all the pus to flow out.
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	then place a cloth on it, bind it, and let it heal, then treat the wound until it is clean;
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant;	and if the white cloth does not allow the blood to flow out of the wound, it is necessary that you insert a needle or the instrument used to drain water from wounds, in such a way as to form (the desired effect) beforehand;
et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	and carefully probe the wound, and know that if blood returns, it gathers after six months or so, and when it gathers as before, then the patient will recover his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	You know that in the treatment of this branch there are more harmful dispositions, which is why it seems to me that it is better to leave it alone.
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	and I will tell you about the work and appearances of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions;	I therefore say that many abscesses come where there is inflammation, especially in the bowels.
et c’est par mout de cas.	and this is through many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	This is to know by way of excessive acidity and aguity, which is spread through wounds or percussion.
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors;	and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the flesh.
et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	and it causes no pain, but the abscess is painful.
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	and sometimes it is a grey and purple abscess, with a bright red color, and does not come from any new artery or vein swelling.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is from an artery, if it is known by the hot swelling of the abscess, when you press it with your hands;
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and it is not appropriate that you touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	What is made from vein inflammation is known by its arrangement in the gentle touch of the hands, and it can be carefully cut along this line, and on other similar parts.
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and it is that you cut the cord of the veins, then the heat goes up, and the white color becomes satisfying, and releases the suspending from all parts of the heat.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the eye is already inflamed with these hot poultices, then it is necessary that you treat the eye and the socket.
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	and if it is swollen to the point of pain, or in those parts within the veins, then you must release all that pressure, and treat the socket accordingly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the source of the pain is behind, it is necessary that you remove it entirely, and extract the foreign body, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is completed, immediately apply a moist woolen compress with rose oil and wine to the wound, then use other remedies until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	This is an abscess wrapped in a similar covering to a boil, with the softening of the tissues, and it prevents the patient from moving much due to the pain.
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	and the treatment for this illness is also very painful, as I have mentioned before, and nonetheless we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	It is necessary that you make the patient lie on a clean bed, then apply a suspension of herbs below the armpits on both sides, to all the vessels close to the limb, and wrap them tightly with bandages.
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	then cut with a sharp spatula along the vessels, as they are exposed, and then scrape from each side, as we have said in the extraction of arteries that are in the temples.
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	then he inserts an needle with a double thread, and ties it to the first place where the bone came out, and then ties it again to the other side.
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	Then place them correctly in the middle, according to the length of the body, and remove the corrupt moisture.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	then treat the wound as with others, binding it tightly so that no one lags behind;
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	for if no harm comes from it, and all the vassals come together, then it is necessary to bring everyone together;
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	so that the eyes do not lose their vision due to the incision of the vassals, and become dry and cannot help themselves.
de la routure dou syfac	From the rupture of the sinew.
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The remedies of this branch are obtained through incision where it is needed, or by extending it on the belly in the region of the angles, so that the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the organs.
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes:	and this rupture is either from the incision or from the extension, and these two methods of movement have various causes:
ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	or from percussion, or jumping, or screaming, or the lifting of heavy sorrow, and similar things;
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	and the signs when it is from the extension, are that it happens little by little, over a long period of time, and does not come suddenly.
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	and it makes the abscess even until it reaches the healthy part, because it pleases to straighten the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the sign is when it is from the incision that a sudden pain arises at the beginning, and various abscesses appear under the skin close to it, due to the discharge of the intestine and the flow of blood from the syphilis.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And never remove the pus with the intestine, as it becomes stuck and causes great pain for the patient, especially when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these poor treatments with iron, for which one must be wary.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And the method of this work is that you instruct the patient to straighten the intestine with their fingers inside the wound if they are able.
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	then remember over their collarbone. Between your hands, lift the cheeks.
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	then take the knife above, and shave all the hair from the legs down to the root.
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	then insert into the books of the stomach with hooks according to what you need to open the wound, and be sure that it can no longer protrude.
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	then peel off the skin that is beneath the muscle tissue, exposing the white flesh on all sides until it is completely uncovered.
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac;	then insert your index finger between the muscle, between the white flesh that is beneath the skin of the thigh, and between the second flesh, starting from behind the bone, and between the second flesh.
et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	and then move the hand on the right down towards the heart, and let it rest with its palm facing upwards on your left hand, easing the pain throughout all the affected areas towards the waist.
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	and instruct the attendant to extend the pain-relieving agent upwards, and release that which is behind the bandage.
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	and cut between your fingers if any part of the intestine is wrapped up or has hardened, and if you feel anything, press it into the belly.
puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions;	then take a needle with a thick thread made of X threads, and pass it through the posterior part where there is flesh, after the skin of the cheeks.
aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz;	after the cutting, then sever the parts that appear as threads, as long as there are four threads.
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars;	then assemble them one on top of the other in the shape of a cross, and bind the skin, which we have said is beneath the flesh of the cheeks, with a strong thread from both sides.
puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	then wrap the parts with threads and bind them so that no foreign bodies can enter inside, preventing any abscesses from forming.
et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	and then take hold of the ligament according to the first long ligament, and after these two ligaments, leave it as it satisfies the depth of the tissues, half a digit from the heart of the matter.
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte;	and after all the other according to the shape that the eye has;
puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	then cut into the part that is beneath the skin of the tissues, as long as it is free from bones and muscles, as we have said before;
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	then apply moist wool in oil, and cover the wounds, and apply the ligament as we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never cauterize the white flesh we have mentioned, after incision, out of fear of bloodletting.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui;	For this often happens, leaving the ligament intact until it chooses to heal on its own.
et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	and if it takes time to heal, apply hot water and continue with what we have said until it chooses to heal.
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	then treat the wound with another remedy until it is completely healed.
de hernie carnouse	of flesh herniation
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this case, never has anyone dared to treat it with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the elders say that it is made like a root that holds the joint together, in such a way that you bind the vessels, after trimming them lightly on both sides.
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient;	then cut me open, and treat the abscess of him who opens, until the veins bleed.
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus;	No fracture should occur suddenly, as we have said, and open the joints.
et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	and do not allow any intestines to protrude like buttons, and if they do, it is a sign of great danger, and repair them every hour.
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	and nevertheless if it stays too long at this point, he believes there is a wound or ulcer, until the intestines descend.
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	and this happens due to the extension of the ulcer, which is aggressive, as we have said, because it extends, then softens and swells up, opening up.
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit;	and the treatment is by cauterization, as we have said before;
et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	and it is never cured with iron in this manner:
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois;	and make the patient lie on their back between your hands, then cut the ligament of the dislocation with a sharp knife according to the quantity of three fingers.

et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	and press it fully on the belly, then cut the two apparent ligaments of the dislocation on the side of the needle, and cut each one.
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	then extract the side of the needle, and do not cover the dislocation with any substance or extend it, as I have told you in the treatment of intestinal hernias.
puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	then treat with wound care.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you treat the wounds, if they are dirty and the injury is clean, then do so until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The treatment is difficult, and it has no appearance in the rupture, but the cauterization moves in this place, and is closer to healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the thick skin of the testicles
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir;	Often the walls of vessels in no man's land become softened, because the substances within them are mellowed, and it is visible.
et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil;	and it requires skill, when one wishes to cure it, to lay the patient on his back and cut into the softened tissue on his natural skin.
