dou chastrement	1. This treatise, a guide for medical practices, offers
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre;	You know that chastity is esteemed in our law, and for this reason I would rather not speak of it in this book.
et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres:	and it is not necessary, except in two ways:
dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure;	one is that he should answer wisely when asked, and in a way that indicates the remedy.
et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	and the other, because we often have need of cautery on certain animals to help us, as with a goat and sheep and cat and other creatures.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres:	I say, therefore, that cautery is performed according to two manners:
ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	either by attraction or by incision.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant;	In the method where we employ attraction, let us immerse the animal in hot water, so that the muscles relax and remain relaxed.
puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	then press it with your hand until it is healed and you no longer feel it.
Du chastrement de taille:	From the castration of the body:
covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez;	It is necessary that you hold the animal, and press the hide of the testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspender, and cut each one separately, when you have well scorched them.
et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz;	and do not leave any pain or discomfort, nor the subtle pleasure that is on the vessels.
et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure;	and this method of castration is superior to that which is done by attraction, because with attraction, perhaps something from the testicles remains, causing the animal to desire lust.
puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	then treat the wound as long as it is clean.
des hermofrodites	Of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes:	Hermaphroditism exists in two manners among humans:
l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	one is when it is between the two sexes so similar to the form of a woman's nature, with hair and never cuts short.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is in women, who have a penis on their hand, as if it were a phallus, and two vulvas.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies;	And the treatment for both men and women is that you remove all the infected parts, and treat them as other wounds.
en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	In a second manner, of men whose urine jumps through the skin of the testicles, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	Of the tendon
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir;	Tendons are a tightly adjusted char on the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see.
et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	and no woman has it as much as a hand, and that is the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement;	You should remove the excess of tendons from your hand or fingers, and cut them lightly.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do not harm me too much, lest the blood flow bring about further complications, then apply another remedy until he is healed.
et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	and there is another affliction that appears in the mouth of the mare, and spreads, and perhaps jumps, and resembles a cow, and for this reason the ancients called it the "cow disease.
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If it is necessary to take care of it, as we have said before, with the tweezers and cure as long as it is healthy.
de erratique	erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis;	Erroneous is the judgment when the nature of women is not properly perceived, or the opening (hernia) is small.
et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est;	and it is either by nature from birth, or accidentally from illness that it occurs.
ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit;	or it is through the adjustment of parts, or a subtle and specific cause, and is done in perfect harmony, whether in front, or on the side, or beneath, or in any way.
et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir;	and one must be careful with conception, childbirth, and sometimes even the flow of flowers to have.
et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	and the knowledge of these is through the observation of dance.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the dislocation is recently apparent, whether by your own hand or by chance.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi:	If it is a delicate pleasure, and close to the heart, if you are quick, and the tongue thus:
met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes;	with your two index fingers together, and the woman on her back, spreading her legs;
puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens;	then the two hands form a circle, as long as the delicate pleasure is round, and it covers the stoppings.
puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	then take wool and soak it in oil, and place it on the wound, and lay the woman face down each day, so that she cannot move.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the dislocation is hard and deep, then you should use a spatula-like instrument resembling a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope;	If the dislocation is of the shoulder, hold it still with bands and slings.
et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef;	and use remedies to stop blood, such as licorice, dragon's blood, incense, and plenty of eggs.
puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder;	then apply a wide poultice, so that the wound cannot heal.
et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec;	and thus continue for a long time, applying a dry linen bandage.
puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat other ailments as long as he is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when the swelling comes from heat, if it needs to be covered, do so according to this manner; if it is not an abscess, apply compresses.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an abscess swollen from heat, do not apply any treatment with the hand.
des emorroides	From hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul;	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that, without proper care, can become severe. When hemorrhoids have been present for a long time, they tend to worsen.
et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	And we have discussed in the previous section the similarities and signs, and I will now describe those that receive treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and their complications, when they are completely in the rectum, and do not appear to be felt, can only be effectively treated with iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that are at the opening of the rectum can be felt, and these are those that can be treated.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses;	It is therefore advisable to place the woman in a cold house, then apply the other treatments with tweezers, and cauterize her roots, then powder herbal remedies that stop blood flow, such as mullein and dragon's blood, and similar substances.
puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide;	then immerse his feet in the wall for an hour, then place them in cold water;
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	and if the fever persists, prepare a decoction of sumac and bark from pomegranates and gallstones and similar things, then take flour from barley, mix it with honey and oil, and make an ointment to apply to his back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it becomes moist, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir;	If that does not help, apply cupping glasses to his back without injuring the breasts;
puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	then take flax, soak it in the juice of plantains or in the juice of hawthorn with old wine, and apply it to the joint.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when the abscess rests, apply a clean dressing to the wound until it is healed.
et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul;	and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a sharp point, so it should be covered as I have said in the previous text.
et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then apply the cure until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses in women
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many different types of abscesses occur in the body, such as chancre, previous abscesses, herbs, boils, fistulas, hemorrhoids, hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the section.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe;	It is therefore necessary that I explain in this treatise the hot abscess that comes in the gum, which is not a true abscess but one that is bow-shaped.
et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	and if you want to know the work of fire, look to see if the abscesses are inflamed at the beginning of their appearance, and full of heat and fever, and if it turns red, then you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie;	Then do not hasten to pierce, but let it die as long as the pain is soothed;
et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe;	and then make the patient lie on his side, and have him take small sittings, leaning back and resting on his back, bringing his feet together to stretch out the leg;
et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien;	and let his legs be spread apart, and place his arms beneath his knees, and bind them well with a strong ligature.
puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme;	then push the tongue towards the right side, and use the instrument to open the mouth of the wound, from which comes the shape.
et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide;	and it is necessary that when you use this instrument, you first insert the right side to know the depth of the wound, so that what enters with the instrument does not go further than it should, and it does not harm the patient.
et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve;	and if the instrument is larger, it should be covered with a deep layer of cloth so that the instrument does not hurt.
et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	and it is necessary that he places the horn of the instrument above and turns on the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit;	And when the abscess opens and it is punctured gently with the hand, if it is necessary to cover it, use a cloth over the top, leading the pus.
et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec;	and when the bowel is emptied, it is necessary that you place moist gauze in the wound, either with rose oil or dried green oil.
et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites;	and place the clean, moist cloth over the wound at the exact point of the fracture, and place it firmly over the fracture and the attached forearm, using hot herbs or lukewarm water.
puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it after two days of healing have passed, as long as it is healthy;
et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites;	and never raise the fracture or wound with a cleansing of water and honey, and then water or cooked roots of lys and long arista (herbs)
puis reveigne a l’oignement.	then return to the dressing.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is healed in the margin, it is necessary to be careful not to use fire, but treat it as we have said in the previous section.
de l’enfantement	from childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar:	Trade is first in birth that she knows the form of natural childbirth, and the signs are when you see the woman rushing below, and longing to smell the aroma.
adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir;	then the child hastens to be born.
adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui;	then know that these children are according to the natural form, and their heads and shoulders are the first to emerge.
et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost;	and when you see these signs, it is necessary to gently press the belly, so that the child is born quickly.
car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification;	because when it descends towards its head, it follows with him, and is freed from its excesses through good cleansing.
et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	and this, which comes otherwise, does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises;	For it never comes on its own feet, but rather invades the body or attacks a joint, and the hands, or it appears in the abdomen, or above, and turns by chance onto its neck, or takes other malicious forms;
si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	if one must dance, they should be wise and subtle in these matters, washing away error and disappointment, and I will show you all the forms as to how one should assist.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent;	If the fever comes upon his head by natural cause, and the woman gives birth painfully, and her strength is weak, making her stay on a saddle, or women hold her;
et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	and if his nature is of oil or fenugreek cooked, then boil it between his two fingers using the small spatula whose shape is as follows:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers;	and split the second layer, and cut into his nail as much as the moisture that is deeply embedded;
et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament;	and press the woman's belly as the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to enema the woman with fennel seed mucilage mixed with sesame oil;
puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre:	then make him breathe deeply and sneeze from the condition, and hold his mouth and nose for an hour.
si istra maintenant l’enfes.	if the child is now born.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc;	And if both hands come out, it is necessary that you reset them gently, little by little.
et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut;	and if they cannot enter, place the woman on a seat, and raise her feet high.
puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement;	then he should stand up from a seated position on the ground, and tie down the woman so that she does not try to get up.
et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	if he cannot insert his hand, the fetus dies, if he cuts with a knife that is placed before him, extracts the child, and resets it just as before.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	From the birth of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the child comes onto its feet, it should be pushed up.
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	and then turn it back and forth, until it is even.
puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	then press gently from the feet and extend little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	He can jump as high as his feet allow if he is commanded to press, and the action makes him sneeze due to the condition.
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	if he jumps, God wills it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not happen as we have said, if it returns little by little, according to the natural form.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it becomes slightly easier.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier;	And if it does not come out as we have said, take a small amount of musk and oil from the anus, and gum melted, and grind all in a mortar;
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	and place it over the female nature within and outside this remedy, then make her lie in deep water up to the ribs.
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	and when she is soaked, make a collar of myrrh and place it over her, leaving it for an hour.

de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	From the emergence of the child onto its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the child takes this form, it will move its hands little by little.
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit;	then he should be mindful on his collarbone, and let the weight hang down below, and lie still on his side.

et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	and if he feels pain, he should take his feet and move them slightly, then move the belly upwards, and finally bring the hands together.
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc;	and gently move the child.
et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	and instruct the woman to impregnate herself as long as the child is inside.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	From the birth of the child who comes with a large hand during
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	I understand it is my duty to bring back the hand:
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	if it cannot be brought back, then lift the woman and let her go;

de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same manner for all the rest
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it appears in this manner at regular intervals, if the second one catches on your fingernail, while the moisture is being drained.

adonques si istra legierement.	then gently stretch it.
de l’issue des gemelz	from the issue of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII;	Know that many times twins are born, and never more than three or four.
et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	and this is not an unusual thing, and it happens often.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	These are strange things, and they do not live long, without name.
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know that they multiply, and are devoured by the pleasure that creates them, which is related to the mouth.
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	and never depart so naturally from all of us, as we have said.

de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	No joint is ever formed in the margin I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more than XV, and they are all shaped like a child according to the measurement of its glorious sagacity, and it is necessary that the wise healer knows all this, for sometimes a similar occurrence happens.
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	it is done according to what is appropriate.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you cure a woman who has lost her child or is pregnant, as I have said in the previous section, and there is no sign of delivery, and you are forced to intervene by hand;

Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the limb is on its side, and you can put it back in place, apply what we have said for the living child;
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	and if it cannot be joined together again, after being separated into pieces, it leaves no trace of dislocation.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when this is done, apply what we have said about the incisions that come from the sea.
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	and if the flow of blood comes, it should be treated with immediate restraint, and other remedies should be applied.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose belly had been bitten by a child; then I examined another on that same spot, and removed the other bite.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, a painful abscess formed in her cheek, swelling so much that it opened, and began to cause great pain.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to treat it, and I thought for a long time, but could not heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied strong plaster, and an egg came out, and after some days, others.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very surprised because that stomach has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point;	I examine the wound, and if there are broken bones, I treat them until the woman is in better condition.
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and examine the woman long tens thus, and then let go a little of the pain from the blue.
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	and I have never recorded this chapter except because, when the masters encounter a strange thing, they know how to provide aid.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	return the woman to her place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres;	After this comes the form of pressure, with which one binds the books.
et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	and at the second turn, as the second joint of the limbs.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	However, the horns should be more subtle in their tightening, and they should be made of ebony or boxwood;
et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	and the mouth should be wide enough to fit two fists, and the margin of the cut should be one palm and a half long;
et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	and also adjust the two limbs to be equal in length of this same fist, firmly joined together, half a palm's length or slightly longer;
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	and these two adjustments are fitted into the mouth of the joint to open it when turning the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, with a more subtle and lighter appearance, should be made of ebony or boxwood, according to the shape of pliers.
et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large;	and it should have two adjustments, as you see, of a palm's length, and two fingers' width;
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	and when you see the vagina open fully with the instrument, have the woman lie on her back, with her legs apart and knees bent, then carefully adjust both adjustments into the vagina, holding the end of the instrument beneath her hips.
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	then use your hand to grasp the entire instrument, just as you did with the pincers equally, according to the amount that you see opening the mouth of the wound, until the pain ceases to be what it was.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances;	all these instruments are thoroughly constructed and have many similar counterparts;
et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	and when you have equipped them, the more quickly they operate, and the greater their effectiveness for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not disregard the instrument even if you have not arranged it properly, for its necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the second stage of childbirth is reached, it is important that you instruct the patient to hold her breath and then make her sneeze forcefully, holding her hands firmly over her mouth and nose.
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	and if it falls through this, it is fine.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If the bone does not come out, take I a tool, and make I an opening or cover, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the wound, such as fennel, rue, anis, chamomile, kasia, and centaury;
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu;	all of these herbs, or none of them, should be cooked or put in water on the fire;
puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris;	then put a tube or opening into the wound, and the other end in the mouth of the injury, and hold it until the vapor comes inside the wound;
puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	then make him sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the patient experiences a second complication.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine;	And if after this treatment she remains weak, and is not fully recovered, she should be instructed to moisten her left hand with sesame oil or almond mucilage, then apply it to the affected area, and let it rest in that position.
et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	and when she feels it, she should gently press and stretch it little by little straightening, so that the pain does not hinder the extraction.
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie;	but it is necessary to move slightly to the right and left, then pull.
si venra et se desaerdra.	if it comes and goes away.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the mouth of the mare is tightly closed, we have said the remedy of sneezing and inhalation of herbal fumes.
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	and if it is not from all that we have said, be careful not to follow the milking.
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	but it is necessary that one who is at the mouth of the mare, you bind it to the woman's thigh, and then wash it with a four-ingredient ointment.
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer;	if it loosens and resets, it will return again;
mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	but nevertheless, if it loosens and causes a foul smell in the stomach and head, and makes the patient pale.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu:	Therefore, suitable fumigations should be used:
aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	No one among the ancients has tried fuming with arugula and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument with which one cauterizes a woman to stop the flow of blood and milk is as follows:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it is like a glass vessel, and one places the head gently in its natural state, and wide openings over the fire.
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and let there be fumigations over coals, and scabs until they are completely healed, and start again with another one.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who have not yet had their roots pierced, but they are quietly satisfied with a subtle remedy.
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	so it is necessary at the bath to pierce this remedy in its proper place, and do not pierce it with a sharp instrument, and secure the bandage so that it does not touch it.
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then place a moist linen cloth soaked in wine and oil, and continue the treatment with the ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it does not return, insert or open a plug of flesh, and leave it for a long time, and it becomes rigid when the child wants to move into its chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme;	And never does this stopping of the wound or abscess come suddenly;
si covient coper celui soudement:	if it is necessary to stop that sudden flow:
si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	if it is cured, as we have said about the pain of drowning.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula from its foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors;	Fistulas that occur beneath the fundament are called "nodation," and those that come from above the fundament are larger, or in the space between the two parts, if there is one fistula or more;
et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans;	and when this node is old, if it opens again and moisture causes a white or subtle swelling, then these fistulas do not heal.
et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	and they are known to those who observe its management or vent as the patient makes an effort, and by chance one jumps up.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge;	And if the fistulas penetrate just below the bladder, and just halfway up the penis;
et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	and reach just below the knee joint, and just above the calf.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus recognize the present fistula in the fundament, and not middle:
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and if you insert your index finger or fundament, and push a fine needle of steel or iron into the fistula where there is no curvature.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if there is curvature, if you push a thin point, or a horsehair, as far as you feel the point or hair with your finger;
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you do not feel it, and it does not come out with extraction or blowing, as we have said;
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie;	says that he shouldn't pierce at all;
si te haste dou curer.	if you rush the cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula persists up to the bladder or up to the urethra, if it lets go of the urine, and cannot be healed by medications.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it is pierced just before the joint of the thigh, then the blood tends to flow towards the joint;
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	if there is no distortion and the pain around it is not severe, if it bows again later, and no sudden treatment with dressing is effective.
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	And regarding these persistent fistulas, there is no sure cure but through hard work, and the folly of those who interfere.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos;	In the one that is neither persistent nor ancient, there is hope for healing through fire, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient lies on their back between your hands.
et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and flexes their legs up to their thighs, and inclines their hips towards their belly.
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	then wraps a bandage of cloth, or a sponge if there is curvature, as long as you know where the bandage begins.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet;	If the patient feels pain deep within, it is necessary that you press your index finger upon it, and they will then feel the point piercing them.
et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	and if you feel a hole between your thumb and forefinger where the satisfaction or pleasure is felt, then know that it is open.
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	if it does not heal properly with any treatment, then it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	Nevertheless, there is nothing that we can do to fully heal them, but it happens rarely.
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and with this aid, it is when one applies the heat of the cautery gently according to the extent of the fistula, as has been said before.
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement;	and the entire heat is applied to the fistula until it removes the source of the problem.
et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and do this twice or three times, as long as you know that these marks must be burned, which resemble the feathers of an eye.
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then apply warm, moist compresses until the inflammation subsides, and finally, use a soothing treatment that draws out and seals the wound.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he/she is in such a state, it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If this cannot be cured in any other way, then it must be treated thus:
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and insert between them, and do not pierce through to the deep muscle that is at the base, and between your finger and the tent, place a thick covering of cloth or something similar, and you will see the fistula opening where the covering touches the heart.
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	if you seal the beginning of the fistula and pull it back before the tent, then cauterize after, as long as it reaches the top of the tent.
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra;	and he will be freed from pain and suffering.
puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	then identify those marks that resemble a bird's feather, and do not remove anything without reason.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the pain attacks you and cuts between you and the work, cauterize it with fire or sharp medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses:	For fire cautery combines two good things:
c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	that is to say, the burning of these adjusted parts, and the stiffness of blood and the dryness of moisture;
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	then apply a moist cure or something crushed, while the bones are bowed, and push the burnt parts into the bow.
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	Then treat the wound with hot irons and hard charcoal, which are dry medications.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it becomes healthy and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula appears all the way to the bottom of its origin, and it is distant from the body, if you press on its root or origin, it will hurt.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres:	If you feel a tent, and within it is the web or the glue or the charcoal, or it is ready to pierce, and there is no other way out of danger or hope, through the administration of one of the three methods:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	or you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it all the way through, or if you can, you apply a tent and treat it as before.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and do not force me too much, so that you do not disrupt the attachment which holds the fundament, and the expulsion comes from the side without willingness.
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then apply the cure, as we have said;
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	in case it should heal, remove that covering and clean it, then as it is freed from the fundament, either with a needle or another instrument pointed;
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then remove the foreign body from the wound as much as possible;
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement:	then study to restore the wound and hold the fistula in the part devoid of the base.
si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	if it is a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere:	And never are fistulas like this way:
et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	and it is when you push the tent into the fistula, and it is on the side near the base from the leather above, then take a sharp knife at the top according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And press the thread wrong in two, and press the tent along the entire thread into the fistula as far as it goes to the top.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it is persistent on the edge near the foundation within, then extract the thread from that hole, just as you insert your finger into your foundation.
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II;	and take the thread from the head, and gather the two joints together, and tighten one to the other, and leave it for one or two days.
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and do not loosen it, as long as the thread breaks these three threads that are between them, and tighten.
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	then dress the wound as long as it is sealed and healthy.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If you cannot puncture the fistula, no matter what method you use, it will not be too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not appropriate to make the wound too deep, and then treat it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	He describes a form of painful, thorny spasms that cause the formation of a fistula if it is severe and persistent, one side cutting and penetrating.
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and on the other hand not, because one cannot catch what one should not catch, as you see here:
des emorroydes	Of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres:	Hemorrhoids occur in two ways:
ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement;	or they are inside the anus, as hard as a grain of resin, and there can be small or large ones, and sometimes they ooze blood, and sometimes they have one or more, protruding from the anus and extending into the anal canal.
mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	but those that are burnt have little moisture, and still, even now, if there is a little of the citrus water or some blood, and they have the colour of fresh flesh;
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the treatment for those who have them deep within the fundament, so instruct the patient to stretch himself slowly to move into rooms, until the fundament is healed and the children appear.
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	if you act quickly, and have a pair of pliers, or hold it with your fingernail, then cut it at the roots.
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if they cannot hold the eyes due to moisture, if they take them in a cloth, or cotton, or a piece of chamois;
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and then extract them carefully, cut them, and sprinkle hot powders onto the wound that are suitable for cauterization;
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or you cauterize them as it is said in the chapter on cautery, and treat other ailments until they are healed;
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the roots cannot come out, if you give the patient a harsh and biting enema to wash what is in the fundament, so that it can come out firmly.
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	Let the patient lie still, and if their legs are deeply embedded, it is a light cure.
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and if you pin them with your fingernail or pliers, cut them off, then treat them as we have said, while they are still healthy, and fear the incision with iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere:	It is necessary that you administer the stitch according to this manner:
pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large;	take a twisted thread, and wind it into a needle, then pass the thread over the top and pierce the needle from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread back through the needle, making them wide.
et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and hold the thread tight, then twist the thread, and extract the needle, and do thus with all the others, and leave some for draining the excess blood.
puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then place on the base a moist cloth or a rose-colored oil-soaked cloth, and place it over the wound, and instruct the patient to rest.
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then leave it until they heal, and when they have fallen off, apply treatment and other remedies until they are healed.

dou fremit	Douloure" is the Old French word
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	Ants are small, hairy creatures that burrow deep within the body, and they continue to grow in strength.

de la forme dou clistere	of the form of a cloth enema

Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those are therefore small, used in the treatment of children who are weak and suffering.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	He must prepare a small and wide enema if it is too narrow above; thus, the abdomen is tied according to this manner.
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez;	and I say there is a desire or the belly should be tied, as you see, and the feces should be seen to pass through.

puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet;	then the healer should grip the enema bag with both hands together, until it is completely full, then extract the enema and gently lower the patient's legs against the wall, allowing the medicine to exit as best as possible.

des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies;	We have already discussed the treatment of wounds;
or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	or we will tell you the treatments of hands and medicine, according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the parts where the wounds are made, and from what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by the striking of stone, and the cutting of sword and knife, or of spear or staff or arrow, or of similar things;
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or according to the laws of the body, as when a wound breaks out on the neck, or on the head, or on the side, or on the belly, or the liver, and similar parts.
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the treatment for each wound, and begin with simple wounds of the head, because the remembrance will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut:	I say that when a simple wound appears on the head, and the bone is not broken, be cautious if it is caused by a sharp object or similar things, and the skin is nonetheless torn and the wound is great, and you doubt slightly of an abscess forming.
si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	if it soon becomes healthier on its own, especially if the wound oozes little blood, and it heals on the contrary from the affected part.
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and patients should avoid drinking wine and eating fatty meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not want to heal, let his flesh be reduced, and he should not drink wine, nor eat meat.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and apply this to the wound; if an abscess forms and it comes out, then use cotton moistened only in rose oil or strict wine.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no hot abscess, then apply to the wound, if it is fresh and all its blood is not moved by air or powder, I will say a little later.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it moves again, after having applied any heating, as long as it is healthy.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like the size of a sword or similar, and the edges cannot come together, they should be brought together by stitching, as I will explain for wounds in the belly from the stitches.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope;	If the wound is exposed to the bone, and it bleeds heavily, but only for a short time, then he should apply pressure.
puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	then treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of leather, and instruct the patient to eat substantial meats, such as beef, cooked wheat, as well as poultry, and similar foods.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find putrefaction in the flesh or leather that does not reach the bone, apply pressure to stop the putrefaction and treat it.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped without cutting, and you cut it, even if it's only by a thread,
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere:	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the cure is light:
et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	and it is that you put this powder which hardens so that the fire consumes it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est:	And the method of the powder is thus:
pren encens une partie;	take a portion of incense
sanc de dragon II parties;	dragon's blood in two parts
chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	take living chalk in three parts, and grind it finely, and apply it to the wound, and form it tightly, until it disperses well and joins with all its blood.
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle;	and then bind it well, and leave it to loosen if it does not swell.
car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	because one should not remove medicine as long as it is healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never should one use charcoal only, unless you have frankincense or dragon's blood, but the fire must have moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	and if the wound has changed or moved, especially in an infected state, unless someone puts this powder on it;
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but apply no hot compresses or poultices made of ground barley flour with water and honey while it is still fresh.

de la plaie dou col	of the deep wound
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound occurs on the neck and it is simple, then it has no distinction from that in the head, but if there is damage to the nerves of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is the nerves, there is no other remedy but to let them heal, and do not put anything constrictive, for it harms the nerves and causes them to retract.

dou derrompement dou ventre	disruption of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The ruptures in the belly are great, medium, and small;

si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	if it cuts deeply into the flesh and does not deflect, then see the shape:

Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	When the wound is large and located in the lower abdomen, it is necessary that you make the patient lie on his back and elevate his legs higher than his head.

Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;	For small wounds, make them as if you are equipped, then take in your hands a gentle remedy that heals every break and closes the lips.
et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	and this is the common method of stitching: you should puncture a needle or more, according to the extent of the wound, then leave two spaces from the edge of the wound, and insert a needle where there is good strong thread.

puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	then tie the thread just as you did with the first needle, and do not stop doing this according to your need for needles, until all the wound is constrained.
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	and let the needles be of moderate size, between fine and thick, for the fine needles take all the blood, and the too thick ones cannot enter properly.

et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	and do not insert the needles too far beyond the depth of the flesh and dermis, as they will puncture and open the wound before healing.
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and then cut off the ends of the needles, so they do not irritate the patient when sleeping, and place a cloth or blanket over the ends of the needles to keep them still, and leave them until the wound is healed.
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	and this method of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds, as it requires only one or two needles.
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	The second stitch is common, and it is that you join the two parts of the skin and the two parts of the tissue together with a needle using one strong medium thread.
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	and when you have joined these four parts together, return the needle to the beginning part, and stitch in the same way that you sew clothes.
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and leave a space between each stitch, no thicker than the diameter of two needles.
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	This stitch opens the wound, and I sewed a wound that had a knife in the stomach, which was deeply cut, more than a palm wide, and it extended from the intestines two palms wide, and the wound was in the stomach.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned the intestine to its original position after it had been out for twenty-four hours, and the wound healed completely within fifteen days, and he was cured.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And they marveled that he was alive, and it was a miracle.
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not cure him with any treatment, as I was in a place where none could be found, neither any medicine.
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and apply a cold compress to the wound two times a day, and wash it with honey water until it is healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	Now, I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle, and hold it against the affected part from inside to outside;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	when it has pierced the center perfectly, if the tip is sharp or blunted or you have held the needle in a certain way, and it pierces from inside to outside again, do the same on the other side of the affected part.
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and the understanding of this stitch is that you sew as a tailor sews fur, and leave once the thread satisfied on one side, and take it up again on the other, until the stitch is entirely finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	The second way of stitching, which Galens calls the proper way, is as follows: just as some join the two parts together naturally, and apply one of the main threads to the other main thread in this manner.
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	take a needle or a thread of magic nearby, and pierce only one side, leaving the two threads of the stitch;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	then turn the needle and make it pierce from the furthest part towards the inside, until it reaches the affected area.
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then pierce both parts from the furthest towards the inside, in two other areas of the mirror-like surfaces on either side.
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the most effective method of stitching, and the most common one.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	These words are from a medieval medical text, and no one can testify to their truth—one must sew the belly with needle and thread.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and you should push one needle from one side, and the other from another, in the manner of those who sew corsets.
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, it is the most difficult stitch compared to other stitches in the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	and it is that when you discover the fresh wound filled with blood, and the flesh has moved, then press on the wound and the intestine, and stop the bleeding.
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	then apply the burning powder, and it will change the color, if you put on any dressing that is available, as long as the wound is open.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and take the thread, make it strong, and secure the healing, and the mirror.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat the wound as with others, as long as it is healed.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and if you have no medicine, then apply this, as soon as it begins to open again, cotton cloth, and move it two times a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you need no other medicine in various arrangements when the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and if you doubt that the wound affects the principal members, then it is necessary to apply a light bandage in warm olive oil or rose oil, and place it around the affected area, and under the armpits.
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	and if it causes pain or inflammation in the bowels, and this often happens, then they should enema with red wine, especially when the inflammation reaches the intestines.
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and pierce it from within, and know that when it is the large intestines, it is easier to heal than the small ones.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestinal organ, called "young" (or perhaps "innard"), cannot heal when it is wounded, and this is due to the frailty of its vessels, the subtlety of the entire body, and the similarity of its nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the cauterized wound jumps or moves, place it back as it was before, just like the intestine, while it is still fresh.
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	and if it becomes much and turns towards red or black, then you must hold the black part still, for there will be no further blood flow, as there are veins and arteries.
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	then cut away what is between the bones, and hang both parts from the outside of the wound until they fall off, to ease the extraction when the cauterized parts come out, and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	from the rupture of the bowels
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	When the intestine is torn and the wound is small, it can be restored in no man, for I have seen that a noble man was wounded in his belly by a lance.
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became infected and formed a fistula, and from there issued evacuation and flatulence.
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I applied treatment according to what I could, and did not cease to bandage subtily as long as it was healthy, and the wound healed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw him bound, I doubted that the patient would have pain in his stomach.
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and he did not have any pain, but rather improved conditions, foods, and drinks;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and they said no experiments should be done when there is a small wound in the intestine, it must be tied in such a way:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	take a large needle, then gather the edges of the wound, and when the needle has opened the mouth, place it between the two lips, so that it pulls the mouth together.
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	and then cut off the head of the shoulder, and this remains so that it cannot dislocate, then place another piece in its place in this manner as before, until the wound is completely healed.
et cout la plaie.	and examine the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	If the pain is sharp and penetrates into the intestines, and causes no harm to the patient, one can bind the intestines with a fine thread cut from the intestine of an animal in this manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	take the end of this thread from the intestine, which is well cleaned, and then bind it to the end of this fine linen thread twisted, then thread it onto a needle, sew up the intestine, and rearrange it in its original position.
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this method of stitching with stitches is not stronger than according to the path of purpose and hope.
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is great and wide, especially when it affects one of the vital organs, there is no treatment subtle enough.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula, whether it be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Every wound or abscess, when it becomes infected, is generally called a "fistula", especially when it is covered with pus and feels warm.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	And a fistula is according to the truth, hard and white, where no pain is felt, and it is also smooth like the feathers of a bird.
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and it never becomes clear at any time, or dense at other times;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	not at all times, and sometimes enough;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	and I have spoken of the division of wounds; that every wound which is not clean, and there is no fever, is only outside one of the nine causes.
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is to say, due to the smallness of blood or pus;
ou por sa malice;	or because of its evil nature;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is a hard fever inside, and on the lips, which does not allow anything to grow;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	for there is too much bowing;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	for their bones are brittle, and the material is of poor quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	for their medicines are not good for treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	for this is how corruption is a manner of pestilence;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	for the proprieties in the region are delayed digestion, and slow health, and oppressive by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	There are veins or bones here.
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already described all these causes, signs, and treatments of medications in the previous section.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is necessary that I tell you about the treatment of a fistula which is performed by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	You know that fistulas occur in all parts of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	because there are fistulas that affect large veins, arteries, and nerves, as well as the bladder, intestines, or kidneys, or any of the ribs, or the spine in the back, or any joint in the hands or feet.
