et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it occurs at a point that belongs to the main member, and has similar joints.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas of this nature are difficult to heal, and there is no remedy but labor and ignorance.
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if there is no fistula that does not come to the place I mentioned, and you have faith in the remedy, and you see it take effect, take a piece of iron or steel, if the fistula is deep, then press it.
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	and if the fistula is crooked, try to insert a thin piece of something flexible, for the bend will conform to the curvature.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	and if it is a fistula, wide open and you cannot examine it properly with your fingers, then close it by inserting a plug in one of the openings, for moisture flows from one opening to another and purifies it.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	then grasp it firmly with your power, so that you know if there are bones or nerves, and pull it out completely, and ask the patient in pain where they feel the pain when you press your hand, and the place where they feel it.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and when you truly know the place where it is, and whether it is far from a joint or nerve or artery or vein, or in none of the places I told you, then cut it according to what I told you, and remove the disorder and the corrupted flesh within.
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	and then the cure as long as it is clean, and if the fistula is deeply located in the right place, it is necessary that you remove it completely, as much as you can, then apply wet compresses with a medicinal herb, and keep them on top of the fistula until the medicine corrodes the excess that remains at the bottom.
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then apply warm compresses with healthy garlic, as long as it is clean;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if it is not clean through this method, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, remove it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or nerve does not affect your principal limbs, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and blackening, remove it as soon as possible, then cure the wounded area thoroughly until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	and if it is not healed, and the bone still curves as before, know that you are not yet allowed to proceed.
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	if it becomes exposed and you want to proceed deeply, remove all the corruption, then reset the bone to its original position.
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus healed, so much the better.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If that is not the case, know that the corruption is too extensive that you cannot overcome it;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other force but to leave it to nature;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there is a small corrupted bone, and you can extract it with tweezers, using an appropriate instrument, and if there are many bones, they should be extracted carefully, leaving none behind.
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	and if moisture makes it worse, there is no doubt or fear, for warmth and moisture, and freeing the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	And if you cannot remove them for an hour, then apply something to the wound that promotes putrefaction, and leave it until the bones are rotted around them, and then they will become lighter.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	and if it is a large bone, like the leg or thigh, then apply so much pressure to the putrefaction until all blackness is removed from the bone, and then dress the wound.
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a great amount of corruption within the heart, it extends almost to the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	if it is necessary, cover and protect everything up to the point of corruption, then heal as long as it remains sealed;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	and I will tell you about a fistula that occurs in a person's leg, so that you can take an example from it and receive help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	It was a young man around 30 years old who had pain in his leg due to something within the body that caused materials to reach the leg, resulting in a large abscess that could not be opened.
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	but because of their madness, they pricked too deeply into the abscesses, and burned many things, and it became a fistula, and there were many openings through which blood and moisture left the body.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and many others had no cure for over two years, and there was no wise man in the art of healing, until I was called to it, and I saw his leg and the remedies with which he was cured, and what was corrupted through the openings in the body.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the skin of the young man became red, and had the color of a citron.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I set up a tent in one of these openings, and then I examined all the openings, and found that some came against each other from every part of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	I quickly prepared a tool, and inserted it into one of the openings until I discovered a piece of bone, which I found corrupted and pierced, and the corruption extended all the way to the bone.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I realized what I was seeing with the corrupted bone, and believed that there was no other corruption except for the one I had left.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and I began to treat the wound with strong medications for a long time, but it could not heal.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and then I began to recognize and discover the bone as I have mentioned before, and found the corruption continuing in the bone, and treated it, and then tied it, and focused on fusing the joint.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	but I could not until I had completely wrapped the bone in cloth, then treated it with all kinds of medicine.
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and it became healthy and the joint was healed firmly, and it did not want to repeat the operation again unless because of the weakness of the patient who could not bear it, and for the fear of death that I had of him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For in the evacuation of blood, it often happens completely, and a hard callus is formed in its place on the bone, which is well arranged and causes no harm or damage to anything at all, neither coming nor going.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if a bone is broken in any part of the body, it must be treated in this way:
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	take hold of the ligaments, and strain the end of the bone that is opened, and command anyone to extend it upwards;
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and attach another stronger thread to the first one, and bind it onto the part where the bone is separated, extending the end, so that you pull the corrupt flesh away from the bone, and uncover the flesh on the place where you want to treat it, so that the bone is not damaged.
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and place I a table beneath the bone to keep the flesh from moving;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	it is important to examine it carefully as one can see and smell the corruption, and sometimes in another way.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	and if the bone is corrupted and will not open, and the corruption is in one place or another, it exposes the flesh completely.
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	then place I a table beneath, and then gently move from one part to another the corruption, and be sure that the pressure is just long enough on the corruption as we have said.
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, cut out the corrupted joint, and the bone it contains from the other side.
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the continuity of two joints, cut out the affected part if there is no other option.
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	and if the corruption is in the wrist of the hand or the ankle of the foot, and it is very strong, nonetheless you must inquire about that corruption how it opens.
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and purify it in every way that you can, but ensure the vein or nerve does not oppose your actions.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and knows that the saw and the threads to cover these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and thinness, and their size and smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and for this, it is necessary to match each type of operation with its appropriate instrument;
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and knows that the work will show you the instrument of which you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the manners of diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	if you think of the instrument you need according to what is appropriate.
dou feu	with fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The joints may become dislocated either internally or externally;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	and when you have treated that corruption with medicinal cures but they are of no avail, it is necessary to immobilize that member until the corruption disappears, so that the patient may be saved from death or from the greater evil of a defective limb.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	and the signs of this are that the limb turns black, as if it were burned by fire, and then the corruption spreads from member to member, taking over the entire body.
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	If you hastily cover it, and if it's due to the penetration of some venomous creatures, such as a sea scorpion or snake, and the corruption is at the top of the two, if you hit it, and do not give it any space to come up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes up to the hand, if you hit the joint, so that the corruption does not come up to the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	and if it comes up to the arm, if you hit the shoulder.
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and if it passes through the cut, it is death, and there is no remedy outside of the quantity of its virtue.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	and do the same when corrosion or rust occurs.
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	if it occurs on the first joint, then chop after the other joint.
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it occurs deeply, chop all of it.
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it ascends the leg, chop at the knee joint.
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, there is no other cause but to bring the patient to death.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and the method of binding or wrapping the member: if you fasten it above and below, extend one minister from the lower link, and another minister from the upper link, and release the band that is between the two links with a wide spatula, until the bone is exposed.
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	then bind or wrap it, and place each drape of linen on either side so that the lint does not touch the healthy flesh, bringing about further injury and abscess to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	And if the occurrence of blood comes when you open, if you cauterize the wound too harshly or place any restrictive powders on it;
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then return to your treatment as long as it is complete, then bind the afflicted member with a strong ligament, and heal it until it is sane.
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	and I will tell you if it happens at home as if it were a dream:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	it had a blackness that seemed burnt from fire, and that corruption first appeared on its second toe, spreading over the entire foot.
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the bone feels the heat, it hardens itself against the pain, and becomes healthy.
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and after a long time, the pain returns or the bone feels weak in the hand, and it comes to me, and I place it on things that resonate after the purification of the body, but it cannot stop the pains.
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and it made me grasp the hand, but I did not want to hurt the matter.
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	and I also doubted that if he cut off his hand, he would not die, for the strength of man was weak.
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he becomes desperate, returns to his land, and covers his hand, and is healed.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have no objection to this, unless it is done differently, as needed.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Abscesses never occur in fat tissue, and they stay for so long that they cause a great gathering of bowels.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then they rot and pierce, breaking the bowels and remaining in the body like a vassal.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and the skin that is above is as delicate as fine cloth, and does not cut to the bone or nerve, and such a condition is called 'healthy', and is not called 'fistula'.
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so extended that it reaches the bone in its progression, then it is called 'fistula'.
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the skin is such that you must cut through it completely, especially when it is delicate, just as if it were fine cloth.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and does not cease because of its putrefaction.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And if you think that the skin is rotting but the putrefaction is not yet complete and the skin becomes very hard, treat it with a cleansing enema as follows:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	check if the swelling is large and the bowels emitting a bad odor, then use an enema with Egyptian medicine prepared as follows:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	take as much honey, oil, and litharge, equally, and cook it in a vessel over fire until the medicine turns red and becomes as thick as honey.
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and then take according to your need, and make it with water and honey, and enema the breast, and tighten the opening.
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	leave the medicine on for two hours, then extract it while squeezing.
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this several times, until the breast is healed and the pain is gone.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	and never enema with water and ashes when this medicine is not present, but you press ashes from the bark of a vine tree, pour water over them, then strain it and use it for an enema, until you know that the breast is fully healed.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	and if the patient cannot endure it, neither Egyptian medicine nor water from ashes can help, if he is enemas with water and honey, or has a little litharge ground in it.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	or you give him an enema of honey and sweetened wine, since honey has purifying properties and washes away impurities, and the wine makes the body air and healthy.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and once you have done this and are confident that the seeds are well purified, give him an enema with what causes a certain pain in it, and press on with cauterization, and apply it with rosin oil and wine.
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	You should administer some medications and remedies to it, of which I have spoken about their properties in treating wounds.
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	and if the wound in the side is small and the cannula of the clister cannot enter, enlarge it a little with a hot iron and insert a plug of Egyptian or basilicon poultice, as long as it is enlarged.
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the wound is too wide, so much that it causes a great suffering to the patient or prevents the cannula or clister from entering, and if the opening that leaks is above or below the level of the wound.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the bowel is completely healthy, it does not allow anything to ferment inside.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	and if you cannot cover the stomach as you see fit, arrange it in such a way that the bowel reaches its lowest position, for when the bowel is completely healthy, it does not allow anything to ferment inside, and if you cannot cover the stomach as you see appropriate, arrange it accordingly.
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	so that the bowel moves slightly downwards, and does not leave any part of the bowel behind.
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	and take consolidant medications to put on the wound, and apply them under the linen cloth that covers all the wound.
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	then cut with force around the hole in the side of the chest, making it larger than the first one, and apply gentle dressing on another cloth according to the size of the hole, and place it over the wound in the chest to align the muscles, and do not remove the large initial cloth until after several days.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and the one who is over the chest wound often removes it to release pressure on the muscles, and knows that whatever comes from the muscles, whether it's poison or blood or not enough, or digestion or indigestion.
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or no, and when the medicine has extended in this way and you see the nature that springs from the wound, then know that healing has already begun, and approach health.
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	and then untie it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you unbind the wound, change to another bandage, and renew the dressing.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast feels bowed and indigest after many days, knowing that it will not open.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons manifest after a long time, do not despair of your health, for health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For there are people who tardily begin to care for their wounds, and others who do the opposite.
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if the patient has an indigestive stomach ache for many days, knowing that the pain does not subside.
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	and if the pain persists for a long time, then use remedies that are moist in substance and dry in virtue, as a final treatment, since there is a great part of vitriol in them, which is the last medicine.
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take the final treatment, and make it with rose oil, and mix it with old wine of equal substance;
puis le confit et en use;	then bind it and use it;
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	and itself makes the honey thick and rich, when garlic is not present, take myrrh and aloe and incense, and grind it, and sprinkle it over the honey while it's still warm from the fire;
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and then I wrap it, and extend it over the breast, and never administer aromatics or long roots of celestial herbs, which is also like flour of grain and lint;
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	and use of simples or compounds;
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	Break them, and make a powder, and add the honey I mentioned, and use it;
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	and if the cure is prolonged, and this cure does not heal it, then know that the corruption is deep, and it leaves an impression on the bone, or makes the members hard, or the limbs stiff.
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the cure for the fistula, as we have said above.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	from the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	A pustule is an abscess that forms under the nail of the hand, or foot, or occasionally in other areas.
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and when they become old and care is not taken, if an abscess forms, they run and throw themselves down until the root of the nail runs out, and perhaps they will cut it off entirely.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and the inflammation comes right up to the bone, causing such intense pain that it smells bad, and the swelling becomes very large, and the color turns red.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When treating it as we have described in the previous section, if the treatment is not effective, then you must remove all the dead tissue from around the nail, and after that, cauterize the wound.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	Cautery is very helpful if the bone is healthy and the nail is uninfected.
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and if the nail becomes infected and begins to hurt, and a blister forms, you must insert a knife under the nail that is causing the pain, and lift it up, and then cut the infected part gently and slowly, and apply hot and corrosive medications to remove everything.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then attend to the treatment of wounds as long as they are clean.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corruption is in the bone, cut it off and remove it, for as soon as the bone decays, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if you see both bones corrupted, cut them off as mentioned above, then treat them while they are clean.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is injured, swollen, and causes great pain, then you must first heal it.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	then cut the nail with a sharp instrument diagonally from above, and be sure that the cut does not go all the way to the quick of the nail, as the patient would feel too much pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, apply something that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain so sharp and intense strikes the hand.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	He who is born into the hands of no one, perhaps quite fleshy, and by chance has a part with bones, but never a nail, and none are born in the root of the joint, where birth is against nature.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	He who is born without any new pain should not be mute, and he who is born with a joint pain may remain mute.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the cut on the fat person should be light, in this way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Cut it at its root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	He who is born at the root of the joint is difficult to cure:
si te tien dou coper.	if it holds you down tightly.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In those who are born with or develop a deformity, it is necessary that you first hold the round shape of the joint firmly towards the bone, then dislocate the bone to a suitable position, and finally cure it as long as it is healthy.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The deformities that come together in a joint may be due to birth, or the healing of a wound, or burns from fire, or similar conditions.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	You must ensure that you heal the tightly closed one according to its natural forms.
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then place between two moistened oil-soaked cloths so that they do not adhere.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	You should insert between two thin pieces of cloth, as long as the wound is closed, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If dislocation occurs in any of its fingers with the palm, secure that joint as appropriate.
des vils	venoms
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Their veins are thickly wrapped, filled with melancholic excesses that affect various parts of the body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	And it is more pronounced in the legs of those who walk, work, and carry things, compared to others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is necessary for you to administer purgative once and then cleanse the bowels.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	The treatment for this is according to two manners:
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	One is with a knife, and they scrape out the black blood.
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other method is that you open the vein, and scrape it out completely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The size is according to this manner:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	first, the leg with the hot water becomes very strong, so that the flesh remains tender, then stretch the sick leg from above the ankle to the part below the knee.
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then open the vein in its place, either in I or II or III, with a wide cut, then gently and carefully squeeze out the black blood with your hand, from one end to the other, as much as the patient's strength allows;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then apply it, and command him to eat foods that produce dark, black urine;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and resume the evacuation and cleansing when the veins are full, and harmful to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	The remedies for this are as follows:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	Lift the leg of the ailing patient, if there is hair on it, then immerse it in hot water and raise the leg with hot water until it turns red and the veins swell.
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you have no bath, then warm it over fire, and then apply it to the vein with long heat at the top of the knee or in the area below the ankle.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then open the skin at the joint, and scrape the vein from each side until it appears as if one can feel it.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and it appears red and black, and when it enters or pierces the skin, it seems like a white cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	then pull the right of the socket, as long as it is lifted from the skin, and then bend it slightly to the oncine, then cut across in another place on the other side above the third joint.
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then strip the skin from the vein while it is open, then lift the flesh slightly, as you did before, and bend it to another oncine, as you did first.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	then take another size, or as many as you need, then gently, and cut it with the right foot, then treat and move it until it reaches the second size.
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then extract it gradually, as it becomes stronger, then cut it.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and if you cannot pull and lift it, take a needle with a very strong thread, tie it, pull and move it from side to side until it comes out.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and be careful that it does not cut, for if it cuts, you cannot pull or lift it, and it brings harm to the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	and when you have finished treating it, immediately place a warm compress of wine and rose oil on the moistened wound.
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	And if the vision is contracted, twisted, and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must split it in an unconventional way but do not cover it.
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	and treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The form does not allow for extracting the eye if it is stuck, without cutting the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and it is very difficult, because if it were delicate, it would cut the vein, but since it is thick as we have said, this is its form:
de la voinne civile	of the natural vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is located in the legs, in warm regions where no plants or trees grow, and on land that is not moist.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	and by chance it may appear in other places than the legs, and this results from a putridity that arises from beneath the skin, as if it comes from within the body, winding and writhing, nestled between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein appear, it is that there is a very great inflammation in the leg, then the color changes, and the vein begins to emerge forcefully, just like a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the joint is open, you should wrap it tightly with a piece of cloth from one and a half to two fingers wide, and compress it, leaving the cloth on the leg, and every time there is no movement, you should rewrap the cloth around the affected area.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, cut off a part of it and wrap the remaining portion, but do not cover its root until all the blood has stopped flowing.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	because if you cut it, it will return to the root, causing an abscess and putrefaction or gangrene there, leading to a severe illness.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	For every small thing, it is necessary to treat it quickly and carefully from its root, leaving nothing in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	and there is no time when this vein should be treated with anything other than the palm of your hand, or with a needle, and often a patient comes to me whose vein is as long as ten palms, and when you cut it, if it bursts open or closes up, and pierces through to the bottom, then everything flows out.
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	and it should be emptied of the matter that is inside, and then apply medicated poultices for several days, and then treat it as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	And never should this vein be cut again, especially when it opens at the ankle or knee joint, and much injury occurs, and from which it bleeds a lot.
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	Treat it as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	vers that are born between skin and bone.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This illness is called the "beef disease" in our land because it often affects cows, and it is a small worm that appears between the skin and muscle, spreading throughout the body, ascending and descending, and causing great pain from limb to limb, until the skin is broken where it has spread.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and it is caused by putrefaction of some humours, as they come and wind and worms and parasites in the belly.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	and doubt arises about the nature of his illness, for when it spreads throughout the body, it ascends to the head, and reaches the brain, perhaps returning and destroying the brain.
et ceu avient maintes fois.	and this often happens.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it healing and draining, it cannot be done again until it has passed.
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	If it is necessary, then you must place the limb firmly and tightly above and below with a strong bond, then cut and pull it until it moves freely in the socket, and if you cauterize it with fire, let it heal.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm it does is when it bleeds, as we have said.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming close to the wound, tighten the muscle below forming a bump, then cut and pull.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and it is necessary for the patient to purify his body with solvent medicines to remove harmful humors, and to eat foods that prevent putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from flatulence
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This disease is called "vakerir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes in no particular member, but can move from one member to another.
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and I have shown what I told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to see a sick woman, and I examined her arm, and noticed a small swelling in the vein of the arm.
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	and then I saw, the spirit rising in the shoulder, more so than anything else, as bright as living silver when it cuts through flesh to another.
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	the pain departs from the affected limb and fixes itself in the shoulder, then after a short while, it spreads throughout the body, until it reaches the other breast.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then it told me that it returned again around the body, as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled much at how it moved from one limb to another, for I had never seen this disease in such a way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	Nevertheless, I wanted to know why the pain moved from one place to another, but I did not understand it, as I saw it in the woman.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and I thought it was because the woman had dry skin, her veins were exposed, and this constraint of breath was apparent.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and did not appear according to this reason to those who are delighted, and have moist skin and veins covered.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	And when you see this illness healed, and the patient feels this pain, if it opens as we have said, press it from above and below vigorously, and then continue until this constrained breath at the place leaves.
et cauterize le leu;	and cauterize the place;
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	and if you do not see it to your own, if the treatment of these winds, like foul pills, and pills of serpentary, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows vary, according to their appearance and the parts of the body they pierce.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	Their diversity is such that there are those with great points, and small, and curved, and solid;
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and those with sharp angles, and some with tongues, and others where there are pieces;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	and those that break in any limb break in two ways:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or in the main limb, as the head, body, liver, kidney, bowels, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it breaks in any part of these members, then the signs of death that I will tell you below will appear:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	you must be wary of extracting this arrow, as death comes after in various ways;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when this evil sign does not appear at all, and the arrow is not entirely extracted, if you pull it, treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And the sign of the brain when the arrow breaks and pierces the bone, and swelling appears on the head, it is a sign of concussion and stupor and drowsiness and red eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	and perhaps it is without feeling in the nostrils or ears;
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and by chance he loses his speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and there springs from the moist wound a white discharge resembling pus, and also as if from a bruise of a horse;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if this sign appears, if you hold to the cure, and pull the arrow if it is not fully out.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it breaks or withdraws is that it is near the left breast and feels as if it were stuck in hard, non-empty matter.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and by chance, he may become mute as if he were a bird, and there appears black blood, and coldness and cold sweat, and fainting:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	so he knows with certainty that death descends.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow that the patient never sweats is that no foam comes from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's face turns pale, and he breathes heavily and stops moving.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the arrow comes out under the skin, it is necessary to clean the small costs;
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	and it gives great pain and causes great sorrow and sighing;
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	and it moves all the members of the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if an arrow pierces through the stomach, perhaps something from the undigested meat will jump out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow pierces through the belly, and there is no sign of healing through the intestines, then there is little hope for a cure, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if an arrow pierces the bladder, the urine jumps and flows out, and the patient feels great pain.
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	you know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, as they are formed and their joints and neck and shoulder and helper (muscles) and the sharp pain in the back and the forceful and stiffening (of muscles), and the foot and legs, and the appearance of the limb, differ according to various dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or an artery and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, because you must do the same.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a man that an arrow struck him or pierced his side.
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it, and I pulled from the other side under the ear's fat, and it healed without scar.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And take a needle in hand, insert it into the fat under the paper skin, and the needle is withdrawn with only its point towards the wood, and the needle is large as an arrowhead, very light without ears.
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	it became healthy, and no bad accidents befall it.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And take a needle from the throat to a Christian, and it is an Arabic needle with ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I opened the jaws, and as I gently withdrew it, the Christian became healthy.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And take an arrow from the body, which was stuck in its stomach, and thought it was dying.
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then it passed XXX days, and its condition did not improve;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut the arrow, and opened it up, and pulled it out, and there was no bad outcome.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see a person with an arrow stuck in their back, and the wound is deep;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and hold the arrow within it, and do not change its natural positions, nor find harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And see another man, to whom an arrow has fallen into his face, and the wound was deeply seated;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	and held it thus without suffering great pain;
et mout d’autres semblans.	and many others of similar kind.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And pulled out an arrow from the body of a prince, the king, which had been struck in the neck and was slightly inclined to the right side;
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and it was the arrow completely withdrawn.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called to treat her after she had been bedridden for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I probed her with utmost care, and found no sensation.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and she felt sharp pain and discomfort behind her right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was from the arrow's point. I applied a soothing poultice to the wound, as the swelling had not subsided.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I saw the arrowhead appear.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I applied the hot hand to it for several days, and then sutured the wound accordingly, holding the patient for a long time until he felt the arrow inside his flesh.
et il le me dist.	and it came out.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I applied strong, corrosive medication to the wound for several days until it opened up, and after testing it, I felt the tip of the arrow still stuck in the flesh.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then adjust the opening of the wound with this medicine until the head of the arrow becomes visibly apparent.
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and after three months, the wound healing process should be well underway, and then it widens, so I inserted pincers, pulling from both sides, but it cannot heal.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	so I did not cease to try and invent new tools, until I found a set of well-made pincers, according to the shape that would be described at the end of this chapter, as I continued to pull and turn the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the greatest experts believe that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored.
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I then restored it, and the wound healed, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	Or, I have told you about the quality of extracting arrows, so that you place your cure on what I do not mention, for books cannot encompass everything.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	but the most skilled physicians consider even the smallest thing and what is present and lacking, a true new work, and new tools, at the decline of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that arrows do not leave the limbs where they are embedded, but in two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or through the place where they enter, or from another side;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which comes out from the other side where it enters, is an arrow entering into flesh, and never comes out again.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not come out now, leave it until the flesh around it decays, and then free the issue.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and also if it is stuck in the bone, it cannot come out, unless left like that for several days, and moves each day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it jumps, and if it does not jump, it pierces around everywhere inside, narrowing the joints around until they are wide enough, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if an arrow is stuck in the bone at the head, reaching down to one of the belly cavities near the brain, and none of the symptoms I have mentioned affect the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If it cannot be pulled out, but left as long as it remains even after several days, for if the arrow goes all the way through, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is embedded only in the bone and does not come out satisfactorily, it leaves the patient no rest for days without further harm, if the skill of pulling it out is lacking.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot be pulled out, then apply herbs around it as I have told you.
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the limb as long as it is healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is embedded deeply in the body and cannot be seen, then try to extract it with all your might.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, use a suitable instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and if you cannot reach the wound due to its depth or the arrow's position, and there is no bone, nerve, or vein to be seen, then cauterize it until the wound heals.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and extract the arrow if you can, and if it has barbs that hold it in place, carefully remove the charred part from both sides as much as you can, then break or bend the barbs of the arrow until you can pull it out.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and gently, without breaking the arrow, draw it out more forcefully.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, so that the limb is entirely relaxed around the joint, then continue to treat it, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the bloodletting causes adverse effects, then apply the treatments as described in that chapter.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	and beware of cutting into nerves and veins, and use any means you can to draw out the arrow safely, either quickly or slowly, firmly or gently.
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	and place the patient as he was when the arrow entered, for that is the greatest aid, and if you cannot do it, then follow the signs shown to you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another direction, where it opens something within, or the skin is swollen in a noticeable way:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	then cut it, as the pliers can grip it, and then extract it:
si saut fuer maintenant.	if it jumps now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	If it is stuck in the bone, turn your hand round, until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then extract it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, leave it for now and then try to extract it again until it comes out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the arrowhead is in the flesh, it presses against the entire flesh.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	and if the arrowhead is extracted, you must apply pressure, if you administer an instrument, ensure that the tip of the arrowhead enters the channel of the instrument.
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and then press firmly, and if the arrowhead is embedded, insert an instrument with a pointed end to facilitate extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is embedded, it is necessary that you clean all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, and then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrowhead has come out in the stomach, or bladder, or ribcage, and it is accessible, then you may cover it;
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and guard to not cover the vein and nerve, then extract it, and then stitch the wound, it is a skill.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and the treatment as long as it is healthy.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The instrument used to extract arrows resembles a bird's beak; here is its shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	And there are many ways:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	great, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead is like a feather, to point the tip of the arrow, just as if it were the form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of pincers, to pierce and hold if it is thus:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	There are 31 veins from which one derives health, of which there are 16 principal ones, namely:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	II beatens that are after the ears, which are called the soft "herbesh";
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	and the two arteries that are in the temples, appearing;
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and the veins that are in the arms of the limbs, called "aspires";
et li voine que est emmi le front;	and the vein that is on the forehead;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is on the head, near the eyes;
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two glands which are at the collarbone;
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are on the upper lip near the mouth, and these veins are called "augeherich".
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the two veins that are below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The veins that one commonly knows are 'V' shaped in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic vein, which is on the left side of the body, and people commonly call it 'vein of the head'.
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	and the middle part is called "fast" (tight), and it is composed of the head and body parts, and common people call it "vein of the heart".
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and the basilic is on the right side, and common people call it "vein of the belly", and it is beneath the skin, and it is the one that heals, which opens clearly on the wrist.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the saving vein is the one between the little finger and the ring finger, and if it rains (i.e., swells).
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	and in the leg and where the foot has three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	one is detached from the ribcage on the left side of the body, and the second is at the ankle on the right side.
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the vein called "nesse", which is in the ankle of the other side.
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg, there are three veins detached from those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The healthy purification of veins located after the ears is beneficial for old catarrh and migraine.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	and the qualities of the healthy substance, as I have said, and it is that you apply the head of the patient, and rub the affected area or veins with a rough cloth.
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	then tie the patient's collar with a string, so that both veins behind the ears, dependent from the head, become visible.
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	place your two fingers there, and where you feel the pulse under your thumb, it is certain.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	then take the lancet, and cut through the vein just beneath the bone, then gently place your hand over the entire vein upstream, and press and hold the skin and the vein well, so that blood can flow out as you see.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then stretch and hold it, as long as it remains healthy;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already spoken of incision and cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	The health of the two arteries in the temple, which is worth an old and steady migraine, and a habit of sudden blindness, and the heat of acute tears in the eyes.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the quality of a good healer is such as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is that the patient holds his breath, as long as both veins are widely open;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feel the intense pain from both sides, and then seal with a bandage.
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	then gently apply pressure on the vein at the top of your thumb index, insert the lance from below, and draw out the blood, first from the vein above and then the sap, just as you did with the other veins, allowing the blood to flow according to your need.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then free the patient, and place your finger on the vein for an hour, then apply cotton.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	and then the wound forms, and leave it until it is healthy;
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and we have spoken much of their treatment and extraction, as the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The healing of the vein on the forehead is just as valuable as the healing of the skull in ancient facial diseases, and for migraine and redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and its quality is such that the patient tightens their neck by twisting, until a vein opens.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument called "fosseur", which has this form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	and place the tip on the vein, and press with your hand or another object, allowing blood to escape according to the quantity you see.
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then gently release the patient's neck and tie the vein until it is healed and never open a wide wound with a flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	Nevertheless, one must not let the flames be too fierce;
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	and do not let the healthy part be crossed, for the bone is hard, and perhaps break the flames when they are subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The health of the two veins that are in the arms is especially helpful for abscesses, and for itching, and redness, and inflammation in the eye, and facial diseases;
