et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of their health is such that the patient feels no pain from any twisting of the veins, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then bring the healthy flesh, and make it heal across, slightly narrow than the length of the flame, for there is no need for excess.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	and if the flames are subtle, they might break.
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	then make the blood flow, as much as needed, and then tie it up on cotton, securing it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	The flesh around the nose is most valuable for healing quickly, and for severe wounds, and for facial diseases, such as migraines and redness that appears on the face, especially when it's old.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	and the quality of the wound is such that the patient squeezes his throat, then pulls his nose towards your left hand, and takes the thin flame with long tips, and inserts it between the space of the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well enough, and blood will now begin to flow.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not be too hasty in its application, and let the blood flow according to your need, then bind it for a night, for it is often quickly restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The holy water of the two eyes helps in the narrowing of the pupil, and at the onset of illness, and in many diseases, and in ulceration, and corrosion, and herpes, and swellings.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of the water is such that the patient draws their breath from both within and without, as we have said.
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	and if the master is standing over the patient's head, and the patient sits in a certain place, then open the vein with a long and slightly wide cut, then treat the blood with warmth as much as necessary.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	then repeat the process on the other vein, then loosen the ligature, and tighten the veins gently so the patient is not strangled.
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	and leave it until morning so the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	from the health of the veins
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The health of the veins in the mouth helps to prevent colds, and the corruption of gums, splits in the lips, and pain and swelling.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the healing is such that you should have the patient sit before you, and tighten their collar as I have said.
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	then turn the patient's face, and look at both veins, one on the right side of the mouth and the other on the left, and you can recognize them by their black color and the small, black lines around them.
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	So deal with each separately, and if you do not know them and are in doubt, take the largest one from each part, and also make the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	From the cleansing of the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The treatment of the veins below the tongue is most helpful after treating the neck, and it is for conditions of the throat, eye, and mouth.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	And the quality of the treatment is such that if the patient feels a sharp pain in your hands under the sun, lift their tongue and look below each side for a black vein.
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Then heal both of them, but do not cut too deeply, for they are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins through which blood flows, which are commonly healed, are treated according to two methods:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or cutting through all the inflamed tissue with either a broad knife or a thin blade, as you would cut through flesh, and it is called "anezyl".
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and they are broad and thin according to the width and constriction of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the fevered area turns red and is very renowned, and it is large as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary to open the veins with a sharp knife on the smooth, broad sides where there is much blood visible, which contains much blood and pus.
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the form of olive oil flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more delicately pointed, and is for healing the delicate veins where there is subtle citrus-colored blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The vein from the basil (one of these veins) is very helpful for illnesses that are beneath the throat, and the collarbone, and the chest, and the stomach.
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is necessary for the doctor to draw blood wisely and wash away the vein that lies beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if it affects the artery, and bleeding occurs, it must be stopped, as I have said.
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and the flame must not be pricked, but cut as if with a gentle tool.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the vein does not open clearly, it is necessary that you extract it and change to another one.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	or if you want none of this, you heal it above the vein in the arm.
elle apert manifestement;	she opens clearly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and apply the flame gently, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you recognize the place of the wound, it is necessary that you extract the arm, touching the place until you feel the pulse.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the place with a sign, and then tie the arm, and apply the flame gently.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	and be sure not to injure the artery when you see the bone enter (the joint), for it is the artery.
eschui la donques.	then avoid it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it protrude at the top as well, like the urine of a child, and the skin is red and tender, know that it is an artery.
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	then act quickly, and place your finger on it for a long time, then remove your finger if the skin becomes numb, which often happens.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	he lies with his arm relaxed, leaving it thus, and does not move the patient;
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	and he should be afraid, and does not move until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	And if the wound is not healed, it will worsen, and no remedy is present, especially if an artery opens, as with the root of the problem.
et estainche li sans.	and heal the wound.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a piece of fig bark, and cut it, and take one half of it and bind it tightly to the other side;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	if it does not become numb, that is good;
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if it does not, apply as we have said, powders that numb the blood;
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the numbing should not be too strong in various preparations due to the small size of the wound and the power of the limb.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The surgeon of the vein should clean it with care so that he treats the blood from the top and bottom of the wound, for it is composed of the basilic and cephalic veins as we have said.
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and the surgeon should wash for the nerve that is exposed, and if he does not cut it thoroughly, he may damage the nerve, causing swelling and infection, and perhaps it cannot heal.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any place due to its subtlety, then you should use a gentle instrument to heal it.
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and avoid using your strength.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if a vein is between the two bones, it makes it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The healer of the head should draw out the blood from the head and aid the joints.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is necessary for the healer to prick with olive or myrtle flame, for it is the safest of all veins, as it does not damage any nerve or artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, it is necessary to seek the lightest limb, and do not be grieved if it hurts the first time, and repeat.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and by chance the swelling may appear on any man, as it does the first time, but it causes no pain.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the wound healing depends on your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing you must know about healing is that health care is not merely a cure for illness, but also a means of preserving health and preventing future diseases.
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	and let the health be established in one of the three veins, namely:
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	that is to say, the cephalic, the femoral, and the basilic;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one should heal in the beginning of prayers at dawn, and in autumn and winter afterward, when the sign of fullness appears.
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	and one should heal the first day or the third, after two or three hours of the second day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The healer who is assigned to diseases has no set hour, but whenever it is needed, at any time of day or night.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and it is not advisable to heal children under twelve or women who have not been pregnant for less than seven months.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	One should not treat the old who have passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when anyone wishes to be healed, in any way, it is necessary that he cleanses the bowels with a light enema if they have retained much feces, so that the veins do not attract the excess waste from the intestines, harmful to the main members.
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	One cannot heal himself who is too soaked in the juices of meat, or who has excessive or weak humors.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and he should wash himself after colic, vomiting, abdominal distension, frequent defecation, multiple pregnancies, childbirth, watching and fasting, and this due to the weakness or condition of either the weapon or the body.
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then gently draw out the humours, if they are thick, through food and drinks and medicine, if you have such means.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	then enter the bath, if nothing prevents it, to draw out the blood, and cleanse the vein deeply from within and around it, as we have said.
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and guard yourself from work, and worry, and lust, and similar things that day.
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	and be calm and joyful, and make the healing better than that of others, and rub the arm twice or three times, then gently squeeze the ligament from above, for if it is too tight or loose, it will not heal well.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub the limb with both hands until the veins swell and feel hot.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	then moisten the wound with a little bit of old oil, then place your left-hand finger on the vein below the limb where you want to heal, so that the vein does not open and cause harm.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	For there are veins that flow like strings when healing, and if they are filled with pus, so much that when the fire is applied, it withdraws from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus one suffers from this condition.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if it opens a vein, if the wound is too tight, then it is necessary that the healers be aware of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if the vein opens for the first time, that is good.
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	if not, it is necessary to repeat this a little further down the affected limb, otherwise the limbs will not heal.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the limb is swollen, and the patient is frightened, let it be for one or two days, and do not tie up the arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	Perhaps there come abscesses suddenly.
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	He should not bathe immediately, then renew the dressing if it seems suitable.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if it is a small opening, pierce gently and doubt not that there will be little blood as you see, pressing firmly on the same piercing to draw out all the heat.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	and open it slightly gently, so that the joints may be inflamed.
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	Because this often happens, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the vein swollen, do not immediately reopen the wound, but apply a little oil, because it lightens the body of blood, and the sticky substance that is attached to this vein is dissolved by the oil.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer the oil in each wound that you heal the veins, to stop the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	and it also acts as a cure and draws out the evil, when it is applied to the vein;
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	if subtly the bone moves and separates when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if there develops a large abscess, which often happens, especially when the patient is not in good health and the opening of the vein is small, then hurry and place a moist sponge soaked in wine and silk on it, and hold it for an hour.
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary that you do this after the flow of blood from the vein stops, and if it remains in place for several days without any black or green discoloration, then it does not harm him.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see, place on anything cold or mirror, soaked in an ointment of calamine, show, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And often abscesses and swelling appear at the wound of the sanctuary.
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	then place your hand on it, and if you feel the place soft at the pressure of your hand, then this is the appearance of evil.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	So be careful not to put anything that we have said, for suddenly it might cut off the flow without an artery.
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	but he makes an embrocation of dry plaster to harden the joint, then applies other remedies until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each case of pain according to the quantity of its strength and the color of the pain.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	For if the skin is pale, let it continue to turn red.
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	and if you see it swelling, let it continue until it becomes subtle.
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is necessary for one who is bloated and strong, and requires the extraction of blood, to make a larger wound, with wider flames.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for those who are weak, do the opposite, and they should be treated healthier and more often, and it is best to heal them by cutting across, not piercing.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this method of healing is free from the corruption of blood and the loss of nerves, and it should be done in a way that extends from long to wide.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	and for those whose body requires healing, it is necessary to apply a moist dressing with pomegranate juice.
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	if it is overheated, then apply cold three or four times a day, and if it has a cold complexion, before the healing, moisten the wound with syrup made from fresh pomegranates, or honey syrup infused with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and anise, and a well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints during cleansing, after the release of much blood, it is necessary that he inhale a brew of charcoal and subtle fragrant syrup, and use other things as we have mentioned in the section or chapter on syncope for vein evacuation.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to straighten his arm and heal it later, if it is weakened by much blood loss, he should pull it little by little, according to the amount of its strength continues.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wants to straighten his arm after the first dressing and has a strong contraction, he should heal it seven hours after the first dressing, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to heal from another side, he should be healed on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	For there is much blood within the body, which is already heated, and it causes fever.
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	if it is necessary to draw out a large amount, and expand the wound as wide as possible, until it completely heals.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	then you should consider all the signs of healing, and place your hand on the pulse when it is whole, so that death does not come in its place, which often happens when the healer is negligent.
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it is not good when you see the arm dislocated and blood coming out again, and the wound is closed, that you press on it forcefully.
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	If he is bent, he should stretch the arm slowly, for it would be harmful.
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	but he should let it heal completely the second time;
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	or you should apply the tip of the flame to the frozen vein until it bursts, then immediately wrap it in cold water and gently press.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is inflated, leave it alone and do not squeeze it until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to drain blood a second time due to the abscess recurring in the same place or in another vein or arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is healthier in place of the vein from the head because it is composed differently.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the method of healing is that the patient should immerse their hand in hot water until the veins are red.
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then tie it gently, so that the vein opens well, then apply the medicine across, not too wide or too long.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and if the opening is wide, and the wound is close to the joint of the hand, and the pain prevents it from leaving, then immerse the hand in hot water and let the blood flow out into the water until enough has been drawn.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if this does not help, do not push the hand back into hot water, as more harm than good may result.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the health of this vein is safer than all other veins, as there are neither arteries nor nerves in it.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The health of the vein in the right hand is worth for all diseases of the liver, and this is the way:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	strain the hand, and immerse it in hot water, as long as the vein is inflamed, if you see that;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and hold the hand across, and if it hurts in any way at all, do not worry;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and do not hurt the patient too much, for the nerves are entirely exposed without any flesh, and then apply the hand to hot water again, so that the blood is frozen in the wound, and it cannot flow out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as best you can, then apply oil and string to seal the wound tightly, and do so for every person.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The healthy person holds the eye with their left hand to cure the disease of the mouse, and does everything as I have told you towards the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The healer of the soul holds itself to all diseases that afflict the body, such as illnesses of the heart, and retention of flowers (possibly referring to a condition related to flora or a metaphorical 'blooming' issue), and diseases of rain (potentially meteor-related or a metaphor for humidity-linked ailments), and old joints and legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And the quality of his health is such that the patient should immerse himself in hot water and rub the vein until it bursts, and tie over the joint with cloth.
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot it flows with much blood.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	Heal then the wound, whether it is deeper or wider, at the shoulder, or ankle, as it was before.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you heal it on the foot, be careful with the bands that are underneath, and also heal across it as if you were sewing.
et soit li flaimes anesil.	and so the flames will subside.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	If the pain cannot be relieved, immerse the foot in water and allow the vein to drain completely.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if you heal it the first time, be careful to start again from above a little, because the ligaments are salty.
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and do the same for the wisdom of the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The vein's lion is at the foot's ankle, and its health corresponds to the pain of the back when it is hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And the quality of his health is such that if the patient is in the bath, he should pull three times on the ankle, otherwise the vein will not open.
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	and if it opens, take the health in all ways that you can, and crossing.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it is worth that you hold it, for the veins are safe, and it is much relieved by many hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not release it, so that no healthy ray of light enters through the opening or hole in the back or foot, and turn towards the little toe, and guard against constriction.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	and apply pressure with your hand to the blood as you see it, then unbind the ligature and place cotton on it and tighten it.
ele est maintenant sanee.	it is now healthy.
des sainies de ventouse	from the suction of the cupping glass
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Vacuum cups are made of horns, or iron, or glass;
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	and ventilation is done according to two manners:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	or by perforating and drawing out pus, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this ventilation without piercing is according to two manners:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	or it is with all fire, or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	and ventilation done through piercing and extraction of pus is performed in twelve to fourteen parts of the body, so that one part remains entirely still at the top.
et li autres est emmi le col;	and the others are at the neck.
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and the others on both sides of the neck.
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the suction from below the jaw.
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and the suction from both shoulders.
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the suction on the knees.
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and the suction on both arms.
et les ventouses des II jambes;	and the cups on both legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	and the cups on both ankles;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and the ventilation does not remove blood, because of the small veins that are scattered throughout the flesh, and for this reason it does not weaken anyone, as is done with healthy veins;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it is not advisable to allow it in any case without fire or sensation of fire, in any disease that arises from overindulgence, as long as the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if, by necessity or due to habit, it is required to expel air, we must do so each hour at the beginning and end of the month, and in every season.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are such people who, when they need to expel air, have a heavy head.
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and if such people experience relief from pressing and redness on their face, head, neck, and darkness around the eyes.
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and such people who experience a drop of blood in their mouth, have an inflamed tongue, and feel pain.
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and if there are any who think, and see through blood and pain and fear and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, especially in the middle of the month, we order it to be ventosed after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The surgeon of the wound uses pressure on the neck ... to bring relief, and it is not appropriate that this be done after the evacuation of all the blood.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and this compression should be done on the neck of the surgical patient, and it is not appropriate for those of a cold temperament or who have catarrh, as it does them much harm.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and for this reason, it is not appropriate for the elderly or those with cold diseases of the head to use it.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who recover from it often become obstructed, and for this reason a suction cup should be placed slightly lower in doubt of obstruction.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	The ventilation of the chest is beneficial for the health of the heart and basil (organs), and therefore it tightens the pains in the chest, opens the channel of the windpipe, and helps digestion and replenishment.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it is necessary to know when to release pressure, because if it is held too tightly, it can cause forgetfulness or stomach and body pain.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	The wind flows between the ribs of the chest if it causes head, eye, and temple pain, and strangulation, and tooth root pain, and is detrimental to the health of the heart and basil (organs).
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and it is necessary that you instruct the patient to extend his hand when placing it, so as not to damage the artery and prevent bleeding complications.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	The removal of the tooth is beneficial for mouth disease, gum corruption, and similar ailments in the mouth.
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	and it is located in the gums between the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The inflammation of the shoulders is associated with disease that arises from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	The extraction of the roots is just as important as opening three veins in the arm, because it draws blood from these large veins.
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instruct the healthy not to cut too deeply, for the flesh is bare of fat, and knows veins and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The leech placed on the rump is worth much, for it draws blood from the depths and treats internal ailments, and it must be large, made of iron, and have a good suction to draw effectively.
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	and if, by chance, it were too delicate, it would break.
et i fai grans plaies.	and it causes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	The suction cups on the legs are tightly sealed, for they draw blood from throughout the body, and they are as painful as ancient rains, and inflammation, and bladder issues, and they cause paralysis.
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	and they are attached to the inner and outer ankles, yet they weaken the body after long use and cause pain in various ways.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The method of applying the suction cup is as follows: you apply it first while it is empty and suck thoroughly, then place it firmly, and move it equally, without ceasing to do so, until you see red and inflamed skin, and open the blood-letting wound.
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	Then apply heat, and remove the suction cups, and take care in the placement of the leeches, for there are some with strong blood flow and clear pores.
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	if it is necessary to strike only once, then wide wounds should be made, and deep cuts.
et suce legierement.	and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if the pain is intense, it is necessary to strike twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	The first time to gently uncover the way of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to pierce for the third time;
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	and when we want to draw out blood little by little, it is enough to do so only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we want a lot of blood, we should not recommence often;
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and if the blood is thick, piercing it successfully will complete the process, so that the veins are suddenly perceivably filled, and it is necessary for those with thick, hard skin and calloused pores to apply oil to the suction cup before and after use.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is of a purple oil, or of sweet almond oil, or of oil from pumpkin seeds;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is of olive oil, or of watercress oil, or of lily oil, or chamomile oil, or any similar one.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is thick and cold, take amaranth oil, or balm of Gilead, or donkey oil, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if anyone has a skin that is too sensitive and has narrow pores, it is not advisable to apply oil, but instead, after cleansing with rosewater, or cold water, or water of mulberry, or water of calabash, or water of porcelain, or any similar thing, they should wash it.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And for those with excessive moisture, they should rise from it using myrrh water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have abundant secretions should rise from old wine, or elderberry water, or chamomile or anise decoction, or any similar thing;
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	and should not attempt to use a vacuum (for medical purposes) before or during a bath, but rather after the bath, one or two hours later.
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and do not sleep after the bleeding, and it is necessary that he washes himself, when he must be bled and when he is bled.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	and beware of those who have a hot temper, and if someone is too aggressive and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	it is necessary that he apply cold things, such as grapes, endive and lettuce in the shade, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and eat figs, and grapes, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And he who has a cold complexion, should sip syrup made from honey, and drink fragrant wine mixed with herbs, which is between old and new, and eat small portions, and enjoy raisins and small birds.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and on the day when he feels hungry, he should drink more than eat.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary not to give any hot drinks or spices to anyone, either before or after the treatment, to comfort the main limbs.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and let the treatment be subtle, but it is not suitable for those who are hot to drink such things.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The suction cups that are used to harm are those placed on the liver, and the skin, and podagra, and the stomach and the bowels and the kidneys and the spine, for this member cannot be harmed except to attract blood from one member to another, as we do with mammary glands when nursing.
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	to reduce the viscosity in the member, as we apply suction cups to the stomach and bowels to ease the pain.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and alleviate the pain when there is oppression or stone, if by its attractive power it removes the oppression, or deserts the stone from its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	and thus it is done when one places it on the liver and stomach where there is retention of wind, and these suction cups are left empty to suck only for a time.
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	and never should they be used together with fire, and never should they be filled with cold water, as in the case of diseases that cause excessive tearing, and in such a way one fills the cup with hot water, or with water he has boiled with medicinal herbs.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the suction cup administered by fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And it should be two and a half palm widths in length, and on one side near the middle there is a small opening, as wide as to push an needle through, and it should be made of iron or any other suitable material so that it does not hurt the patient when placed on the limb.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and tell him to place a stick diagonally across it, either of iron or wood, to hold a bandage in place, according to the size and age of those who suffer from them.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the suction cups of children are different from those of adults, thinner than fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one must thus place this suction cup over the member:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	take the cloth of wax or linen and place it between the suction cup and the stick that holds the suction cup, so that the light goes to the bottom of the suction cup, preventing it from burning the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it over the member, and your fingers should be on the opening that we have mentioned, so that when you want, the vapour goes there, and we remove the suction cup.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and take up the bandage as before, and repeat often, if you have need.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the case of the suction cup, which is applied to treat pleurisy, and any acute condition, it has no opening or gap, and is only effectively applied when it is filled with water, and placed over the member accordingly.
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	According to the context of the text, this line translates to: "Without being able to apply suction for their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar parts.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in parts without hair, such as the face, hands, or feet, and similar areas.
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of the user is such that when you find veins that are smooth, clear, and free from any impurity, then take them.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and place a needle in hot, sharp water, as long as they are familiar to her, and have nothing in their bellies.
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then make the vein and cupping glass clean, and rub the limb until it is red, and apply the compresses.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they stop crying and whining, if it is a place where a cupping glass can be applied, apply it, for this helps greatly afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If that is not possible, then raise the limb gently, and wash it well with water, and then dry it.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and hold the eyes steady too after the body of the wound, if a damp linen cloth in cold water is placed on it and left until the pain subsides.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the pain increases, add vinegar or gall, or similar things, until it subsides.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you can place half-peeled beans on the joint and leave them until they adhere to the bone, which will now soothe it.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if this method is more suitable for you, then take other wounds.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the veins do not want to be captured, so strongly rub the fresh vein with blood, or you insert an needle until the vein bursts, and then place them back on, and soon as they feel the blood, they will move.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are moving, sprinkle a little aloe and silk powder, or ash, and they will now stop.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	We begin the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it restores fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know this, dear reader, that the folly of this chapter flows from it, for never did they see or read of such things in any ancient books.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and for this reason, the art is strange in our land, for I never found any good about it.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing of it, except through the knowledge of ancient books, in which I have studied so much that I have acquired knowledge of it, both through experience and through the habits of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained, and at the end I have summarized it, and clearly shown the shapes of the instruments that are used, as I did in the two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we explain in this prologue of this book the essence of the words and the chapters where the wise apply their understanding, focusing on truth, so that those who are tested know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a fracture, dislocation, twist, or sprain occurs in any part of the body, it is necessary to quickly attend to the patient from both sides, if nothing else prevents you, such as weakness of the body, illness, or old age.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	or if it is very tight or too cold;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	and warm things, such as hot poultices, and cloth from pigeon's blood and horse chestnut, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty foods, or consume too much meat that fills the veins with blood, until you have no doubt of a hot abscess or the spreading of material in the member;
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	if the patient returns to sleep after having been under stress.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that the patient be relieved of the foods that cause heavy digestion, or have a viscous quality, like cooked flour in water, and rice, and vegetables, and wine, and fresh fish, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For heavy digestion often returns and makes the injury worse.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the bones broken from old age or decay cannot heal properly and mend according to their nature due to the stiffness of the members, nor those that are too soft, such as the bones of small children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	but there is no cure, instead, hold the broken bone with strong fingers that separate and join the member together, as it was before.
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	and do not restrict it entirely from its movement, and because of this, one must avoid heavy foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot, and in this chapter, I will tell you all manner of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes to the bone, and another when sharpening, just like the edge of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if the fracture is with a wound, and there is a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each condition has its own mechanism, and its specific instrument for restoration, according to the memory that comes to it naturally.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and the fracture of the bone is recognized because the joint is twisted, and it opens well when pulled away from the body, and responds to pressure with the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no twisting or pressure, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no fracture.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can still have twisting, or splitting, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	You should not move it with the hand, but apply medications that come here later, and then tighten it very subtly now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the fracture that goes up in the air, and the two parts are disjoined, now you must put them back together evenly so that an abscess does not form from it.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if an abscess forms, leave it without moving for as long as the abscess is healed.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	then align it evenly with gentle and firm touch, and know that the healing of it is easier than the healing of one where it has been broken.
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then tighten it, as it should be after this.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if in the broken bone there is dislocation from two parts, whether it's of the hand or foot, or one small member, or both tendons, or a tendon and your hand.
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and place the member according to its natural position, so that when the parts of the broken member are out of alignment, by all means reset them to their original positions, and ensure through your care that no further injury or pain comes to the patient.
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and adjust both parts of the bone according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And feel the pulse well with your hand if it seems not to be well.
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	if the dressing is done well and not pulled too tightly, nor pressed as those who, by their own will, cause hot abscesses and contractions in the member, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the member is at its worst, gently encourage the patient not to move it, neither awake nor asleep, nor in any other way.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and ensure that the member is so secured that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	Because when he feels no pain, except perhaps at a specific point, it is necessary to put him in a position where he feels no pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and ensure that it is set correctly, preventing any curvature when it is restored.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the broken limb should be as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	You know that broken members are diverse in size and shape and strength.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	Because it has small members, like arms and legs and similar ones:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	if it is necessary to cover with soft and delicate cloth;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	and those that are thick, like the foot and leg;
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	it is necessary to cover with a wide and firm bandage, as the wide bandage embraces the entire limb, holding it tightly from all sides equally, so that there is no movement.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then wrap lighter strips around it three or four times, depending on the limb, tightening your hand slightly across the entire bandage, then move up over the dislocation and tighten less, allowing the dislocation to gradually separate a little.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the skin little by little, as you press deeply into the healthy flesh, then take another hold and return directly over the broken bone.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then go back to the part of the fracture, and hold it gently, neither too tight nor too loose, as we said in the first chapter above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then place thick linen or cloth between the bones until it is entirely even, then bind everything above with a bandage, and then place your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is an inflammation or abscess, apply a hot soothing agent to it, which reduces the swelling, and leave it thus for several days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then strain yourself on your stars, and use half of a narrow cane cut sharply, or of wood from which scythes are made, or palm fronds, and follow this form:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the star which one places on the fracture be somewhat thicker and broader than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and be as long as necessary for the size of the member, whether small or large;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then hold it steady on the stars just as you did with the first fracture, then tie it with a thread as in the first chapter when dealing with the break.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	the tighter it is bound, the less movement there is.
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and it is necessary that the thread be of medium thickness, not too thick nor too thin, and made of soft flax.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the thread is too thick, as I have seen fools make their ligatures from twisted flaxen cords, it is a great error, for the ligature cannot be even if it is too thin, and it is not appropriate that there should be less space between each star.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is angry because of the pain from the stars after dislocating them in their joints, he should put compresses of linen or other soft cloth over them to avoid bleeding.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is accompanied by a fracture, and the bones are broken, I will then describe the treatment below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not appropriate to dislocate all the stars of a member broken in the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limb is large, it is not advisable to apply heat immediately, but rather wait a few days, either five or seven or more according to your judgment of the hot swelling coming on.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	and here, the ancient method of splints for restoring fractures, dislocations, and torsions:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and take flour that clings to the walls of a mill, and mix it with an abundance of egg, and make this mixture, not too liquid or too thick, and use it, and this is the common method of splints for restoring fractures in various positions, especially for women and small children, as it is neither too hard nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another method of plastering restores breakage, dislocation, and twisting:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	Take bark, gall, and gum from the plant and mix them with water, as directed by Doctor X.
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	Mix mirror and aloe, as instructed by Doctor V.
alechil VIIII З.;	Take aloes VIIII (a specific amount or dose) as directed by Doctor VIIII.
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	and make it into powder, then mix it with egg white.
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	If the patient's skin is hot, then use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and it gently restores broken bones, and benefits many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another method of plastering that is beneficial for twists:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	Take moss and wolfsbane, and mix them with three parts of something else (unclear due to lack of context or specific term).
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	Mix mirror and aloe, with nine parts of something else (again, unclear due to lack of context or specific term).
acaice VI З.;	Behold six (parts);
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	mix Armenian (herbal) X parts, grind well, and mix with ample egg or honey, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another method of splinting joints and securing bones to their proper places, soothing the pain that arises, and using saws on the bone, and fractures.
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	take another new cloth, dampen it with water and oil, and place over the bone.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Cyst splints do not restore, but they are good for easing hot abscesses and properly extracting bones that cause pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another method of splinting to restore broken bones:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Take dry fig leaves and terrestrial pawpal leaves, grind them together, and make a splint.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of mending the broken bone and thereby alleviating the pain from the abscess's return.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take the root of alder, chamomile, violets' flowers, and wheat flour, each in equal parts.
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Grind and mix with wine, and if the member is hot, mix with fresh coriander water or water, and apply as needed.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another stronger method of mending the member when a hard abscess arises during restoration.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take roots of vismalve, and flaxseed, and balm, and melilot, and fennel, and violet and chamomile flowers, from all these plants a part.
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	and grind it, and conserve it with salt water, or fresh water, or wine, according to the heat of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates writes in his book that to restore a broken member, one should not use anything but a mixture of wax and oil, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen suggests applying warm, dry substances to a broken member to restore it, such as myrrh and aloe and incense, as we have mentioned.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another method of treatment for injuries and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	take mice and cats from humans who have been cut, or feathers from an eye, and vismalve, and string of equal length, grind them together, and make a plaster and bind it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then dislocate it a little later, and be careful that the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the bone moved out of its place.
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	if it does not dislocate by strong hands.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if pain comes to the place, or itching, feeling no rest, or swelling, act quickly, dislocate it, and remove the splint now.
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	take a light cloth, and a moist sea sponge, and dip it in water, and gently raise the limb until the itching stops, and the pain is soothed.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	then let the member rest for an hour, then place it on a dry cloth, moistened with water or rose oil, and tie it up with a bandage, as long as you are certain of the hot abscess.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	and rest the inflamed member, and if the pain subsides, then resume the bandaging with a gentle touch and some plaster, and do not strain it as strongly as before.
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and gently until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is closed, red, painful and swollen, you have successfully treated it; but if it reappears, as you did at first, then you need to use plaster and binding.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if the member shows no improvement from what we have said, then do not dislocate it until after three, four, five, or seven days.
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	and never leave it for more than a few days, according to what one sees, until the fracture heals and draws closer to the adjustment of the limb on its bed.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	then the compression must be stronger than first, and it thickens its flesh, as I have said before;
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	and if the limb seems healthier than necessary, know that improvement cannot come from it.
