arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	soak it in hot water every time you dislocate it, each day for three days, and slightly loosen the ligament.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	Through this work, then, we cut the nerve passages in the limb, and prudently perform what the ignorant do, which is to straighten a deformed member:
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	This is harmful, and if the work is perilous, I see no other option but to leave it alone or do it correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various methods of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many ways of fractures, various shapes, and the causes are diverse.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	Because there are fractures caused by the impact of a sword, and the bone splinters completely through to the other side, as if cut with a hatchet or club.
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	and for this reason, this method of dislocation is called "hachure.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	He then uses the sword to cut through the bone without piercing it, and this method of dislocation is called "absolute.
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	and this injury from these two dislocations is either great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a pulsation or swelling, or cutting from stones or from blows against stone, or from other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a recent fracture, which approaches the bone tissue underneath or on top of the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if the wound that is closed over the bone is as subtle as a hair, and the fracture is small, then it is called this dislocation "capillary.
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	and if the wound is made by a blow from stone or arrow or similar thing, and the bone fragment enters deeper, and the joints are stiffened as when a blacksmith works on the hearth;
si entre li piere dedens.	if the stone enters inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more frequently to those with soft, moist bones, like a child's head.
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and it occurs in all these ways of breakage, leaving small fragments dislocated as if they were.
et je em parlerai en son leu.	and I will speak to him in his place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all the ways of dislocations by pulling on them, and questioning at each point, and by corrupt flesh above it.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hair appearance is recognized when, after uncovering the bone and rubbing it thoroughly, the dislocation gap opens up.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of fractures, be wary of accidents with the patient, and if you notice any harmful accident, such as vomiting blood, loss of consciousness, dilation, numbness, fever, sudden heat or redness, or other similar symptoms in various combinations, it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any dangerous accidents and hope for healing, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the frost comes first to you, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day of the moon, if you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it happens that you hasten to remove the bone on the seventh day, so that the tissue around the bone is corrupted, then come the complications that we have mentioned.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the fracture of the bone extends to the membrane that covers the brain, then you must cut through the fractured part thusly:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and you should pierce the patient's head with great pain, and expose the bone in every way that you can, and carefully clean the wound, gently removing any pus or abscess that appears, if it drains when you uncover the bone, or a fistula forms, then you must use whatever aid is appropriate, and fill the cavity with moistened, rosin-soaked cloth.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	and make the wound rest until the abscess is completely healed, and be assured of the stop of blood flow.
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	then begin around the bone to open it, and this is done according to two methods of operation:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	one method is that you make a narrow cut at the front, and it takes this form:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I use another treatment even greater than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	and the second method is that you have numerous cuts of different widths, some narrow and others wide, and they are pointed and made of iron indelibly.
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	and when working lightly, do not knock the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is hard and dense, it is necessary that you bore into it carefully, so as to administer the treatment accurately, without going beyond the bone's thickness, and there should be a margin or curve on top of the point to prevent it from penetrating beyond the bone.
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	and you will need several of them, so that each one comes in its proper place according to the bone's thickness, giving you the necessary accuracy.
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	and this is the form of the three types of treatments:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The quality to understand around the broken bone is that you apply the treatment to the bone, and return to your normal activities as long as you know that the bone is healed.
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	then apply the treatment to another area a little later, and do so all around, then carefully incise the space between the fragments of the bone, and make it as subtle and gentle as possible, while still holding the bone in your hand or with any tools you have, such as pliers or tweezers.
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	and ensure you do not touch the brain nor the eye.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced the bone and treated it, it is necessary that you remove the stiffness that is delayed from the bone to all other instruments resembling an incision tool, but it should be more flexible and more subtle than the other incision tools.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	and if it delays nothing of the small bones, nor any scales, gently remove them with the instrument.
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	then treat the wound with care, as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And another method of treatment is as Galen says, which is safer.
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	and speak very loudly, for that is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is first necessary that you expose a part of the bone, either where the fracture is open, so that when you have exposed this part, you will place the tip of this curved scalpel beneath it, whose shape is as follows:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not deviate from this method in any way, for the sharp side is on the second coast, so the incision should be towards the bone.
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	then strike with a small hammer from above, so that you gently compress the bone all around, and be careful to protect yourself from the sharp edges below.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is detached from the bone, if the bone is gently pulled, for it is removed with great pain and fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not reach the skin, and the bone is only cut from above, and there are small pieces, then it is necessary to remove that roughness, and shave off the scales with a delicate razor, having various quantities of it at hand, in order to make each one suitable for its place, according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you encounter great difficulties and then even more subtle ones, do not cease from this task until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	For each of the other haircuts and subtle injuries, it is necessary that you treat them according to their location.
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	and this is something that is not fully answered for those who have dedicated their study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if it brings satisfaction, it is necessary that you apply a linen bandage according to the size of the wound, soak it in rose oil, and place it on the wound.
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	then take another cloth doubled over in two or three, moisten it with wine and rose oil, and place it on top of the first cloth.
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	and make it lighter than you can, without straining the wound, then apply another bandage on top and do not tighten it too much so that it only touches the wound.
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	and leave it thus for a day or two until the abscess is calmed, then remove it and apply medications such as fennel roots, flour of vetch, incense powder, aromatic herbs, and similar things.
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and from these things make a powder, apply it to the wound, and administer world-renowned remedies without biting;
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	and ensure that the wound remains clean, do not leave any treatment, and do not allow it to gather pus, for when pus accumulates in the tissue of the brain, it will corrupt and harm the patient greatly.
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	for when you apply sharp, biting things to it, they do not heal properly.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care therefore, if no bad accident comes to the patient, as we have said, it is uncertain without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if blackness does not appear due to the medicine that has been applied, then it is necessary that you mix a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil, and add a cloth, and apply it to the sore.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then apply remedies in a manner appropriate to healing, as long as he is healthy.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	Knowing that the two parts of the upper arm bones are never broken at the same time, either one by itself or both, because they are two bones.
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	and the inner part is cartilaginous and does not break, unless it bends or twists excessively, then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, it is necessary that you insert your little finger or a pin in the joint, and place the same fracture in your index finger, and by force, until the joint returns to its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and make it gentle, and ensure that the patient feels no pain through your actions.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the upper part of the joint, and the fingers cannot return to their place, then it is necessary that you place it equally at the head of a slightly thicker thread.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the fracture is of the second degree, repeat the process, and hasten to restore it on the first day, if you can.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	if this is not possible, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess has subsided, then apply to the joint two or three linen bandages, if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	Or you apply another from another side, if the fracture persists.
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	and let them (bandages) be so thick that they fill the gaps of the wound.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say that no restoration is complete unless the splints are soaked in butter and changed each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	I do not think that this is good enough, but it is necessary that they (bandages) be moistened in the preparation of egg albumen and mill powder.
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	then remove the bandage, as long as the bone is hard and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And never should feathers of a goose be used in place of bandages, and if a wound is wrapped with silk, and the break holds, and the patient breathes among them.
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	or make sure you see well.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses appear at the new wound while you are treating it, apply a plaster or moist cotton in rose oil, or in a poultice of eagle's fat.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if an abscess does not come out, apply a poultice from outside with flour of wheat bran and powder of incense, preserved with egg yolk, then place light bandages on it and do not tie the nose.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	and if the nose is broken and in small pieces, extract it with suitable instruments, then cut the fracture and treat the bleeding with charcoal and other appropriate bandages.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if there is no internal wound, he should rest for a while and apply poultices until he is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	from the rupture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is ruptured and there is no external wound, and the fracture is not severe enough to cause two pieces to be separated, but it is slightly displaced, then if you gently know how to recognize it, it can be realigned.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	If the fracture is in the right side, insert your index finger into the mouth of the patient with the injury.
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	and if the fracture is in the left lower jaw, insert your index finger of your right hand, gently push the fracture back into place, and use your left hand to pull it out, equally.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is severe in two places, it is necessary that you administer an extension to both parts, as long as they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if the movement of the teeth occurs, or the fracture, if it is strained with a thread of gold, silver, or silk, then apply cera to the broken jaw and place a double cloth on top.
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And place it on a cloth, a large star-shaped pad, or an equal piece of leather, long and wide according to the jaw, and fix it with bandages as best you can, and order the patient to rest, and eat light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you see that the shape changes, after three days loosen it again and then reset it when it has changed.
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	and apply a poultice of finely ground powder with plenty of egg or sesame flour after you have removed the plaster.
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	and place on it a light plaster, and if the plaster hardens, and the condition of the patient does not change, leave it until it is completely healed.
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	often it is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess forms, it is necessary to treat it as we have often said.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if there is both a fracture and a wound together, treat none of the bone that has been broken.
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	if it is possible to remove the bone with delicate tools.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, expand it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And after you have extracted all these pieces and it does not delay, clean the wound if it is wide, and cover it with suitable bandages to promote healing.
de la forcele	from the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	It forces breaks several times towards the shoulder, and the fracture is according to three manners:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	or it is broken and displaced in two parts, and there are fragments, and it is the easiest to restore;
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	or there is fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the work is when the fracture is without a wound, that you have two ministers, so that one holds the aid that feels the forced break.
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the others extend the collar towards the affected area;
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	then make the fracture even on both sides, so that the shape is as it should be, and there is no bulge or depression.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you need to further extend it, place a round, thick cloth or woolen spear beneath the shoulder of the patient, as large as needed.
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	and gently extend the force, stretch the spear with your hand, ensuring an even fracture as required.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the arm out due to its attachment, since it comes off completely, then the patient should lie on their side with the injured arm under their body, and have someone press down on the shoulder above, until the bone of the arm is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	And then address the fracture with your hands, and if you feel the bone is broken, it is necessary that you cut through it.
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	and gently try to move the pieces, and if the bone cannot join together despite your efforts, then the fracture is in one of the incisions you have.
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but that you apply the strength of this instrument beneath, to ensure success.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and it should resemble a spoon, and not be thin, and also as wide as necessary, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work.
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and say to him, as you see, one should be wide and the other narrow, just like the opening of the wound that you made when you treated the bone;
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are certain of the hot abscess, if you cut the wound, and if its opening is small, then you doubt the hot abscess, if you use a drape or tent on the wound, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot abscesses occur, then moisten the cloth with rose oil and wool and wine, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The straining of the bone, when it is sensitive to touch and has no incision, is that you place on the bone the plaster of fine-milled powder and egg albumen, and put light stoppers above, and insert a spear from below the joint, if necessary.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	then take a very wide bandage of one palm's length, then place the cloth doubled over the stumps, and apply the plaster.
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	then take a very thin and long stick of three fingers' width and wrap it around the bandage, so that the top of the bandage is exposed.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	and place the stick on the fracture, and turn the bandage around the collarbone, and remove the healthy armpit, and remove the affected armpit.
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and reset each part, and when you see that the bandage holds the fracture well, and you clearly see that the stick does not move on the broken bone, tighten it each day, and when the ligaments loosen, release the constraint.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	and make the patient lie down on his side, and place a small pillow under his armpit to raise the affected limb;
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	if the fracture is light, secure the shoulder with a splint, fasten the arm to the collarbone, and do not unlock it for no ill accidents come, for up to 20 days;
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	then recommence the splinting if you see that it needs to be done again, tighten it and leave it thus, until it is restored;
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	and it is restored within 28 days, or even less for no one.
de la brisure de l’espaule	from the dislocation of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	It is often the case that the shoulder breaks or becomes severely dislocated and cannot be moved, except by touch.
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	if the apparatus is adjusted according to the shape of the fracture and reset according to its natural form in every way that you can.
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	then place a light pouder of finely ground chalk and egg whites, and soft bandages, and cover with a double cloth.
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	then place a wide and delicate blade, slightly wider than the shoulder, and dislocate the blade from any part of the shoulder, using the sharp edge of linen cloth, so that the blade cuts evenly.
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	and then tighten it with a great tight band firmly, so that the blade does not move from its place, and observe it each day.
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	and whenever it loosens, relax the band and put the blade back in its place if it has moved, and lay the patient on his side.
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	and the shoulder is reset within 10 to 25 days.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when this number of days is completed, if it becomes loose, and be sure, for it is not bone that will immediately settle firmly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a fragment of bone sticks out and does not go inside the wound, it is necessary to do as we have said in the calming of the hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	from the rupture of the worst
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The skin is never completely broken, but it happens rarely.
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	but it often breaks under heat.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it recedes inside and causes the patient great pain, and weakness, and sometimes bleeds, and opens up the wound in the broken bone, and it feels much better.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the restoration is such that the patient lies often on their back, and places a cushion between the shoulders, then compresses them, and aligns the ribs to each other with both hands, subtilly making them even in all ways possible, so that the shape of the bone is as it should be.
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	Then place on it plaster and poultices over the delicate salt or other light bandage, wrap it in a cloth, and bind it to the broken bone so that it does not move.
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	and return the ligament to its original shape on the back, tighten it carefully, and check the patient's freedom of movement every hour, relaxing it if it becomes tight.
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	if it needs to be released due to erosion or itching that develops in the area, or pain or abscess, act quickly, release it, remove the plaster, and treat what has come up with appropriate remedies.
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then reset the splint, and hold it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	from the fracture of ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	Know that the breaking of ribs only occurs in the upper back and at the top, and they do not bend unless they are clearly broken.
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	and the patient feels well at the examination.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is such that you put it back in place as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the plaster, tightening it with a splint if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the breaking of ribs is declining inward, the patient feels very great pain, stabbing, as well as crying, because the bone pierces through.
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	and so with fingers, touch and press deeply the blood, which is great pain, and they have put much art into it by the ancients.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And for those who say it is appropriate to administer foods that cause bloating in the stomach to expel the fracture from within.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not pretend that hot poultices will not come if they have not already arrived.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it comes back, as healthy.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	and they say among themselves that one should not use cupping glasses on the shoulder to draw blood, as it is akin to madness.
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	however, there is doubt that the cupping glass does not draw out excess blood from the shoulder for its own sake due to weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that none of you should cover the limb with moist wool and hot oil, and place tents between the ribs to even out the space around, then apply treatment for pleurisy, flesh, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	and if the patients feel great pain that they cannot bear even to the bone where the flesh is torn, then doubt creeps in for the patient, and it is necessary to cut through the skin of the broken rib and put beneath a tool to relieve the suffering.
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then one must cut the bone, pull gently, and stitch together both edges of the wound, if it is large, and treat it with bandages, until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if abscesses form, place moist, oil-soaked rags on them and cover with a warm compress.
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat while the compress is on the abscess, and place soft pillows under the affected area, as needed, until it heals.
de la brisure dou col	Of the dislocation of the collarbone
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	No break should occur between the collarbone and chest bone, and if it does rain;
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	and also to the pain of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to anyone and you want to know if they will recover, be on the lookout for their hands becoming soft, swollen, and numb, and unable to move or stretch them; if you can push an needle through without pain, then there is little hope.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	You know that it is deadly in many ways; if the limbs remain motionless and there is no pain when they are moved slightly, then know that the joint of the bone is intact and the patient will recover, if proper treatment is given.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if similar symptoms occur in the pain of the back, you should know if it is healthy or not, take care to see if the feet are weak, and if there are any accidents that affect the hands, and on the back, sudden weakness and expulsion without will.
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	and when it is remembered on the stomach, sudden expulsion without will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is recalled to its back and wants to move, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	Knowing that it is deadly:
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	if he does not work hard in his cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not occur, then the thing is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	And the treatment is that you apply rose oil or egg yolk oil to the hot abscess, as long as it is soothed.
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	then place a comfortable and drying bandage on it, tie it with a band, and instruct the patient to rest.
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	and do not sleep on that part where he feels the pain, as long as he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	And if any bone becomes detached, then it needs to be covered with a bandage over the heart.
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and take the bone, then bring together the two edges of the wound, if it is large, with stitches, and then apply a healing dressing made of clean cloth, until it is healed.
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	and if the bone fragment is broken, which is called the "fragment of the wound," take your pouchet (a small instrument) with your left hand and place it equally in your right hand to hold the fragment, then apply plaster and a splint, as needed.
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	then hold it tight, and if there is a bone out of place, push it back into position, and treat the wound until it heals completely.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	From the fracture of the bone of the shoulder blade
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	Often, the first thing to happen is that the hip bone is broken, and if so, there should be no significant loss of blood from the head.
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	and causing it to stretch long and thin, bending towards the patient's body, bringing pain, swelling, and bruising to the broken area.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	And the restoration is such that you extend your hand above, as long as you are on the broken spot;
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	and such are the fracture and form of it;
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	and if the fracture is only in the head, then make all such fractures even, as long as they are in their natural form.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is very long, it bends inward, so make the patient lie on his belly until the restoration of that fracture becomes visible.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	And when you have made it even, then place a splint over it, and then a wooden or iron bar, and hold the fracture still so that it does not move.
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	and apply pressure from the inside of the ribs along the sides until the limb is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	And if an abscess appears and it is not touched, as long as the abscess remains calm, apply what we have mentioned above.
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	and then return to reducing it, and hold it as appropriate if there is no adverse event.
et c’est li maniere.	and this is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder joint
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The aider is the space between the shoulder blade and the top of the shoulder, and if it is broken, one should restore it according to one of the two ways:
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	Don't take one that is neither too hard nor too soft, according to this form.
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	And bind the two parts together, twist them upwards, and place the patient in a sitting position.
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	then pour the patient's broken arm over the foot, until it is relaxed, and place a splint of wood across it, then twist it upwards to any heavy object or have the attendants pull it downwards.
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	then place the splint against the break so that it is even with both hands together, until the break returns to its proper position.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And another way is to lay the patient on his back and tie one hand to his neck, then instruct the assistants to have one apply pressure over the fracture at the level of the hands, while the other stretches all the ligaments, extending them as far as possible.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that extraction is too painful, hold the broken piece firmly, and on the break, stretch each of the assistants to their side.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	And if the fracture is near the top of the shoulder, it is necessary that you apply a moderate tie beneath the joint, and another towards the neck, beneath the fracture.
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	and also if the fracture is towards the neck, it is necessary to apply a light tie without strain, as long as the fracture is level on both sides of the shoulder and neck.
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	then make the fracture even, as it should be, and hold it tight, if abscesses do not appear.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	And if an abscess appears, it should not be squeezed for seven days, and a moist cloth soaked in rose oil should be applied to it until the abscess at the base is calmed.
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	then squeeze it, and the manner of squeezing is that you place the plaster on the break, then reassemble the arm above the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or the breast.
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	and apply the bandage, squeeze above the shoulder and the arm, so that the arm is in a straight position, unless something prevents it or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, use a splint, and place a wider and stronger stick across the break, leaving two spaces between each stick, and let each stick extend beyond the break by three parts.
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	then strain the sticks, as I said at the beginning of this chapter regarding the break, making them stronger and less distant.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if you observe the position of the sticks and their strain, as we said, when you return the broken limb, and you doubt whether the abscess is hot, leave it bound for seven days, as we have said.
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	Then each day for three days, look at the wound to ensure it does not swell or become infected, or any redness cannot reach the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If it is appropriate, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	And if no such accident occurs, the dislocation should only be corrected after three days or more, and the patient should sleep on their back, with their hands on their stomach.
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	and place the dislocated joint in a soft cushion made of equal parts wool, and every hour during the day or night, check to ensure the limb's shape is not changing, or the bonds are becoming weak.
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	if it is cured by the virtue of medicine, and gives him food that we have previously mentioned, in such a way that the food is first subtle.
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	and when it begins to recover, it will be significant.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	And it is customary that the aid and leg should be recovered over forty days in all.
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	and then one must free it and administer baths and medicines of ointments to direct the limb.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the tightness is severe and compressed, it may take up to several months or two months to release.
de la brisure du bras	of the dislocation of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "forearm," where one is smaller and follows the direction of the hand.
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	and the other is larger, which is located below the smaller bone towards the hand.
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	should the larger forearm bone break by chance, or the smaller one, they may be joined back together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	When the smaller bones are broken, their restoration is easier, and healing follows quickly.
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	and when the bones are broken and healing is poor, it becomes more painful than when they were initially broken altogether.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only the small bones that are broken, then it is sufficient to extend them slightly and make them even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	And if it is a large fracture, then the tension must be increased.
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	and extend it on the cushion, placing the palm higher than the other hand, with the small fingers lower, and cross the patient over it, with the cushion in front, higher than the patient's discomfort allows.
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	then extend the minister's right arm to the side of his hand, or to the joint, and another minister extends his left hand above it.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then set it back even, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the fracture each piece is set back in its place, and if there is no misplaced bone that grips the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place by manipulating it above and below, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	And if there is a break in the wound, I have spoken of it in detail to the specific chapter.
si pren la cure.	if takes the treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	And in the beginning of restoration, when abscesses occur, I wrap them with a mixture of rose oil and white wax, not too hard or too soft.
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	and lay it gently over, until the abscesses close.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	And then remove the bandage, and apply the plaster of the soft powder with plenty of egg, then place the needles, and let the needle of the dislocation be stronger, a little more forceful, and slightly wider than the others.
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	and know that he must have 6 needles or arms in various positions:
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	so that the dislocation is in one of the bones, or both;
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	and hold tighter over the dislocation than anywhere else, and all the while moving less as I said at the beginning of this chapter.
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	and let the cloths that are on the gentle and moist wound not be hard or rough.
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	and let the thread, from which it is drawn, be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the member and the ligament after no days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	And if any bad accident comes to the member, such as itching that comes to the member, then it is necessary that you wash the member with hot water until the itching is soothed.
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	and let the member not be squeezed too tightly at rest.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then repeat the straining, and if the ligaments become slack and the bones disarrayed, or any similar thing, address it accordingly.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if any tightening prevents the member from healing, because it is too tight, then you must soften it slightly and leave it for a few days until the tightening subsides, and then strain it again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things we have said comes to the patient, then he shall be dislocated for twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	You shall gently inquire, then make him rest his hands on his chest, and ensure his collars are even, and guard against movements and gestures, and have him sleep on his back.
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	and know that this fracture is healed in thirty days or forty-five, and perhaps in twenty days, according to the combinations and complexities of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	You know that at the back of the hand and on each finger there are often small fractures, and it brings only pain many times over.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	And when the hand's bone is broken or bent, it is necessary that the patient make a cross cut, and hold it straight before him equally.
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	then place his hand on the extended board, extend the broken bones of the minister, and align them evenly, until they are properly joined.
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	and apply the plaster and hot compresses, if an abscess forms, then place a stick according to the size of the wound.
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	and it should be wrapped in a linen drape.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	And if the rupture is near the abdomen around the plant, make a ball of cloth and instruct the patient to press it against their ruptured part.
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	and then apply a long strip of cloth, and make the heat as intense as the palm of the hand, and tighten it, as necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is in the open air, it is necessary that you place a stick above and another below on the limb, so that the hand is open and straight, then tie it tightly around the hand, and stop the bleeding between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	And if a fracture occurs in any of our joints, it is the dislocation that causes it, so it must be set correctly.
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	and tighten with the palm, and if you see that a small, straight heat correctly aligns the fracture, it will not move.
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	and if the fracture is in other joints, as in the example or any other, set it correctly and bind it with the healthy joint that follows.
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	you should hold them all in place with a bandage, or put a splint on them as you see fit;
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	and be careful in the restoration and arrangement of the hot abscess, and support those who come to it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	from the broken hip
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	The bones of the foot are often broken, and one can clearly see them when they return to their place in front and behind.
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	and the restoration is when they bind them together above the break and from below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	And the patient lies on his face, then each limb extends its own joint equally.
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	and this is when the fracture is through the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is close to the root of the hipbone, one of the ligaments should be bound towards the knee, and the others should be bound over and around the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	And also if it is close to the knee, then the joints around the knee are relaxed and the extension is downward.
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	then aligns the broken bone with both hands, according to its natural shape, and then applies the splint and binds it, so that the fracture does not move.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	And if there is a hot abscess, let it calm down, then return to your work and treatment;
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	The bandage is made in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	You should wrap around the fracture a hard bandage doubled in two or three layers, and remove the excess, then turn the leg until the heels reach the root of the toe, and insert a long thread between the calf and the leg, passing through the knee from below, and bring the end up above.
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	Then turn the bandage around the leg and thigh, then place a splint across it, and put a stick on the bone of the leg.
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	Then use the eighth part of a cloth soft between the leg and thigh to apply even pressure, then begin to tie three turns or four around the splint.
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	and as you go further up the splint, loosen the tension.
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	then take the two threads you have woven between the leg and thigh, and tie three stitches on top of them, then go back to the other side towards the ankle with the thread until you are done.
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	and hold it still, if it does not move from its place, then leave it as such, so that no abscess or swelling or anything similar appears.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	And if it happens that it becomes dislocated again and you address what comes, as we have said many times before;
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	and if there are pieces of bone that cling, it is advisable to extract them, if possible.
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	and if one cannot extract it, then it is advisable to break the joint and draw it out forcefully.
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	and the treatment is as we have said, as long as it is healthy.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	And never should the ankle be broken in this way with staples, as is done in the case of the leg or arm.
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	However, this restoration, so done, does not benefit the patients.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the foot is restored in 7 days, or less or more, depending on the diversity of complexes.
de la ruelle dou genoil	from the alley of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	You know that in the alley of the knee there is little breakage, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, even if it is only a crack or an opening, it affects every wound, and without a wound, and this feels good for everyone.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	And the restoration is when everything is placed evenly that it can be moved again with strength.
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	then apply the plaster, and place a round stick, if necessary, and hold it as appropriate, then follow all the arrangements that we have mentioned in other fractures, such as hot abscesses or similar.
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	if, for each of these accidents, it is necessary, as long as it is healthy.
de la brisure de la jambe	from the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	You know that the leg has two bones, of which one is called "right" and not "mustelz", and the other is called "foscile".
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And it continues to break as it comes to the arm, and for this reason, restoration is similar to that of an equal arm, and all work is involved. And if both bones are broken together, then the leg returns from every side.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the thin bones are broken, they return to their original position.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	And if the large bone is broken, it causes great pain, and one can see it clearly.
et torne desoz.	and it turns inside out.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	Then apply extension, and set it equal, and bind the stars equally.
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	but nevertheless, it is necessary that the fracture be ugly, and there are many pieces, so that the extension is smaller and lighter.
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	and lighter according to your ability.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;	And when you have completed your task, take two strips of strong cloth that are suitable for binding the leg on both sides and are sufficiently long to cover the leg from the knee to the sole.
puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	then wrap around both legs from above and below, and tie them together in the middle, so that the leg cannot bend to the right or left, and thus it is good.
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	and no one should administer any medicine to the long bones of the leg, especially if it is broken, and the leg is placed to prevent movement, and it is properly done at the fracture where there is an injury.
et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;	and each day move the leg to see if there is an abscess or any other complication;
si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	if the treatment continues until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	From the fracture of bones in the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no fracture, but the bones in the foot can be fractured and the toes, and they do not always break in a single place, but in various positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	And if there is a severe fracture of the foot bones, and you see these bones stacked on top of each other, causing the patient to lie with their foot flat on the ground as if they wanted to walk, then place your foot on theirs, holding where the bones are raised, and press until they return to their proper position.
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	Then apply the plaster and stop it up, and place under the belly with a small board across both shoulders, then tighten at the foot's end, after you have wrapped it with drape and other things that you need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And after three days or four have passed, if you loosen the bandage, for you will find the bones either even, either broken, or discolored.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	And if neither of the bones is broken, if it is restored, as we have said about the bones of the hand;
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	then place on the broken bone a splint according to the length of the bone, and make it slightly wider, then under the foot place the board I mentioned, and tighten at the end.
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	and if there are two or three (or more), break them, then place on each finger a piece of salt according to its quantity, wrapped in a cloth of linen, and tighten the table under the foot.
et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	and make sure it is firmly on the top of the table, against the stomach of the foot.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit;	And it is important that you do not forget the other things I have said about other breaks, once we have discussed them.
et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	and secure each case as it requires.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	On the fracture of the bone in the hand.
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	When the bone of a woman's natural structure is broken, if it causes swelling, then incline her to the side with the affected part towards the back and hold her there.
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	then fill the wound with cotton, and also put in as much as necessary.
puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;	then stand up the woman, gently pressing her back bit by bit, and pull out the cotton until it reaches the opening of the bone, allowing the bone to return to its place with the cushion.
et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and after she has urinated, put it back, and do this for seven days or so.
si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;	if it is possible to repair the fracture, and if you see, take a bladder of a goat, and tie a cane to the wound, and pour all the bladder into its natural state;
puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:	then blow into the cane until the bladder is fully inflated inside:
la nature si revenra li brisure;	its natural state will repair the fracture;
puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then fill it with cotton and leave it thus for several days until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche;	And when a bone of a man or woman is broken, restore it as we have said for the hip bone;
et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	and these fractures are not hidden from him who applies his study and skill, and heeds this book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration:	For this fracture indicates various dispositions for the right way of restoration:
enten le donques.	understand deeply.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge;	On a broken arrow, take a goose throat and insert it into the arrow;
puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	then wrap rags around it and leave it for three days or until it heals completely.
de brisure avec plaie	from fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	For one who has a fracture with a wound, especially if it is large, such as the bones of the leg or shoulder or similar, it is important to seek immediate care, so that the healing which we have mentioned serves as testimony.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, but there is lingering vitriol, and you have no other remedy, then begin to restore the fracture in the same hour or day, before abscesses form.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if the abscess appears again, it is best to let it heal for a new day or two, until the abscess is calmed, and do not touch it even on the third or fourth day, as you might cause a worse complication.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible upon uncovering the heart, it is necessary that you place it gently with your hands, at a slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;	If the extension does not appear to be of equal length in both hands, reset this instrument which is made of iron, with seven or eight inches in length, and the width should be according to the size of the wound.
et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;	and because it is a delicate operation, it should be soaked for three or four days, depending on the need for each fracture treatment.
