et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	and it should be neither too thin nor too thick, so that it does not bend to pressure on the limb at your command, and is firm in front and thick in the middle towards the front, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent;	and it is called "palainche," therefore the crooked bones should be placed on top of the visible bone's head;
et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	and twist it once, as it returns, and let them be even on each side.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle and the instrument cannot properly grasp the bone, it is necessary that you hold the head of the bone, until the instrument has a good grip.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;	and if you cannot bring the bone back as we have said, then use a suitable tool, such as a knife or scissors, within your power;
puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	then remove whoever is delayed in the bone due to stiffness and small cuts.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is brought back, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, knowing that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit;	if you do as much as possible to have it in its place, then wet the cloth with a black, astringent wine, and wrap it carefully around it;
et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption;	and do not place any ointment or other substance on the wound that would cause putrefaction and decay;
puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;	then administer bandages after you have reset the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, removing any debris, according to the size of the wound, and be sure not to stretch the wound with the bandage.
et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;	and often they have done this foolishly, and brought upon the patient either death or corruption many times.
et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	and so the tightness and pain from other fractures should be more gentle and softer.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles;	And if the wound is deep or great, and you doubt that a bad accident might come, as we have said, and you feel pain instead of relief, if it's not appropriate to put pressure on it.
mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	but wrap it around, instead of pressure, with hard cloth, and bind it.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that the wound is bowing or sinking, then remove what you have put on it and apply a healing dressing for wounds, such as a four-part ointment or similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you loosen the limb twice a day, in the morning and evening, as long as it is healed and cured.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be dislocated in such a way that the bowstring corrals the bone slightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if it persists for a long time and cannot heal completely, knowing that there are small fragments of bone, then you must open the wound with a knife and remove all these misplaced pieces to stop the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula or other form of corruption occurs, it is necessary that you treat it according to what is said in this chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse;	And when a bone is broken and exposed in the member, such as the bone of the shin or the shoulder, or other large limbs, do not pull it immediately, for many times death results, but leave it until it decays.
par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues;	if, by chance, it heals after twenty or thirty days, then treat the wound if possible.
et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	and if you cannot, leave it be.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	burns that come from the heat
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre;	Many times we encounter after the healing of the break, especially when it is near a joint, and the sight of the misaligned limb is an unpleasant one.
et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	and by chance cannot perform the natural movements of its limbs.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres:	Beware then, if it is fresh in us:
si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;	if you administer astringent medicines such as aloe, incense, myrrh, sarcocolla, bayberry, and similar others, by immersing any of these things, or all together, in astringent wine or abundant egg yolk or honey.
et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;	and place them on the wound in compresses, drawing it tight, and do not loosen them for several days.
et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee;	and then dislocate it, and begin again with another, until the nodosities are removed;
ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite;	or hold it tight on a well-made plug;
car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres;	for the property of this plug is such that it removes all swellings from the limbs;
et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent;	and if the nodosity has become hardened like stone, it must be removed, cutting off the top and draining the excess.
ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	You must remove it with any razor while it is fresh (or raw), and treat it as long as it is clean.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	The weak member after treatment.
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:	When the fracture of the bone is healed and the limb remains weak and delicate, this happens for many reasons:
de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;	due to the fact that it was tied too tightly and not properly adjusted as it should have been;
ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre;	or because it had too many constraints, and cannot follow the natural movement of the limb;
ou por multitude d’arosement;	because of the abundance of inflammation;
ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre;	or due to too great movements, not staying in its hour (i.e., not settling properly);
ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	or because it has little blood in its body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui;	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and make the body firm, until the blood increases within it;
et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce;	and administer baths, and give joy and comfort;
puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre;	then place lead on the member, so that the lead attracts great pain, and raise it often with cold water, until the pain subsides in the member.
et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	and it returns to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	Both members twisted after health.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil:	When the member is twisted after restoration and the bones are broken open, and the shape of the member is ugly, yet it does not lose its natural strength.
si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre;	do not believe the fools who say one must break the member from the very beginning, and many foolish things have been done in our land.
et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors;	and this work is blamed, causing great harm, and perhaps even death.
toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses;	However, if the nodulations and tortures are fresh, then they should be treated with hot water or cooked herbs that soften them, such as fennel leaves, roots, melilot, and similar things.
et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus;	and prepare a mollifying plaster, as is well-known, using fennel seeds, and preserve them in gelin grease or sesame oil, and apply the plaster.
ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	You take greasy figures (fat deposits), and crush them with fine collic (a tool or process) and similar medications that reduce inflammation.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is the bone dislocated by rubbing continuously and for a long time with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And allow the limb to move every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement;	And if the swelling and hardness (edema and fibrosis) is like stone, and requires opening with iron, it is necessary to cut gently with a fine instrument up to the bone.
et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	and apply compression and study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book on dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocations occur from a joint moving out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs due to no apparent cause, it is necessary to try to bring the limb back towards its normal position urgently.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu;	For if treatment is delayed, the limbs swell, and perhaps they return to their original position, but it tightens at the joint.
por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez:	Because it is not necessary to move it, as long as it is inflamed.
maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	often causes inflammation and other pains;
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez;	nevertheless, when this occurs, if it makes the patient healthier, then let it be, until the abscess is completely healed.
puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	then raise the affected limb with hot water and oil, then gently reset it, and treat each limb as the cure comes to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations of the shoulder joint up to the foot.
des mandibules	and of the jaws.
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres:	Soon, it happens that the jaws are dislocated, and the dislocation of both is according to two manners:
ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc;	or they are slightly out of their place, and softened slightly;
ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	or they are completely dislocated, hanging down towards the worst, and cutting the saliva from the mouth that he cannot hold it, nor can he close his mouth, and he wraps his tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns to its proper position through various dispositions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is whole and complete, then it is necessary that you reset it hastily, and do not delay.
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars;	and in such a way that the physician places his finger on the patient's head, and presses it deeply into the root of the dislocation of the lower jaw within the mouth, thus dislocating it by half.
et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal;	and the other two hands should be prepared, equal to each other;
et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	and instructs the patient to soften his jaws and move them from all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And balance them equally until they return to their proper place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement;	And if they return to their place, especially when both lower jaws are together, then apply hot water and oil, gently dislocating them again.
ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	We must not delay any longer, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are brought back evenly, and the patient's mouth is closed well without softening, place moistened lint wrapped in a cloth made of rose oil and wax, then gently bind it with soft bands.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and make the patient sleep on their back, with their legs between two pillows, so that they do not move to either side, and do not strive to move more, but gently press the flesh until the pain is gone and the jaws are relaxed.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then massage it gently, and do not strain to open the mouth for eating or drinking, until the jaw is well closed and healthy.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be brought back to their original position within an hour and do not return to their normal place, this causes fever and frequent sweating, and perhaps intestinal problems, and sometimes pure colic vomiting.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions;	And when you see this, then know that it is a sign of harm;
et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	and often causes the death of him who has it, within nine days.
de la forcelle	of the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The fork cannot be removed from the inside of the continuation of the bone, and the more it is pulled, the worse it feels. It is never right when taken out towards the outside, and one can feel this clearly.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras;	And the recovery is that the patient lies on his back, and extends his arms;
et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra;	and then press the joint firmly in your palm, and it will return.
puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	then apply the splint and bandage it tightly.
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer;	and the joint that is towards the neck cannot be dislocated.
se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit;	if it does not dislocate, and if it does not return to its place, as we have said, then you must reset it.
puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	then apply the splint and bandage it tightly, and instruct the patient to rest until they are healed.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	and thus, itself is brought back to the shoulder joint when it deviates from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	**Shoulder Dislocation**
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres:	Know that the shoulder is misaligned through three manners:
de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz;	one of which is that it deviates at the part of the shoulder blade towards the back;
et li seconde est a la partie dou pis;	and the second is at the part where it joins the arm;
et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	and occasionally it deviates at the upper part, and this is rare;
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners;	and do not dislocate it behind for the shoulder, and do not dislocate it inside for the nerves;
et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment;	and repeatedly dislocate towards the armpit, especially those with little flesh, for at these joints it pulls sharply.
a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	at these joints with enough flesh, it pulls sharply, and returns slowly.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes it happens to no one that there is a bruise or fracture, and a hot abscess forms in the shoulder, and he thinks it is dislocated because of that.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains;	You must therefore test it, as long as you are certain.
et adonques encomence la cure.	and then begin treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And dislocation is recognized when it deviates towards the joint, and makes a distinction between the injured shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find their differences manifest.
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes;	and you will find at the top of the shoulder a socket, and by pressing on the joint, you will feel the top of the shoulder as if it were one.
et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and the patient cannot bring their hand back to its normal position, nor move it in any way.
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	and also, if it is dislocated at the top and not properly hidden, for you can feel it clearly with your touch.
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	and this method of dislocation is not to be used unless it is fresh, or if the patient is suffering from great pain.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu;	The method is that the healer places his hand on top of the patient's dislocated joint, then puts his palms beneath the joint, and pulls the joint upwards towards its proper place.
et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz;	and the healer lifts his hand, extending it upwards, then places it beneath.
si venra hastanment.	if sickness comes.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude;	And if sickness does not come as we have said, it is necessary that the patient be bathed in hot water.
et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	and apply it gently and soothingly, such as with a decoction of althae, fennel, and melilot in water, and let it be applied.
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	then the patient should be placed on his back, and a soft cloth of equal thickness should be put under him, neither too soft nor too hard. Then the foot of the sore leg should be placed on the cloth, and gently lift the head of the affected shoulder, and draw the hand of the sick person.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval;	and other assistants tie the patient's head so that it does not move below.
celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	the shoulder now returns, and if it is dislocated, reset it according to this manner:
et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides;	and make sure that this is done at home, which should be larger than the patient.
et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and be straight towards the side of the cost, and turn the patient's shoulder away from the dislocation, and lift the joint above, so that the patient hangs on the other side.
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	and other ministers take hold of the patient's hand below the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, and any heavy thing causes no pain, then the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere:	And it is also adjusted in another way:
et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	and it is fixed with a long stick in the ground, so that the joint is also firm like a pistle, and not too thick or too thin.
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust;	then it is placed beneath the patient, but with soft cloth above, and the patient should be stretched out long on the bed.
puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	then his hand should be stretched out on the other side, forming a new shape, and the joint will return to its original place safely.
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure:	and if she does not want to return due to all the things we have said, then do this treatment:
pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	take a knife of great size and three fingers in width, which has its blade rounded off so that it can enter completely beneath the skin along this shape.
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide;	then lay on the patient's head two cloth strips below, so that they do not hurt the sick person, and insert them beneath the skin of the affected area.
et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part:	and extends one arm over the thigh lengthwise, and binds the shoulder to the thigh, and raises the arm from the elbow of the hand, then places the arm on the broad edge of a chisel, and lowers the hand downward, and lets the body hang from the other side.
li jointure reva ens maintenant.	the joint moves back now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is dislocated, in any way, it is necessary that you put beneath the joint a thread of equal wool, then apply the plaster with the apparatus, consisting of fine powder, incense, and egg yolk, over the entire shoulder and around, then pull the joint gently, and tie the bandage to the plaster, and press the hand against the collarbone, and let the hands remain in this position.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost;	And it is necessary that he moves slightly, as long as the limb is comfortable, because it will heal more quickly.
et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve;	and then move more after two or three days, and continue to move it.
et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	and if it is closed and not softened, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is stuck due to moisture or another cause, it is necessary that you administer cauterization at three points, as is described in the chapter on cauterization.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis;	And if you do all this, and after seven days the joint still does not hold, and the patient cannot raise their arm above their head, then know that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is either compressed, extended, or softened.
et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure;	The dislocation that is towards the worst, and the joints, either in front or behind, are caused by a sudden movement, extension of the arms, and other similar actions; then another treatment is required.
et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and heal as long as he is healthy.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And after healing, cracks may appear in the member, and delayed movement; if the patient uses it many times, as long as these cracks are light, they will be eased and return to their original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	regarding the dislocation cost
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient;	You know that the joint that is dislocated is damaged and moves in an incorrect way;
et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien;	and is damaged from all sides, especially in front and behind, and the dislocation is not completely healed, because it is clearly visible and feels obvious.
et desalue selonc chescune figure.	and is damaged according to each shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the diseased part with the healthy one, if you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	Because the joint is stiff, preventing the arm from bending and touching the shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener;	And it is necessary that you reset it in such a way that the abscess closes and does not reappear, because if the abscess reappears, it would be painful to reset it.
et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier;	and by chance it cannot be reduced to its original state, especially when it is at the back.
si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	it is worse than other dislocations, causing greater pain, and there is a chance it could be fatal.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains;	And the reduction, when it is possible to return it to its original state, you should place your two hands on it.
et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	and the arms should be spread out, and the hands turned towards the sides according to the direction of the joint, pulling them together at the elbows or the base of the palm, until it returns to its original position.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his palm, and turning the root of the palm, which is out of place, according to the joint.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension;	And if it does not want to return to its place, then administer a strong extension;
et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension;	and this is the method to extend the arm: the healer should hold it tightly so that it does not move during the extension.
puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	then turn the arm in each direction, having wrapped it with a long and wide cloth.
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	and when you see the joint connecting to the hand, if it is not lubricated with oil to soften the joint, then press on the formed joint until it returns to its original state.
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	and when it is in place, apply dry plaster with heat, and stretch the arm towards the collarbone of the afflicted person, and do not leave it for any days, then release it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse;	and if the joint is firmly in place, release the tension, and leave it.
et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis;	and if you see that the joint is not tightly held, reapply the plaster and the bandage, and leave it thus for no days until it is firmly set.
puis le deslie.	then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez;	And if it feels painful after resetting the joint, and it becomes silent, then bathe and gently rub it, and press until it is soothed.
ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	Place a grease-soaked sheep's fat on the joint, then leave it for a day and a night, then remove it, and make the patient take a bath.
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain;	And when it sweats, rub the joint gently, then put on the fat again, and then take a bath.
et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And do this process twice or three times until it is healed.
et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus;	and if you see, place it on a hot stone with butter and stretch it.
si revenra a sa disposition.	it will return to its position.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures.	The joint of the hand is misaligned, and its return to position is slight, more so than other joints.
Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	However, it is necessary to bring it back to its place gently, at the same time that it is misaligned, so that the limb does not swell or an abscess forms hot.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the reset is such that you place the patient's hand on a table, extend their limbs, and ensure they are equal, so that they place their palm over the joint's appearance, and bend it until it returns.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu;	Nevertheless, it is important that you check if it is correctly positioned.
adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	then place the patient's hand, palm down, on a table and extend it, then bend it back.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, let the patient place the back of his hand on a table, and look to see the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	If it returns now, that is good.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If, however, the strain of soothing plasters on abscesses is not eased, it will leave him thus without relief.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back in place for any number of days, then the joint will remain dislocated.
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout:	and do not harm the patient further, as long as his hand is swollen, and he cannot move any part of it.
adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere;	so then know that the nerves or arteries are cut.
si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	If there is no other cure than to extract the condition by gentle cautery, then perhaps there is nothing else worth trying.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is dislocated, if you place the splint as we have said, then stretch it and leave it for a day, then release it and do so again.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he cannot move it well, and there is no fracture, then apply hot water moistened cloth, and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	on the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	Never should the palm's two sides be disrespected, neither the back of the hand nor the palm's belly.
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	then they are dislocated, and the dislocation should be held at the patient's own pace until it returns, then support the head with both hands, and pull it towards the part where it is joined.
et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor;	and leave it for two days, then set it equal to the other side that day.
et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut;	and hold it still as we have said, and loosen it from its socket, and make it move, and reset it in the nut.
et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do this often, while it is still tight, and also do the following if it becomes distorted in the palm of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healed.
et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	and do the same when it is distorted from another side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	dislocation of the spine
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine or the neck is dislocated, and there is no cure, the patient often dies quickly.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I.	And the signs of this are that the patient's legs jump involuntarily and he cannot hold them, and often the limbs become weak, both the two knees or the two arms or one.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars;	And often times the shoulder becomes silent from the third part.
celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	The one that becomes silent at the back is called "gypsiness
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance:	The cure is that you warm the place if the gypsiness has come from childhood:
si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	If there is no cure nor healing from it at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And that which comes from falling or impacts or similar things, they speak of ancient cure methods with great words, but they do not bring any true benefit.
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	but I have abbreviated it according to my understanding, and have fashioned instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the weakness that comes to the feet first, no one has ever been healthy.
et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	and also those that come directly to the second side, and one cannot cure outside unless the one properly coming to the back is treated first, as I say.
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	and it is that the patient should be extended on their side with both legs equal, and have pressure from below so they do not move.
puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	then insert I push the splint into the flesh on the head in a curved shape, and another as pressure, and tie a loose band around the afflicted parts, and another across the hips, and knees, and ankles.
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons;	and both ministers know the bands, one on the head and others on the feet, among the two splints;
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	and they should be well secured, the splint as we have said, and the skilled person places their palms on the curved spine until it returns to its place.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it does not return with this treatment, take a table three feet long, cut through the wall from the inside, place the patient on their side, and turn the head of the table away from the wall, then place the middle of the table over the spine.
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu;	and place the mirror on the other side of the table's head and press firmly until it returns to its place.
et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	and if you see, do it with the turn of the hand that returns to its original position.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And you should insert two splints into the head of the patient with a severe arm injury, and towards the feet, two others, and between each splint, from inside and outside, a palm-width of length.
et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent;	and each splint should have an opening, or you turn them correctly, and the splints are firmly fixed in place so they do not move.
et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	and between each pair of splints, there should be a turning splint, so they can twist, and at each twist, two small splints one palm-width long, to turn the twisted one.
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	and then take the ligament that is among the attachments at the twist towards the head, and the other ligament towards the feet at the other twist, and each of the attendants twists their twist to the whole ligament, and the master makes the spike equal as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is equal, apply a drying plaster with much heat, then the stoppers, and then the steel of a tablet three fingers long, which preserves the joint from the stiffness and the healthy part of the spine, then bind it with a ligament as we have said, and use the patient's gentle rest until it is healed.
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant;	and if any thing comes to an end of health, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medications, with the intention that we have said before.
et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations;	and never should a piece of bone be administered, and never should the appearance come in the rear spine of the back, and it is thought that this is dislocation.
et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption:	and it is the bone that opens, therefore one must not have any presumptions about it.
par aventure feroit venir la mort.	for fear it might bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	Of dislocations of the spine
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures;	You know that the joints of the spine and the joints of the shoulder only cause dislocations, not like the other joints.
et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties:	and the spine joint is misaligned according to three parts.
dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier;	inside and outside, and front and back.
et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	and deeper inside, then less misaligned front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of his dislocation is such that when you join the injured leg with the healthy one, it becomes longer, and the patient's knee opens wider than the healthy one, and he cannot bend his knee fully.
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	and it is the inflamed abscess that causes the joint to be destroyed because the bone of the thigh comes close.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him who experiences this at death, it is that this event is contrary to what has been said before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement;	And the signs of someone experiencing this in front, it is that his leg is weak according to its strength.
toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	however, do not bend the knee without pain, and if you want to make him walk, he cannot do so before, and he retains his urine, and the ankle swells, and when he tries to stand, it passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him who experiences this afterward, it is that he cannot spread or bend his knee, and one leg is more twisted than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the pain is in the thigh instead of below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure;	They reset this appearance of dislocation if it is such that you reward it when the dislocation is ancient, and it lingers according to its disposition, otherwise there is no cure.
et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	and there should be no presumption that it will not happen again.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre;	And in the case of a fresh dislocation, which is one of three types, if you hurry to reset the joint, it becomes stuck both inside and outside, and moves to the right or left.
par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	so that it may not recur, and there is no need for other treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not return in this manner, then you must prepare a strong ointment, and stretch the leg strongly with two hands, or bind it tightly to the knee.
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe;	and other assistants extend their hand over it in such a way that they press their hands down on the sore spot, then tightly bind it with a soft ligature on the calf.
et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	and another ties the head with a ligature.
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	and they extend it upwards and downwards several times, until the patient is completely lifted off the ground once, and remains still.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common to all four limbs, and if the dislocation returns, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance.	If this is not the case, then it is necessary to apply a remedy to his appearance.
Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	When the dislocation is in the shoulder joint, it is necessary to have the patient lie on his healthy side, then place a ligature on the root of the thigh, and the limb that is below the injury, then extend the ligature upwards towards the injury and downwards towards the stronger part.
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment:	then have other assistants place their hands on the patient's arms, embrace the larger limb of the injured thigh, and extend it to a wider opening.
si revenra a son leu maintenant;	if it returns to its place now;
et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	and this method of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot hold it in the manner we have described, then it is necessary to bind both feet of the patient together with a strong, soft ligament on the heels and knees, and let the injured leg be extended two more degrees than the others.
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc;	then it should be suspended from a post, and two arms' length above the ground.
puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	then instruct the assistant to embrace the top of the foot, and have other assistants with the patient who gently embrace the foot, for the joint will now move more easily.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation is external, if the patient lies down, as we have said in the case of a dislocated hip, then gently extract the ligament from the affected leg and also from the opposite side.
puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	then place two sticks, one at the top and another at the bottom, then insert a stick between the patient's thighs, in the middle, in the shape of an arc.
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	and he should surround it with moist cloths, so that the patient does not feel pain, then stretch each limb towards him and arrange them equally in his hand to reset the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, that is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If it does not return, place it on a table and press it as we have said in the previous section, and lay the patient on their healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit;	And when the dislocation is present, it is necessary to stretch the diseased leg forcibly, as I have said above;
et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	and place the mirrors to his pain on the diseased artery, then press with the other hand and stretch it downwards towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches;	And if the dislocation is on the outside, it is not necessary to stretch the patient downwards or lift him up, but rather he should remain as his hip was dislocated downwards, just as we have said gently on both hips.
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	and place it on his face, and stretch the ligament as we have said before, and he must press on the joint on the table;
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz;	and will be at the point when the patient extends his legs, and they will be even.
adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	then fasten the hips, and apply the plaster, and wrap a bandage tightly so that the hip does not move.
et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus;	and rest for three or four days, then untie it, and apply the plaster again.
et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors;	and if you see that they are even, hold them as they were before, and leave it for three days.
puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	then release it, and make it go gently, as long as the limb is comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	From the dislocation of the knee.
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres:	The limb is dislocated in three ways:
c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier;	that is to say, inside and out, and behind;
et ne desalue point devant.	and do not dislocate in front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the sign is that you instruct the patient to bend his leg at the knee, and if it does not return to its place at the knee, know that he is dislocated.
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	and the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit up straight, and extend their leg if they can, and place their face down on your lap, and rest their foot on top of yours.
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment;	then take their knee in your palms, pull it between your fingers, and bend both sides of the knee forming a curve.
et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	and other assistants extend their help until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that it has recovered well its leg slightly bent.
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie;	and apply a poultice, and make the leg recover to the knee, and hold it together firmly for three or four days, then loosen it.
et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and the patient should not exert themselves until the limb is comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not at all straight, apply firm extension as we have said in the treatment of the spine, as long as it is healthy.
de la dislocation dou talon	On the dislocation of the talus bone.
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The talus bone is neither perfectly aligned nor fully dislocated, being both inside and outside its proper position.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the sign of this is that the ankle is swollen, and it turns red at the site where it is dislocated.
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	We reset it if it is slight, and one must gently extend their hands when they are seized only slightly.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it is dislocated to a certain degree, one must ensure the patient lies straight and holds the limb firmly with a helper above the ankle.
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	then take the foot in your right hand, and then with your left hand twice, then extend it upwards, and gently pull the foot upwards.
et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet;	and do this twice as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot.
s’elle revient, c’est bien;	If it returns, that's good.
se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	but if it does not return, the work must be restarted, for it comes back.
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	and if it cannot return in that way, then make the patient lie on their back on the ground, and insert a firm stick between their legs, and wrap cloth around them to prevent the patient from bleeding.
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	then attend to the patient's leg, and have another assistant extend the foot or hold it at the ankle, so that he lies down on his back with his foot elevated.
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	then stretch each limb evenly, and insert something between the legs of the patient to hold them still when they are pulled.
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	then apply heat evenly to the dislocation in both hands, and use other assistants to raise the healthy leg, and the dislocation will return steadily.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when the swelling has subsided, apply an ointment and compresses above, tighten the bandage, and tie the foot to the leg, and hold the stirrups behind the ankle, ensuring the bonds are not too tight.
puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain;	then leave it for two or three days, and gently move it if it is strained.
puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors;	then disengage it on the third or fourth day, and for three days thereafter, the patient must be kept from strenuous activity.
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	and if it goes beyond this point, it is not lucky that he does not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses form, it is necessary to soothe them, as we have said elsewhere, while they are fresh.
des dois	Of the two (parts/sides)
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When both (sides) are dislocated, if they need to be rightly extended without effort, it is a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation is in any other part of the leg or foot, it is necessary that you make the patient lie on his back or on a table, keeping his leg straight, and place your foot on what opens these joints, then press with your foot firmly until it returns.
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie;	and when they are even and open nothing, he places the sole of the foot on a table with two joints, then pulls it firmly, and leaves it for three days, then loosens it.
et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and makes it rest until it is healthy.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	From wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When a wound comes with dislocation and one wishes to restore it, often the patient dies.
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	if you are not presumptuous in treatment, since you are not skilled in the art and have not used it for long, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and slow, do not be bold.
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	and at the beginning of things, apply hot poultices to the abscess, and leave the patient in God's hands, if you have no hope for healing.
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	and if you see hope, then immediately reset the member to its place, so that the abscesses that cause it to move cease.
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	and when the member is in place, apply hot poultices to the abscess, and treat the wound as appropriate, using dried herbs.
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	and if there is a dislocation with broken bones and small fragments, as the bones are disjointed, then follow what we have said in simple diseases.
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	and keep from falling into fear, according to what I have said, for it is your motion according to your Creator, and for the knowledge of your arms and body.
